Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Resident Imam for Traveler After Time and Masbuq as Imam
States two conditions for valid congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that invalidate a congregation in Hanafi fiqh: a traveler following a resident imam in a four-rak'ah make-up prayer, and a masbuq leading others.

Core Idea
A traveler's make-up prayer remains two rak'ahs, so following a resident imam creates opposition; a masbuq is still a follower, so he cannot lead.

This lesson clarifies two specific prohibitions in congregation prayer. When a traveler performs a make-up prayer (qada) for a four-rak'ah prayer after its time, his prayer remains two rak'ahs, so following a resident imam who prays four would cause opposition. Additionally, a person who joined late (masbuq) remains connected to his original imam while completing his prayer, making him unable to become an imam for others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
Start by noting the two conditions stated: a resident imam cannot lead a traveler in a four-rak'ah make-up prayer after the time, and a masbuq cannot be an imam.
2
Understand the Reasoning for the Traveler
For the traveler: his four-rak'ah prayer is normally shortened to two rak'ahs. Within the time, following a resident makes it four, but after time it remains two, causing opposition to the imam.
Opposition (mukhalafah) invalidates the congregation.
3
Understand the Reasoning for the Masbuq
For the masbuq: when he stands to complete his missed rak'ahs, he is still effectively a follower of his original imam, so he cannot act as an imam for others.
The masbuq's prayer is not yet complete in the congregation sense.
4
Memorize the Conditions
These rulings are clear-cut conditions (shurut) for a valid congregation. Commit them to memory: traveler after time cannot follow resident imam; masbuq cannot lead.
These are frequently tested in Hanafi fiqh exams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۸۸) [۶] اور چار رکعت والی قضا نماز میں مقیم مسافر کا امام نہ ہو، اور نہ مسبوق ہو۔
تشریح : مسافر کی چار رکعتوں والی نماز بھی دورکعت ہے لیکن وقت کے اندر مقیم کے پیچھے چار رکعت ہو جاتی ہے، اور وقت گزرنے کے بعد دوہی رکعت برقرار رہتی ہیں ، اب مقیم کے پیچھے پڑھے تب بھی دورکعت ہی رہے گی ، جس کی وجہ سے امام کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی اس لئے چار رکعت والی نماز میں مسافر آدمی مقیم امام کی اقتداء وقت گزرنے کے بعد نہیں کرسکتا۔ اور مسبوق امام اس لئے نہیں بن سکتا کہ جب وہ اپنی نماز پوری کر رہا ہے تو اس وقت بھی ایک گونہ اپنے امام کے پیچھے ہے اور یہ مقتدی ہے اس لئے اس کے پیچھے بھی کسی کی نماز درست نہیں۔
Translation: (388) [6] And in a four-rak'ah make-up prayer, a resident should not be the imam for a traveler, and nor should a masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer) be imam.
Explanation: The traveler's four-rak'ah prayer is actually two rak'ahs, but within the time, when he prays behind a resident, it becomes four rak'ahs. However, after the time has passed, only two rak'ahs remain. If he prays behind a resident, it will still be two rak'ahs, which necessitates opposition to the imam. Therefore, in a four-rak'ah prayer, a traveler cannot follow a resident imam after the time has passed. And a masbuq cannot be imam because when he completes his prayer, at that time he is still in a sense behind his own imam and he is a follower, so it is not valid for anyone to pray behind him.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings: (1) A resident imam cannot lead a traveler in a four-rak'ah prayer (Qada) after the time. The reason: the traveler normally prays two rak'ahs, but within the time, when following a resident, he completes four rak'ahs. After the time, his prayer remains two rak'ahs, so if he follows a resident who prays four, he would only pray two, causing opposition (mukhalafah) to the imam. (2) A masbuq (one who joined late) cannot be an imam because he is still effectively following his own imam while completing his prayer. The teacher should explain that these are specific conditions to avoid conflict in the congregation. The rulings are practical issues in Hanafi fiqh, often encountered when traveling or in late joining.

Key Terms
المسافر (al-musāfir): Traveler; one who is on a journey and prays shortened prayers (qasr).
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who missed part of the congregation prayer and joins late; he completes the missed rak'ahs after the imam finishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't a masbuq (one who joined late) lead a new congregation after the original imam finishes?
A) Because his prayer is invalid.
B) Because he is still considered a follower of his original imam.
C) Because he has not completed wudu.
D) Because he is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
A traveler cannot follow a resident imam in a four-rak'ah make-up prayer after the time, and a masbuq cannot act as imam while completing his prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Imam must not be inferior to follower
Rule with proofs on Imam not inferior

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that the Imam must not be inferior to the follower and explain the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
The Imam must be equal or superior to the follower; otherwise, the prayer invalid because the Imam is a guarantor.

In congregational prayer, the Imam leads and the followers follow. But what if the Imam is less capable than those behind him? The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear condition: the Imam must not be inferior to his followers. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proofs from the hadith on the Imam as guarantor (damin) and the instruction not to differ from the Imam, and the practical consequences of violating this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leading a congregation where the Imam is in a lower state than the follower. The ruling: such a congregation is invalid (ghayr saheeh).
The text gives examples: illiterate Imam with literate follower; Imam lying down with follower standing.
2
Locate the dalil
Three proofs are cited: (1) Hadith 'The Imam is a guarantor' (al-Imam damin). (2) Hadith 'Do not differ from him' (la takhtalifu alayh). (3) Athar from Ibrahim: 'If the Imam's prayer becomes invalid, the followers' prayer becomes invalid.'
The first two are from Tirmidhi/Ibn Majah and Muslim respectively.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Each proof shows why the Imam must be capable: (1) A guarantor must be strong; (2) Inferiority causes difference (ikhtilaf) which is prohibited; (3) The Imam's state directly affects the follower's prayer validity.
The word 'damin' implies responsibility, so the Imam must be competent.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow a less learned Imam if he is qualified, but the Hanafi school is strict because of the hadith on the Imam as guarantor.
This is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative) position is that the Imam must be equal or superior; otherwise, the congregation is invalid. This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۸۶) وان لا يكون ادنى حالا من الماموم (۴۸) وان لا يكون الامام مصليا فرضا غیر فرضه (۴۸۸) وان لا يكون الامام مقيما لمسافر بعد الوقت في رباعية ولا مسبوق تشریح : شریعت میں امام کی شان بلند ہے اس لئے وہ مقتدی سے اعلی درجے کا ہو یا برابر ہو، بہت کم درجے کا نہ ہو، مثلا امام امی ہے اور مقتدی قاری ہو، یا امام لیٹ کر نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور مقتدی کھڑا ہو کر نماز پڑھ رہا ہو، یا امام معذور ہو اور مقتدی معذور نہ ہو تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام ضامن ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله ع الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن والمؤذن موتمن، ص ۵۸ نمبر ۷ ۲۰ را ابن ماجہ ، باب ما یجب علی الامام جص ۱۳۸، نمبر (۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام ضامن ہے۔ اس لئے ضامن کو مضبوط ہونا چاہئے اور اعلی درجہ کا ہونا چاہئے یا کم از کم برابر درجہ کا ہونا چاہئے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث سے بھی اس کا اشارہ ملتا ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله الله قال انما جعل الامام ليوتم به فلانختلفوا عليه - (مسلم شریف، باب اتمام الماموم بالا مام، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۹۳۰/۴۱۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام اقتدا کرنے کے لئے ہے اس لئے اس سے اختلاف نہ کرو۔ اور یہاں اعلی کا ادنی درجہ سے اختلاف ہو جاتا ہے۔ (۳) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ امام ضامن ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال : اذا فسدت صلوة الامام فسدت صلوة من خلفه . ( کتاب الآثار لا مام محمد، باب ما يقطع الصلوۃ ، ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگی تو مقتدی کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کی امام ضامن ہے۔ اصول : امام مقتدی کے برابر ہو یا اس سے اعلی درجے کا ہو، اس سے بہت کم درجے کا نہ ہو۔
(486) And that the Imam not be in a lower state than the follower. (487) And that the Imam not be praying a different obligatory prayer than the follower. (488) And that the Imam not be a resident leading a traveler after the time in a four-rakat prayer, nor a mawsuq. Explanation: In Sharia, the status of the Imam is elevated, so he should be of a higher or at least equal rank to the follower, not of a much lower rank. For example, if the Imam is illiterate and the follower is a reciter, or the Imam is praying lying down while the follower stands, or the Imam has an excuse and the follower does not, then the congregation is not valid. Proof: (1) The hadith states that the Imam is a guarantor. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The Imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is trusted.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) From this hadith, it is understood that the Imam is a guarantor. Therefore, the guarantor must be strong and of a higher rank, or at least equal. (2) Another hadith indicates this: From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The Imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' (Muslim) This hadith states that the Imam is for following, so do not differ from him. Here, a higher rank differs from a lower rank. (3) This athar also shows that the Imam is a guarantor. From Ibrahim: 'When the Imam's prayer becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' (Kitab al-Athar) This athar states that if the Imam's prayer becomes invalid, the follower's prayer also becomes invalid. From this, it is learned that the Imam is a guarantor. Principle: The Imam should be equal to or of a higher rank than the follower; he should not be of a much lower rank.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the chapter on Imamate. It states the condition that the Imam must not be inferior to the follower in religious status or ability. The text gives examples: an illiterate Imam with a literate follower, an Imam praying lying down while the follower stands, or an Imam with a valid excuse while the follower has none—all render the congregation invalid. The proofs are drawn from hadith and athar. The first hadith establishes the Imam as a guarantor (damin), so he must be strong. The second hadith instructs followers not to differ from the Imam; inferiority causes such difference. The athar from Ibrahim confirms that the Imam's prayer affects the follower's. The principle is summarised: the Imam must be equal or superior, not inferior.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; the Imam is responsible for the validity of the congregation's prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): Follower in congregation prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a congregation invalid due to the Imam's status?
A) When the Imam is a minor.
B) When the Imam is illiterate and the follower is literate.
C) When the Imam is a traveler.
D) When the Imam is standing and the follower is sitting.

Key Takeaway
The Imam must be equal or superior to the follower; otherwise, the congregation is invalid, as the Imam is a guarantor (damin) and must not cause differences.

Traveler Leading Resident in Qada and Mawsuq as Imam
Ruling with proof on traveler and mawsuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler following a resident Imam in a qada four-rakat prayer after the time has expired, and on a mawsuq leading the congregation, and explain the proof and underlying principle.

Core Idea
After prayer time expires, a traveler's qada remains two rakats; thus he cannot follow a resident, nor can a mawsuq lead.

This passage addresses two specific scenarios in congregational prayer: the validity of a traveler following a resident Imam in a missed (qada) prayer, and the permissibility of a latecomer (mawsuq) leading the congregation. Both rulings hinge on the principle that the traveler's prayer does not change to four rakats after the time has passed, and the mawsuq is still considered a follower until he completes his own prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states: (1) A resident should not lead a traveler in a four-rakat qada prayer after the time. (2) A mawsuq (one who missed some rakats) should not lead at all.
Both rulings are prohibitions (nahy) indicating invalidity of the congregation.
2
Understand the reason for each ruling
For the traveler: within the time, following a resident makes his prayer four rakats; after time, it remains two, causing conflict with the imam. For the mawsuq: he is still effectively a follower while completing his own prayer, so he cannot act as imam.
The conflict arises because the traveler's obligation differs from the resident's after time.
3
Examine the proof (athar)
The text cites an athar from Thawri: one who forgets a prayer in residency and remembers while traveling prays four; if forgets while traveling and remembers in residency, prays two. This shows the number of rakats for qada depends on the place of forgetfulness, not the current location.
The athar is used as evidence that a traveler's qada prayer is two rakats regardless of where he prays it.
4
Recognize the principle
The principle is 'After the time, the traveler's prayer rakats do not change.' The 'sabab' (cause) of time is gone, so the concession of shortening to two rakats remains even when following a resident.
This principle resolves the conflict: the traveler cannot complete the obligation of four rakats by following a resident after time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۸۸) [۶] اور چار رکعت والی قضا نماز میں مقیم مسافر کا امام نہ ہو، اور نہ مسبوق ہو۔ تشریح : مسافر کی چار رکعتوں والی نماز بھی دورکعت ہے لیکن وقت کے اندر مقیم کے پیچھے چار رکعت ہو جاتی ہے، اور وقت گزرنے کے بعد دوہی رکعت برقرار رہتی ہیں ، اب مقیم کے پیچھے پڑھے تب بھی دورکعت ہی رہے گی ، جس کی وجہ سے امام کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی اس لئے چار رکعت والی نماز میں مسافر آدمی مقیم امام کی اقتداء وقت گزرنے کے بعد نہیں کرسکتا۔ اور مسبوق امام اس لئے نہیں بن سکتا کہ جب وہ اپنی نماز پوری کر رہا ہے تو اس وقت بھی ایک گونہ اپنے امام کے پیچھے ہے اور یہ مقتدی ہے اس لئے اس کے پیچھے بھی کسی کی نماز درست نہیں وجه : (۱) اثر میں ہے . عن الثورى قال : من نسى صلوة في الحضر فذكر في السفر صلى اربعا ، و ان نسى صلوة في السفر ذكر في الحضر صلى ركعتين - (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من نسی صلاۃ الحضر ، ج ثانی، ص ۳۵۸، نمبر ۴۴۰۰ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسافر وقت کے بعد دو رکعت ہی قضاء کریں گے۔ (۲) سبب یعنی وقت بھی نہیں رہا جو نماز کی رکعتوں کو تبدیل کر سکے۔ اصول: وقت گزرنے کے بعد مسافر کی نماز کی رکعتوں میں تبدیلی نہیں ہوگی۔ لغت : مسبوقا: پہلی رکعت جس کی چھوٹ چکی ہو اس کو مسبوق ، کہتے ہیں۔
Translation: (388) [6] And the resident should not be an Imam for a traveler after the time in a four-rakat prayer, nor should a mawsuq be Imam. Explanation: The traveler's four-rakat prayer is also two rakats, but within the time, following a resident makes it four rakats. After the time, only two rakats remain; if he follows a resident, he will still pray two rakats, causing conflict with the Imam. Therefore, a traveler cannot follow a resident Imam after the time in a four-rakat prayer. A mawsuq cannot be Imam because when he completes his own prayer, he is still in a state of following his own Imam; thus, it is invalid for anyone to follow him. Proof: (1) There is an athar from Thawri: 'Whoever forgets a prayer in residency and remembers it while traveling, prays four; and whoever forgets a prayer while traveling and remembers in residency, prays two.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) This athar indicates that a traveler only prays two rakats for qada. (2) The reason (sabab) i.e., time is no longer present to change the number of rakats. Principle: After the time, the traveler's prayer rakats do not change. Lexicon: Mawsuq: one who has missed the first rakat(s) is called mawsuq.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the traveler's qada prayer behind a resident Imam. The ruling states that after the expiry of the prayer time, a traveler cannot follow a resident Imam in a four-rakat prayer because the traveler's prayer remains two rakats while the resident prays four, causing conflict. Additionally, a mawsuq (one who joined late) cannot lead because he is still effectively following his own Imam. The proof is an athar from Thawri establishing that a traveler's qada prayer is two rakats. The principle is that after the time, the traveler's prayer does not change to four rakats. The text also defines mawsuq.

Key Terms
مسبوق (mawsuq): One who has missed one or more rakats of the congregation and joins later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a traveler follow a resident Imam in a four-rakat prayer?
A) Only if the traveler intends to pray four rakats.
B) Only within the prayer time, not after.
C) Only if the resident is also a traveler.
D) Only during travel, not at home.

Key Takeaway
A traveler cannot follow a resident Imam in a four-rakat qada prayer after the time has expired, and a mawsuq cannot lead the congregation.

Barriers Invalidating Congregational Prayer
Rules about barriers between Imam and congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four barriers that invalidate congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school and apply the exception for walls when the Imam's actions are perceptible.

Core Idea
A physical barrier between Imam and follower that prevents knowledge of actions voids the congregation.

Congregational prayer requires a direct connection between Imam and follower. The Hanafi school specifies four physical barriers that break this connection: a row of women, a navigable river, a busy road, and an obscuring wall. However, if the follower can still see or hear the Imam without doubt, the exception for walls applies. In this lesson, we will examine each barrier and its scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four barriers
From the passage, list the four barriers: women's row, navigable river, busy road, and obscuring wall.
The wall is conditional: if it causes uncertainty, it invalidates.
2
Understand the ruling for each barrier
For each barrier, note that the congregation becomes invalid (fasid). The exception is the wall if the follower can still perceive the Imam's movements without doubt.
The ruling is the same for women's row, river, and road; the wall has a nuance.
3
Trace the evidence for women's row
The Hanafi proof includes a hadith (Anas praying behind Prophet with Umm Sulaym behind), a Companion statement (Ibn Mas'ud: 'put them back'), and a Tabi'i statement (Ibrahim disliked prayer across a woman or road).
These are zanni (probative) proofs but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario with one barrier, determine whether the congregation is valid or invalid, citing the relevant condition.
Consider the exception: wall only invalidates if it causes uncertainty.

Source Text

(۱۴۸۹ وان لا يفصل بين الامام والماموم صف من النساء (۴۹۰ وان لا يفصل نهر تمرّ فيه الزورق وجه : (۱) اثر میں ہے . عن الثورى قال : من نسى صلوة في الحضر فذكر في السفر صلى اربعا ، و ان نسى صلوة في السفر ذكر في الحضر صلى ركعتين - (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من نسی صلاۃ الحضر ، ج ثانی، ص ۳۵۸، نمبر ۴۴۰۰ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسافر وقت کے بعد دو رکعت ہی قضاء کریں گے۔ (۲) سبب یعنی وقت بھی نہیں رہا جو نماز کی رکعتوں کو تبدیل کر سکے۔ اصول: وقت گزرنے کے بعد مسافر کی نماز کی رکعتوں میں تبدیلی نہیں ہوگی۔ لغت : مسبوقا: پہلی رکعت جس کی چھوٹ چکی ہو اس کو مسبوق ، کہتے ہیں۔ ترجمه : (۳۸۹) [۷] اور نہ فاصلہ ہوا امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورتوں کی صف کا۔ تشریح : حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ عورت سے نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورتوں کا صف نہ ہو تب اقتداء درست ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم انه كان يكره ان يصلى بصلاة الامام اذا كان بينهما طريق او اء ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی الرجل والمرأة يصلى و بينه و بین الا مام حائط ، ج ثانی ، ص ۳۵، نمبر ۶۱۵۵ رمصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل يصلى وراء الامام خارج المسجد ، ج ثالث ،ص ۹، نمبر ۴۸۹۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورت یا بڑا راستہ ہو تو اقتدار پیچ نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث کی بنا پر عورت کو پیچھے ہونا چاہئے اس لئے درمیان میں ہونے کی وجہ سے اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال صلیت انا ويتيم في بيتنا خلف النبي الله وامی ام سلیم خلفنا ( بخاری شریف ، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفا ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلث کیف یقومون ، ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں کی صف پیچھے ہونی چاہئے ۔ (۳) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کو پیچھے رکھو۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : كان الرجال و النساء في بني اسرائيل يصلون جميعا ،فكانت المرأة اذا كان لها الخليل تلبس القالبين تطول بهما لخليلها ، فالقى الله عليهن الحيض ، فكان ابن مسعود يقول : أخر وهن حيث أخر من الله - (طبرانی کبير، عبداللہ بن مسعود الهند لی ، باب ، ج تاسع ، ص ۲۹۵، نمبر ۴ ۹۴۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کو پیچھے رکھو۔ ترجمه : (۴۹۰)[۸] اور ایسی نہر کا فاصلہ نہ ہو جس میں چھوٹی کشتی چل سکے۔ [9] اور درمیان میں ایسا راستہ نہ ہو جس میں گاڑی گزرتی ہو ۔ [10] اور درمیان میں ایسی دیوار نہ ہو جس سے امام کے انتقالات کا علم مشتبہ ہو جائے اور اگر آواز سننے یا دیکھنے سے اشتباہ نہ ہوتو صحیح روایت میں اقتد صحیح ہے۔
(489) And let there not be a row of women separating the Imam and the follower. (490) And let there not be a river in which a small boat passes. Proof: (1) There is an athar from Thawri: 'Whoever forgets a prayer in residency and remembers it while traveling, prays four; and whoever forgets a prayer while traveling and remembers in residency, prays two.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) [Note: This athar seems out of place; it was used earlier.] (2) The reason (sabab) i.e., time is no longer present to change the number of rakats. Principle: After the time, the traveler's prayer rakats do not change. Lexicon: Mawsuq: one who has missed the first rakat(s) is called mawsuq. Translation: (389) [7] And let there not be a row of women separating the Imam and the follower. Explanation: The Hanafi school holds that a woman invalidates the prayer, so the congregation is valid only if there is no row of women between Imam and follower. Proof: (1) In this statement of a Tabi'i: From Ibrahim that he disliked praying with the prayer of the Imam when between them was a road or a woman. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) This statement indicates that if between the Imam and follower there is a woman or a big road, the congregation is not valid. (2) Based on the hadith, women should be behind, so if they are in between, the congregation is invalid. The hadith: 'I prayed with an orphan in our house behind the Prophet, and my mother Umm Sulaym was behind us.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that the row of women should be behind. (3) In this statement of a Companion: Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Men and women used to pray together among Bani Isra'il, but when a woman had a lover, she would adorn herself for him, so Allah sent menstruation upon them. Ibn Mas'ud used to say: Put them back where Allah has put them back.' (Tabarani) This statement commands placing women behind. Translation: (490) [8] And let there not be a separation by a river in which a small boat passes. [9] And let there not be between them a road in which a carriage passes. [10] And let there not be between them a wall which obscures knowledge of the Imam's movements; but if there is no confusion by hearing or seeing, then in the correct narration, the congregation is valid.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage covers multiple conditions regarding physical separation between Imam and follower. First, a row of women between them invalidates the congregation; the Hanafi ruling is justified by a Tabi'i statement, a hadith placing women behind, and a Companion's statement. Second, a navigable river (for small boats) is a barrier. Third, a road with traffic is a barrier. Fourth, a wall that causes uncertainty about the Imam's movements invalidates the congregation unless the follower can hear or see without doubt. The proof section mistakenly includes the Thawri athar again, but the main evidence for women's row is from Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bukhari, and Tabarani.

Key Terms
مسبوق (mawsuq): One who has missed one or more rakats of the congregation.
نهر (nahr): A river that can be crossed by a small boat; such a body of water is a barrier to congregation.
طريق (tariq): A road on which carriages pass; a busy road that is a barrier.
حائط (ha'it): A wall; it invalidates only if it obscures knowledge of Imam's actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following invalidates the congregation?
A) A row of children between Imam and follower.
B) A river that a small boat can pass.
C) A wall that the follower can see through.
D) A road that only pedestrians use.

Key Takeaway
A congregation is invalid if a row of women, navigable river, busy road, or an obscuring wall separates Imam and follower; only a wall is excused if the follower can perceive without doubt.

Ruling on a Row of Women Between Imam and Ma'mum
States ruling and provides three proofs from the Salaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a row of women between the imam and ma'mum and identify the three proofs cited from the Salaf and hadith.

Core Idea
A women's row between imam and follower invalidates the follower's prayer — women must be behind the men.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of rows is essential. The Hanafi school holds that a row of women between the imam and the male follower invalidates the follower's prayer. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and statements of the Companions and Followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: a row of women between the imam and male follower makes the follower's prayer invalid (fasid).
The imam's prayer remains valid; only the follower's prayer is affected.
2
Examine the first proof
Analyze the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a Tabi'i) that he disliked praying behind an imam when a road or wall separates them. The Hanafis extend this to women, considering them a similar barrier.
This is an istidlal (deduction) from the practice of a Tabi'i, which carries weight in the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the second proof
Review the hadith of Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet prayed with Anas and an orphan behind him, and Umm Sulaym (Anas's mother) was behind them. This indicates women should be placed behind the men.
The hadith establishes a pattern: women are to be in the back rows, not between imam and men.
4
Examine the third proof
Consider the statement of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Put them (women) behind as Allah has put them behind.' This is a companion saying (qawl sahabi) that reinforces the placement of women behind men.
Companion sayings are considered authoritative in Hanafi usul.
5
Understand the Hanafi reliance
Recognize that the Hanafi school combines these proofs to conclude that a women's row between imam and men disrupts the required connection (ittisal) of the rows, invalidating the follower's prayer.
Other schools may interpret these proofs differently, leading to a difference of opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴۸۹ وان لا يفصل بين الامام والماموم صف من النساء
ترجمه : (۳۸۹) [۷] اور نہ فاصلہ ہوا امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورتوں کی صف کا۔ تشریح : حنفیہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ عورت سے نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورتوں کا صف نہ ہو تب اقتداء درست ہوگی۔
وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم انه كان يكره ان يصلى بصلاة الامام اذا كان بينهما طريق او اء ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی الرجل والمرأة يصلى و بينه و بین الا مام حائط ، ج ثانی ، ص ۳۵، نمبر ۶۱۵۵ رمصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل يصلى وراء الامام خارج المسجد ، ج ثالث ،ص ۹، نمبر ۴۸۹۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان عورت یا بڑا راستہ ہو تو اقتدار پیچ نہیں ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث کی بنا پر عورت کو پیچھے ہونا چاہئے اس لئے درمیان میں ہونے کی وجہ سے اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک قال صلیت انا ويتيم في بيتنا خلف النبي الله وامی ام سلیم خلفنا ( بخاری شریف ، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفا ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۷۲۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا کانوا ثلث کیف یقومون ، ص ۹۷ نمبر ۶۱۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں کی صف پیچھے ہونی چاہئے ۔ (۳) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کو پیچھے رکھو۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : كان الرجال و النساء في بني اسرائيل يصلون جميعا ،فكانت المرأة اذا كان لها الخليل تلبس القالبين تطول بهما لخليلها ، فالقى الله عليهن الحيض ، فكان ابن مسعود يقول : أخر وهن حيث أخر من الله - (طبرانی کبير، عبداللہ بن مسعود الهند لی ، باب ، ج تاسع ، ص ۲۹۵، نمبر ۴ ۹۴۸) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ عورت کو پیچھے رکھو۔
And that there should not separate between the imam and the ma'mum a row of women. Translation: (389) [7] And there should be no separation between the imam and the follower by a row of women. Explanation: The Hanafi school's position is that prayer is invalidated by women, therefore when there is no row of women between the imam and the follower, the following is valid. Evidence: (1) In this statement of a Tabi'i: 'From Ibrahim that he disliked that one should pray with the prayer of the imam when between them is a road or a wall...' (2) Based on this hadith, women should be behind, so due to being in between, following is not valid. The hadith: 'From Anas ibn Malik, he said: I prayed with an orphan in our house behind the Prophet, peace be upon him, and my mother Umm Sulaym was behind us...' (3) In this statement of a Companion: 'Put them behind as Allah has put them behind.'
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of following the imam (iqtida') when there is a row of women between the imam and the male follower. The ruling states that such a row invalidates the prayer of the follower. The commentator explains that according to the Hanafi madhhab, the presence of women can corrupt the prayer, so for the iqtida' to be valid, there must be no row of women separating the imam from the ma'mum. Three proofs are cited: (1) The statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a Tabi'i, that he disliked praying behind an imam when there is a road or a wall between them, which is applied to women as well. (2) The hadith of Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet prayed with Anas and an orphan behind him, and Umm Sulaym was behind them, indicating women should be at the back. (3) The statement of Ibn Mas'ud that women were placed behind men by Allah's decree. All these evidences support the ruling that women should not be between imam and male followers.

Key Terms
صف النساء (saff al-nisa'): A row of women praying behind the imam, but here specifically placed between the imam and male followers.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The follower's prayer is invalid because of the women's row.
C) The follower's prayer is valid if he does not see the women.
D) The follower's prayer is valid if the women are behind the last row.

Key Takeaway
A women's row between imam and follower invalidates the follower's prayer in the Hanafi madhhab, based on multiple proofs from the Salaf and hadith.

Barriers Between Imam and Ma'mum: River, Road, and Wall
Details conditions for valid following regarding physical barriers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three barriers that invalidate following the imam and identify the condition under which following remains valid.

Core Idea
A physical barrier that prevents knowledge of the imam's movements invalidates iqtida'.

In congregational prayer, the follower must be able to track the imam's actions. The Hanafi school specifies that certain barriers—a navigable river, a cart road, or an opaque wall—break the connection unless the follower can still reliably discern movements through sight, sound, or a muballigh. This lesson examines these rulings and their evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Barriers
Read the passage and list the three specific barriers that the Hanafi school considers as potentially invalidating iqtida'.
The barriers are a river, a road, and a wall.
2
Understand the Exception
Note that for the wall, if the follower can see or hear the imam (or receive knowledge through a muballigh), the following is valid. For the river and road, the exception is not mentioned, implying they invalidate even if knowledge is present.
This distinction is crucial.
3
Analyze the Primary Evidence
Examine the hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit (Bukhari) where the Prophet prayed in a chamber and followers outside followed him. Identify how this supports the principle that a barrier does not invalidate if movements are known.
The hadith is cited as proof that knowledge of movements overcomes a barrier.
4
Consider Additional Proofs
Review the other proofs: the practice of Abu Hurayra on the roof, Anas ibn Malik with a small road, Aisha's statement on a screen, and Umar's general rule.
These together establish the Hanafi position.
5
Apply the Ruling
Use the rules from this lesson to determine the validity of iqtida' in new scenarios, especially focusing on the condition of knowledge.
Remember: the river and road are absolute barriers; the wall is conditional.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا ۳۲۶
باب الامامة
ولا طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة ولا حائط يشتبه معه العلم بانتقالات الامام فان لم يشتبه لسماع او رؤية
تشريح : یہ تینوں مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنا فاصلہ ہو کہ دونوں الگ الگ نماز پڑھنے والے نظر آتے ہوں تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی ، اور دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنی حیلولت ہے کہ امام کے منتقل ہونے کا اور رکوع وسجدہ میں جانے کا بھی پتہ نہیں چل رہا ہے کہ اس کی اتباع کی جائے ، نہ اس کی آواز سننے کے ذریعہ ، نہ اس کو دیکھنے کے ذریعہ اور نہ کسی مکبر کی آواز سے اس صورت میں بھی اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ ۔ تشریح مسئلہ ۔ یہاں تین مسلئے ہیں، ہر ایک کی تشریح یہ ہے [۸] امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان چھوٹی نالی ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے لیکن اتنا بڑا نہر ہو کہ اس میں کشتی جاسکتی ہو تو امام اور مقتدی اجنبی نظر آنے لگے اس لئے اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ [9] یا امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنا بڑا راستہ ہواس میں گاڑی چل سکے، اور اس راستے پر نمازی کی کوئی صف نہ ہو تو افتد اء درست نہیں ہے [9] امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان ایسی دیوار حائل ہو کہ آواز یاد یکھنے یا مکبر کی آواز سے امام کے منتقل ہونے اور رکوع سجدے میں جانے کا علم نہ ہوتا ہوتو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ امام کی اتباع ضروری ہے اور یہاں رکوع وسجدے میں امام کی اتباع نہیں ہو سکے گی اس لئے اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر امام کی آواز سننے، یا دیکھنے ، یا مکبر کے ذریعہ امام کی حرکتوں کا علم ہوتا ہو اور بہت فاصلہ بھی نہ ہوتو اقتداء جائز ہے۔

وجه :(۱) عن زيد بن ثابت ان النبي علي اتخذ حجرة في المسجد من حصير فصلی رسول الله الله فيها ليالي حتى اجتمع اليه اناس ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما يكره من كثرة السوال و من تكلف مالا یعنیه، ص ۱۲۵۴، نمبر ۷۲۹۰ ) اس حدیث میں حضور مجرے میں تھے اور مقتدی الگ تھے لیکن حضور کے انتقال سے واقف ہوتے رہتے تھے اس لئے اقتداء درست ہوئی ۔ (۲) عن صالح مولى التوامة قال كنت اصلي انا و ابو هريرة فوق ظهر المسجد نصلى بصلاة الامام للمكتوبة - (سنن بیہقی، باب صلوۃ الامام في المسجد وعلی ظهر اونی رحبته ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۵۲۴۴) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ مسجد کی چھت پر اقتداء درست ہے ۔ (۳) رأيت انس بن مالک صلی الجمعة في بيوت حميد بن عبد الرحمن بن عوف فصلى بصلاة الامام في المسجد و بين بيوت حميد و المسجد الطريق ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب المأموم يصلى خارج المسجد بصلاة الامام في المسجد ولیس بینھما حائل، ج ثالث ،ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۵۲۴۷) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ چھوٹا راستہ ہو تو صلى الله عليه وسلم اقتداء جائز ہے۔(۴) قال الشافعي قد صلى نسوة مع عائشة زوج النبي لا في حجرتها فقالت لا تصلين بصلاة الامام فانكن دونه حجاب . (سنن بیہقی ، باب المأموم يصلى خارج المسجد بصلاة الامام في المسجد وليس بينهما حائل ، ج ثالث ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۵۲۴۶) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ حجاب ہو تو افتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ (۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بڑا راستہ ہو تو اقتداء درست نہیں . قال عمر اذا كان بينه و بين الامام طريق او نهر او حائط فليس معه - ( مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب في الرجل والمرأة يصلى و بينه و بين الامام حالک ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۶۱۵۴ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصلى وراء .
Translation: (490) [8] And there should not be a river in which a small boat can sail. [9] And there should not be in between a road in which a cart passes. [10] And there should not be in between a wall that obscures knowledge of the imam's movements. And if there is no obscurity due to hearing or seeing, then in the correct narration, following is valid. ...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage elaborates on three specific barriers between the imam and ma'mum that invalidate following: (1) a river wide enough for a small boat, (2) a road where a cart can pass, and (3) a wall that prevents knowledge of the imam's movements. The general principle is that if the distance or obstruction makes it appear that the imam and follower are praying separately, or if the follower cannot discern the imam's movements (by sight, sound, or through a muballigh), then the following is invalid. However, if the follower can see or hear the imam, or receive knowledge through a muballigh, the following is valid. Five proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit where the Prophet prayed in a small room and followers outside followed based on knowing his movements. (2) The practice of Abu Hurayra praying on the roof of the mosque following the imam inside. (3) Anas ibn Malik praying Friday prayer in houses outside the mosque while following the imam inside with only a small road in between. (4) The statement of Umm al-Mu'mineen Aisha that women behind a screen should not follow the imam's prayer. (5) The statement of Umar that if there is a road, river, or wall between, then it is not considered following.

Key Terms
حائل (ha'il): Any physical barrier that separates the imam from the follower and obscures knowledge of movements.
انتقالات الامام (intiqalat al-imam): The movements of the imam during prayer (e.g., bowing, prostrating) that the follower must be aware of to follow correctly.
مقبر (muballigh): A person who relays the imam's takbir and movements to the followers, often used when there is a barrier or distance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following barriers invalidates following the imam in Hanafi fiqh?
A) A small stream that can be stepped over.
B) A river in which a small boat can sail.
C) A wall that has a window through which the imam can be seen.
D) A road that is not used by carts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a physical barrier invalidates iqtida' only if it prevents knowledge of the imam's movements, except for a wide river or road which invalidate regardless.

Distance and Barriers Between Imam and Ma'mum
Explains rules of distance and barriers between imam and ma'mum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid following in congregational prayer regarding distance and barriers, and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
The ma'mum must know the imam's movements; otherwise the prayer is invalid.

Congregational prayer requires precise following of the imam. The Hanafi school has detailed rules about the allowed distance and barriers between the imam and the ma'mum. This lesson explains the two core principles and their application to three types of obstacles: water, roads, and walls.

Guided Path
1
State the two core principles
1) If the distance makes the imam and ma'mum appear separate, it's invalid. 2) If a barrier prevents knowledge of the imam's movements, it's invalid.
2
Apply the first principle to water bodies
A small stream is fine; a navigable river invalidates because they appear separate.
The criterion is 'appearing separate', not mere distance.
3
Apply the first principle to roads
A small road with no row is fine; a large road where a carriage passes invalidates.
If a row of worshippers spans the road, it becomes part of the congregation.
4
Apply the second principle to walls
A wall that blocks all knowledge (sight, sound, muballigh) invalidates; if knowledge is possible, it's valid.
A glass wall where the ma'mum can see is valid; a solid wall with no sound is invalid unless a muballigh conveys.
5
Connect to the evidence
The Prophet's prayer in a chamber, the roof prayer of Abu Hurayra, and the statements of Aisha and Umar support the principles.
The hadith and athar illustrate that knowledge of movements is the key, not the barrier itself.

Source Text

باب الامامة ولا طريق تمرّ فيه العجلة ولا حائط يشتبه معه العلم بانتقالات الامام فان لم يشتبه لسماع او رؤية تشريح : یہ تینوں مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنا فاصلہ ہو کہ دونوں الگ الگ نماز پڑھنے والے نظر آتے ہوں تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی ، اور دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنی حیلولت ہے کہ امام کے منتقل ہونے کا اور رکوع وسجدہ میں جانے کا بھی پتہ نہیں چل رہا ہے کہ اس کی اتباع کی جائے ، نہ اس کی آواز سننے کے ذریعہ ، نہ اس کو دیکھنے کے ذریعہ اور نہ کسی مکبر کی آواز سے اس صورت میں بھی اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ ۔ تشریح مسئلہ ۔ یہاں تین مسلئے ہیں، ہر ایک کی تشریح یہ ہے [۸] امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان چھوٹی نالی ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے لیکن اتنا بڑا نہر ہو کہ اس میں کشتی جاسکتی ہو تو امام اور مقتدی اجنبی نظر آنے لگے اس لئے اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ [9] یا امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنا بڑا راستہ ہواس میں گاڑی چل سکے، اور اس راستے پر نمازی کی کوئی صف نہ ہو تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے [9] امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان ایسی دیوار حائل ہو کہ آواز یاد یکھنے یا مکبر کی آواز سے امام کے منتقل ہونے اور رکوع سجدے میں جانے کا علم نہ ہوتا ہوتو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ امام کی اتباع ضروری ہے اور یہاں رکوع وسجدے میں امام کی اتباع نہیں ہو سکے گی اس لئے اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر امام کی آواز سننے، یا دیکھنے ، یا مکبر کے ذریعہ امام کی حرکتوں کا علم ہوتا ہو اور بہت فاصلہ بھی نہ ہوتو اقتداء جائز ہے۔ وجه :(۱) عن زيد بن ثابت ان النبي علي اتخذ حجرة في المسجد من حصير فصلی رسول الله فيها ليالي حتى اجتمع اليه اناس ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما يكره من كثرة السوال و من تكلف مالا یعنیه، ص ۱۲۵۴، نمبر ۷۲۹۰ ) اس حدیث میں حضور مجرے میں تھے اور مقتدی الگ تھے لیکن حضور کے انتقال سے واقف ہوتے رہتے تھے اس لئے اقتداء درست ہوئی ۔ (۲) عن صالح مولى التوامة قال كنت اصلي انا و ابو هريرة فوق ظهر المسجد نصلى بصلاة الامام للمكتوبة - (سنن بیہقی، باب صلوۃ الامام في المسجد وعلی ظهر اونی رحبته ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۵۲۴۴) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ مسجد کی چھت پر اقتداء درست ہے ۔ (۳) رأيت انس بن مالک صلی الجمعة في بيوت حميد بن عبد الرحمن بن عوف فصلى بصلاة الامام في المسجد و بين بيوت حميد و المسجد الطريق ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب المأموم يصلى خارج المسجد بصلاة الامام في المسجد ولیس بینھما حائل، ج ثالث ،ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۵۲۴۷) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ چھوٹا راستہ ہو تو اقتداء جائز ہے۔(۴) قال الشافعي قد صلى نسوة مع عائشة زوج النبي لا في حجرتها فقالت لا تصلين بصلاة الامام فانكن دونه حجاب . (سنن بیہقی ، باب المأموم يصلى خارج المسجد بصلاة الامام في المسجد وليس بينهما حائل ، ج ثالث ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۵۲۴۶) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ حجاب ہو تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔ (۵) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ بڑا راستہ ہو تو اقتداء درست نہیں . قال عمر اذا كان بينه و بين الامام طريق او نهر او حائط فليس معه - ( مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب في الرجل والمرأة يصلى و بينه و بين الامام حالک ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۶۱۵۴ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصلى وراء . اصول : [1] امام اور مقتدی کے درمیان اتنا فاصلہ ہو کہ دونوں الگ الگ نماز پڑھنے والے لگتے ہوں تو اقتداء درست نہیں ہے - [۲] یا کسی طرح امام کے انتقالات کا علم نہ ہوتا ہو تب بھی اقتداء درست نہیں ہے۔
And not a road in which a carriage passes, nor a wall that makes the knowledge of the imam's movements doubtful; if it is not doubtful due to hearing or seeing. Explanation: These three issues are based on the principle that if the distance between the imam and the ma'mum is such that they appear to be praying separately, then following is not valid. And the second principle is that if there is an obstruction between the imam and the ma'mum such that the imam's movements, like going into ruku and sujud, cannot be known, whether by hearing his voice, seeing him, or through a muballigh, then following is also not valid. Explanation of the issues: There are three issues. [8] If there is a small stream between the imam and the ma'mum, there is no harm. But if the river is so large that a boat can sail in it, then the imam and the ma'mum appear as strangers, so following is not valid. [9] Or if there is a large road between them in which a carriage can pass, and there is no row of worshippers on that road, then following is not valid. [9] If there is a wall between the imam and the ma'mum such that the imam's movements cannot be known through sound, sight, or the voice of the muballigh, then following is not valid, because following the imam is necessary and here it is not possible to follow him in ruku and sujud. And if the imam's movements can be known through hearing, seeing, or through a muballigh, and the distance is not great, then following is permissible. Evidence: (1) From Zaid bin Thabit that the Prophet (peace be upon him) took a chamber in the mosque made of matting and prayed there for several nights until people gathered around him. (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that the Prophet was in the chamber and the followers were separate, but they were aware of his movements, so following was valid. (2) From Salih, the freed slave of al-Taw'amah: I and Abu Hurairah used to pray on the roof of the mosque, praying with the imam's prayer for the obligatory prayer. (Bayhaqi) This action of a Companion shows that praying on the roof of the mosque is valid. (3) I saw Anas bin Malik pray Jumu'ah in the houses of Humaid bin Abdur Rahman bin Auf, and he prayed with the imam's prayer in the mosque, and between the houses of Humaid and the mosque there was a road. (Bayhaqi) This action of a Companion shows that if there is a small road, following is permissible. (4) Al-Shafi'i said: Some women prayed with Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, in her chamber, and she said: Do not pray with the imam's prayer, because you are behind a screen. (Bayhaqi) This statement shows that if there is a screen, following is not valid. (5) A statement of a Tabi'i: If there is a large road, following is not valid. 'Umar said: If there is between him and the imam a road, river, or wall, then he is not with him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) Principles: [1] If the distance between the imam and the ma'mum is such that they appear to be praying separately, then following is not valid. [2] Or if the imam's movements cannot be known in any way, then also following is not valid.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It explains the Hanafi conditions for valid congregational prayer regarding distance and barriers. The text first states the matn condition: there should not be a road wide enough for a carriage nor a wall that obscures knowledge of the imam's movements. Then it details three cases: a small stream is fine; a navigable river or a road with no rows invalidates; and a wall that prevents knowledge of movements invalidates unless the ma'mum can see, hear, or be informed by a muballigh. The evidence includes hadith and actions of the Companions and Tabi'un. The two core principles are: (1) the imam and ma'mum must appear to be praying together, not separately; (2) the ma'mum must be able to know the imam's movements to follow him.

Key Terms
حائل (ha'il): Anything that obstructs the ma'mum from seeing, hearing, or otherwise knowing the imam's movements in prayer.
انتقالات (intiqalat): The movements of the imam from one posture to another, such as going into ruku, sujud, etc.
مکبر (mukabbir): A person who conveys the imam's takbir to the ma'mum when the ma'mum cannot hear the imam directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If there is a wall between the imam and the ma'mum that completely blocks both sight and sound, and there is no muballigh, is the ma'mum's prayer valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid, because the intention is present.
B) Invalid, because the ma'mum cannot follow the imam's movements.
C) Valid if the wall is less than 3 meters.
D) Invalid only if the wall is made of brick.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following the imam depends on the ma'mum's ability to know the imam's movements, either directly or through a means, and on the distance not making them appear separate.

Conditions for Valid Imamate: Unity of Congregation
Specifies conditions for valid imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid imamate concerning movement difference and identify which scenarios invalidate the ma'mum's prayer.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer requires visible unity — if imam and ma'mum appear to pray separately due to divergent movement, the prayer is invalid.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text outlines essential conditions for the validity of following the imam in prayer. The central concern is that the congregation must appear as a single unit. The text specifies three scenarios where this unity is broken due to differing modes of travel, rendering the prayer invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Scenarios
List the three cases described: (1) imam mounted while ma'mum on foot, (2) imam and ma'mum on separate mounts, (3) imam and ma'mum in separate boats not tied together.
These are the specific prohibitions.
2
Extract the Underlying Principle
Recognize that the common factor is that the imam and ma'mum appear to be praying individually due to differing directions or movements.
The principle is unity of congregation (al-jama'ah).
3
Apply the Principle to Each Scenario
For each scenario, explain how the divergence in movement creates the appearance of separate prayers.
The direction of travel matters: if they diverge, unity is lost.
4
State the Ruling
Conclude that in all three cases, the ma'mum's prayer is invalid (batil).
This is the mufta bihi position.

Lexicon: al-zawruq: boat; al-'ajalah: carriage. Translation (491): [11] The imam should not be mounted and the ma'mum on foot. [12] Or the ma'mum's mount is separate from the imam's mount. [13] If the imam is in one boat and the ma'mum in another, and the boats are not tied together, each boat will go in a different direction, so each will appear separate, so following is not permissible.

Commentary
This passage lists three conditions for valid imamate. The core principle is that the imam and ma'mum must appear to be offering the same prayer together, not as separate individuals. If the imam is on a moving animal and the ma'mum is on foot, or they are on separate mounts, or in separate boats not tied together, their movements will diverge, breaking the unity of the congregation. Hence, the prayer is invalid. These conditions are explained in light of the general principle established earlier.

Following an Imam of Another Madhhab When the Ma'mum Knows of an Invalidating Act
Explains that ma'mum must not know of a factor invalidating imam's prayer per his own madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Hanafi ma'mum knows that his Shafi'i imam performed an act that invalidates wudu in the Hanafi school, and explain the reasons.

Core Idea
A ma'mum cannot validly follow an imam whose prayer he believes to be invalid according to his own madhhab.

This passage tackles a practical inter-madhhab scenario: can a Hanafi follower pray behind a Shafi'i imam who has passed blood or vomited without renewing wudu? The Hanafi school rules that if the ma'mum knows of this, his following is invalid. We will explore the reasoning and the practical consequence of this dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly state what the Hanafi school holds regarding the validity of the ma'mum's prayer when he knows of an invalidating factor in the imam's prayer according to Hanafi.
2
Identify the opposing school and its proof
Identify the Shafi'i position and the basis for their ruling that the imam's prayer remains valid.
Shafi'i does not consider blood or vomiting as breaking wudu.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the two reasons given by the Hanafi school: (1) lack of sincere intention to follow, (2) the ma'mum's own prayer becoming invalid by following an invalid prayer.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in rulings between the two schools for this scenario.
The Hanafi ma'mum cannot follow; the Shafi'i ma'mum can.

The reasons: (1) the ma'mum cannot sincerely intend to follow an imam whose prayer he believes to be invalid; (2) the ma'mum's own prayer becomes invalid if he follows a prayer he believes to be invalid. Conditions Invalidating Iqtida: Preserving Apparent Unity
States conditions invalidating iqtida due to separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios from the passage where iqtida is invalid and explain the underlying principle of apparent unity.

Core Idea
Iqtida is invalid if the follower and imam appear to be praying separately.

Congregational prayer requires unity between imam and follower. But what happens when the imam is on a horse and the follower is walking, or when they are in separate boats? The Hanafi school lays down specific conditions to ensure that the congregation appears united. This lesson examines three such conditions from the matn of Thamaratun Najah that invalidate iqtida because they create a visual or physical separation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage begins by stating that iqtida is valid in principle, then lists exceptions. Note that the default ruling is validity; the following conditions are invalidators (mufsidat).
The general rule: 'صح الاقتداء في الصحيح' – iqtida is correct in the valid (normal) case.
2
Parse the three conditions
Extract each of the three scenarios: (1) imam riding, follower walking; (2) follower riding a different animal not behind the imam's animal; (3) follower in a boat, imam in another boat not tied together. Understand the wording precisely.
The second condition uses 'غير دابّة امامه' – a beast other than the one in front of the imam (i.e., not following the imam's animal).
3
Understand the underlying rationale
In all three cases, the imam and follower are not on the same conveyance or moving together. This creates a situation where they do not appear to be praying as a single unit. The condition of 'apparent unity' (i.e., the congregation looks like one prayer) is crucial in Hanafi fiqh.
The opposite case (boats tied together) is implicitly valid.
4
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Use qiyas to extend the ruling to modern conveyances: cars, buses, trains, etc. The key question is whether the imam and follower are on the same vehicle or attached such that their movement is synchronized.
If the follower is in a car behind the imam's car, the cars are not physically attached, so iqtida is invalid unless they are considered as a single unit by custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صح الاقتداء في الصحيح وان لا يكون الامام راكبا والمقتدى راجلا او راكبا غير دابّة امامه وان لا يكون في سفينة والامام في أخرى غير مقترنة بها
Correct following in prayer is valid, and [it is required] that the imam not be riding while the follower is walking, or that the follower be riding a different animal than the one in front of the imam, and that [the follower] not be in a boat while the imam is in another boat not attached to it.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Thamaratun Najah. The author states the general rule that iqtida is valid under normal conditions, but then lists three conditions that invalidate it based on the principle that the follower and imam must appear to be praying together. The first condition: if the imam is riding and the follower is walking, the iqtida is invalid because the rider's movement will diverge from the pedestrian's. Second: if the follower is riding a different animal than the imam's animal (not behind the imam's animal), then again their paths diverge. Third: if the follower is in one boat and the imam in another boat not tied together, then the boats may move separately, creating separation. The underlying principle is that if the distance or movement suggests they are praying separately, iqtida is not valid.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
الامام (al-imam): The person leading the prayer.
المقتدى (al-muqtadi): The person following the imam in prayer.
غير مقترنة (ghayr muqtarinah): Not attached or tied together (of boats).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Imam on a camel, follower on a donkey behind him.
B) Imam in a boat, follower on a boat tied to it.
C) Imam riding, follower walking.
D) Imam in one boat, follower in a separate boat not tied.

Key Takeaway
Iqtida is invalid if the follower and imam are on different conveyances that suggest separate prayers, unless they are attached or moving as one unit.

Invalidity When Follower Knows Imam's Prayer is Corrupt
States condition that follower must not know of corrupting element in imam's state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the follower must not know of a corrupting element in the imam's state according to the follower's own legal opinion, and apply it to scenarios involving differing madhhab rulings on wudu-breakers.

Core Idea
If the follower believes the imam's prayer is invalid, following becomes impossible.

This passage presents a subtle but important condition for valid congregational prayer. It addresses the situation where the follower's own legal opinion conflicts with the imam's practice. The ruling hinges on the follower's subjective belief, not the objective validity of the imam's prayer. Understanding this condition helps prevent inadvertent invalidation of salah in inter-madhhab settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the Arabic text: 'وان لا يعلم المقتدى من حال امامه مفسدا في زعم الماموم'. The condition is that the follower must not know of a 'mufsid' (corrupting element) in the imam's state, where 'mufsid' is defined by the follower's own legal opinion (za'm al-m'amum).
The term 'za'm' refers to the follower's belief based on his madhhab.
2
Understand the subjective nature
The phrase 'في زعم الماموم' makes the condition subjective. It does not matter if the imam's prayer is objectively valid; what matters is what the follower believes to be invalidating. This is crucial in inter-madhhab situations.
3
Apply the example
The text gives an example: 'كخروج دم او قيء لم يعد بعده وضوئه'. Suppose the imam is Shafi'i (where bleeding does not break wudu) and does not renew wudu after bleeding. A Hanafi follower knows this and believes bleeding invalidates wudu. According to the condition, the follower's iqtida is invalid because he knows a mufsid in the imam's state.
The result: the follower must break off and pray alone or repeat the salah.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle that valid iqtida requires the follower to genuinely intend to follow the imam. If the follower believes the imam's prayer is corrupt, that intention is undermined. Hence, the iqtida becomes batil.
This principle applies regardless of whether the imam's prayer is actually valid in his own school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لا يعلم المقتدى من حال امامه مفسدا في زعم الماموم كخروج دم او قيء لم يعد بعده وضوئه
And that the follower not know of a state of the imam that is invalidating in the opinion of the follower, such as blood exiting or vomiting after which he did not renew his wudu.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This is another condition for valid iqtida. The follower must not be aware of something in the imam's state that, according to the follower's madhab, would invalidate the imam's prayer. For example, if the imam is a Shafi'i and bleeds (which does not break wudu in the Shafi'i school) and does not renew wudu, but the follower is a Hanafi who believes bleeding breaks wudu, then if the follower knows this, the iqtida is invalid because the follower considers the imam's prayer invalid. The underlying principle is that the follower's intention to follow is undermined when he believes the imam's prayer is corrupt. The condition is subjective: it depends on the follower's own legal opinion (z'an al-m'amum), not necessarily the actual ruling.

Key Terms
مفسد (mufsid): Something that invalidates the prayer, here specifically acts that break wudu.
زعم المأموم (za'm al-m'amum): The follower's opinion or belief about what invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the imam's wudu is broken.
B) Because the follower believes the imam's prayer is invalid.
C) Because the imam did not renew wudu.
D) Because the imam's madhab is different.

Key Takeaway
Valid iqtida requires that the follower not know of any corrupting element in the imam's state according to the follower's own legal opinion.

Six Valid Cases of Iqtida Despite Status Differences
Lists six valid iqtida pairs despite status differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six cases where iqtida is valid despite differences in status and explain the general principle that validates each case.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, iqtida remains valid when the follower's status is equal or slightly lesser than the imam, as shown in six specific cases.

This lesson breaks down a concise matn from the Hanafi tradition that enumerates six pairs of imam-follower status differences where iqtida is still valid. You will learn to identify each pair, understand the rationale behind its validity, and apply this principle to similar scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Extract the six pairs
Read the Arabic passage and identify each pair of imam and follower. Note the two roles in each case: e.g., متوضئ behind متيمم (one with wudu behind a mutayammim).
There are six pairs; list them all.
2
Classify the difference
For each pair, determine what type of status difference exists: purity (wudu vs tayammum, washing vs wiping), posture (standing vs sitting, hump, gesturing), or prayer type (nafl vs fard).
This helps see the pattern.
3
Understand the reasoning
For each case, reason why it is valid. The general principle: the follower's status is either equal or slightly lower, but the essence of the act is preserved. For example, tayammum is a valid substitute for wudu, so following a mutayammim is allowed.
Refer to the commentary for explanations.
4
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Given a new scenario (e.g., a person with wudu behind someone with a bandage wipe), decide if it fits one of the six patterns. If it does not, state why it is invalid.
This tests your understanding of the underlying principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح اقتداء متوضئ بمتيمم وغاسل بماسح وقائم بقاعد وباحدب ومؤم بمثله ومتنفّل بمفترض
And valid is the following of one with wudu behind a mutayammim, and one who washes (his feet) behind one who wipes (over socks), and a standing person behind a sitting one, and one with a hump (kyphosis) behind one like him, and one who gestures (by leaning) behind one like him, and one performing nafl behind one performing fard.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage lists six specific cases where iqtida is valid even though the imam and follower differ in the level of purity or prayer posture. The general principle is that iqtida is valid when the imam is of higher or equal status, and also when the imam is slightly lower but similar. These six cases are applications: (1) A person with wudu can follow a mutayammim because tayammum is akin to wudu. (2) One who washes his feet can follow one who wipes over socks, since wiping is a valid substitute. (3) A standing person can follow a sitting person because both are in qiyam, though sitting is lesser. (4) A person with a hump (who cannot straighten) can follow another like him. (5) A person who gestures (due to illness) can follow another who gestures. (6) A nafl prayer can be performed behind a fard prayer, as the fard is higher. In all cases, the iqtida is valid.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): One who performs tayammum instead of wudu due to lack of water.
ماسح (masih): One who wipes over his khuffs (socks) instead of washing feet.
قاعد (qa'id): One who prays sitting due to inability to stand.
احدب (ahdab): A person with a hunched back who cannot straighten.
مؤم (mu'im): One who gestures (by leaning) in prayer due to severe illness.
متنفل (mutanafill): One performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
مفترض (muftarid): One performing obligatory (fard) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the six valid cases listed?
A) A person with wudu behind a mutayammim.
B) A standing person behind a sitting one.
C) A person praying nafl behind a person praying fard.
D) A person with wudu behind one who has not done wudu.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, iqtida is valid in six specific cases where the imam's status is equal or slightly lesser, based on the principle of similarity and substitution.

Valid Following Despite Status Differences in Prayer
Enumerates six cases of valid iqtida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six cases where following an imam with a different state of purity or posture is valid according to the Hanafi school and identify the underlying principle of relative status.

Core Idea
Following an imam is valid when the imam is equal or slightly inferior, but not vastly inferior.

The Hanafi school teaches that the validity of following an imam (iqtida) depends on the relative status of the imam and follower in terms of purity and physical ability. This lesson explores six specific cases enumerated in the classical text, showing that differences such as tayammum versus wudu or sitting versus standing do not automatically invalidate the prayer. We will examine the principle that governs these cases and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
List the six cases
Identify each of the six scenarios mentioned: mutawaddi behind mutayammim, foot-washer behind khuff-wiper, standing behind sitting, hunchback behind hunchback, gesturer behind gesturer, and nafl performer behind fard performer.
These are all cases from the matn.
2
Understand the principle of relative status
The commentary explains that following is valid if the imam is of equal or slightly inferior status, but invalid if vastly inferior. Analyze how each case fits this principle.
For example, tayammum is near to wudu, so following is valid.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As is cited: he performed tayammum due to cold and led companions in prayer. Consider how this proves the validity of a mutawaddi following a mutayammim.
This shows prophetic approval.
4
Identify cross-madhhab difference
Note that some other schools may not allow a mutawaddi to follow a mutayammim under normal circumstances. Understand the basis of the ikhtilaf.

(ابو داؤدشریف، باب اذ اخاف الحب البرد أيتيمم ص ۵۴، نمبر ۳۳۴ / بخاری شریف ، باب اذا خاف الجعب على نفسه المرض اوالموت، ص ۴۹ نمبر ۳۴۵) اس حدیث میں حضرت عمرو نے جنابت کا تیم کر کے ساتھیوں کو نماز پڑھائی ہے۔ جب کہ ساتھی وضو اور غسل
And it is valid for a person with wudu to follow one with tayammum, and a person who washes (feet) to follow one who wipes (over khuffs), and a standing person to follow a sitting person, and a hunchback, and a person indicating by gesture to follow his like, and a person performing nafl to follow a person performing fard.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating six specific cases in which it is valid for a follower (muqtadi) to pray behind an imam even though there is a difference in their states of purity or physical ability. The text explains the underlying principle: if the imam is of a higher or equal level compared to the follower, following is valid; if the imam is slightly inferior, it is also valid; but if the imam is vastly inferior, it is not valid. The cases include: (1) a person with wudu following one who performed tayammum, (2) a person who washes feet following one who wipes over khuffs, (3) a standing person following a sitting person, (4) a hunchback following another hunchback, (5) a person who prays by gesture following his like, and (6) a person performing nafl prayer following one performing fard prayer. For each case, the text provides evidence from hadith, such as the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As who performed tayammum due to cold and led companions in prayer, and the hadith of the Prophet wiping over khuffs, and the hadith that the Prophet prayed sitting while Abu Bakr stood, etc. The Hanafi position is that these are all valid based on the principle of equality or slight inferiority, not vast inferiority.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidā’): Following the imam in prayer by intending to pray behind him and conforming to his actions.
متيمم (mutayammim): One who performs dry ablution (tayammum) instead of wudu due to lack of water or illness.
ماسح (māsiḥ): One who wipes over leather socks (khuffs) instead of washing feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is invalid because tayammum is inferior to wudu.
C) Only if the imam is also with wudu.
D) Only if the follower also performs tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates iqtida in six cases where the imam's state is equal or slightly inferior, based on the principle of relative status and supported by hadith.

Obligation to Repeat and Inform When Imam's Prayer is Invalid
Ruling on repetition and informing when imam's prayer is nullified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an imam must repeat his prayer and inform the congregation upon discovering invalidity, and cite the proof from the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer is invalid, so is the followers'—the imam must repeat and inform.

This passage addresses a common scenario: an imam discovers after completing the prayer that it was invalid due to a hidden defect, such as being in a state of janabah. The Hanafi school holds that the imam is obliged to repeat his prayer and to inform the congregation so they may repeat theirs. The ruling is supported by prophetic and companion traditions that establish the connection between the imam's validity and the followers' prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses what must be done when the imam's prayer is discovered to be invalid. Identify the two obligations: the imam repeating his prayer and informing the followers.
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) leading prayer while junub and then repeating with the followers, and the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that if the imam's prayer is corrupt, those behind him are corrupt.
The hadith is mursal, but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that the Prophet (ﷺ) repeated and ordered the followers to repeat, indicating obligation. The athar explicitly states the invalidity of the followers' prayer when the imam's is invalid.
The connection is direct: the followers' prayer is dependent on the imam's validity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may argue that if the followers were unaware, their prayer is valid. The Hanafi school holds they must still repeat because the act itself was invalid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) due to the strength of the evidence from the Prophet's action and the principle that a corrupt imam corrupts the followers' prayer.
The authority is based on the zahir al-riwayah traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(كتاب الآثار لامام محمد ، باب ما يقطع الصلوۃ ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ
(494) And if the invalidity of his imam's prayer becomes apparent, he repeats, and the imam is obliged to inform the people to repeat their prayers as much as possible.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage states that if it becomes known that the imam's prayer was invalid (e.g., because he was in a state of major ritual impurity without knowledge), the imam must repeat his prayer and must also inform the congregation so that they may repeat theirs. The Hanafi position is supported by the hadith that the Prophet once led prayer while in a state of janabah, and then both he and the followers repeated the prayer. Also, the athar from Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i) that if the imam's prayer is corrupt, the prayer of those behind him is corrupt. And the athar from 'Ali that he led people while junub and then ordered them to repeat. Thus the ruling is established.

Key Terms
بطلان (buṭlān): Invalidity of prayer due to a defect such as being in a state of janabah.
اعلام (i‘lām): Informing the congregation that their prayer needs to be repeated.
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl before prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The prayer is still valid and no repetition is needed.
D) Only the congregation must repeat, not the imam.

Key Takeaway
Upon discovering the invalidity of his prayer, the imam must repeat and inform the congregation, because the followers' prayer is invalidated by the imam's invalidity.

Standing Behind a Sitting Imam is Valid
Ruling that standing behind a sitting imam is valid, with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that standing behind a sitting imam is valid and identify the hadith proof that supports it.

Core Idea
Standing behind a sitting imam in prayer is valid, proven by the Prophet's own practice during his illness.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: when the imam cannot stand due to illness or excuse, he may lead the prayer while sitting, and the followers may stand. The Hanafi school affirms the validity of this arrangement based on a clear hadith from the Prophet's final illness. We will examine the ruling and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? State the hukm level (valid/invalid, sahih/batil) according to the text.
The act is followers standing behind a sitting imam; the ruling is sahih (valid).
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite? Quote the hadith and its source.
The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about the Prophet's illness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove the ruling? Which part of the narration shows the permissibility?
The explicit action of Abu Bakr and the people standing while the Prophet sat demonstrates permission.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools disagree? What is their position?
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it preferred for followers to sit or consider it makruh without excuse.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
What is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school and why?
The Hanafi position is that standing is valid and sunna when the imam has an excuse.

The proof is the incident when the Prophet (peace be upon him) was ill and led the prayer sitting, while Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) stood next to him transmitting the takbir, and the people stood behind. This demonstrates that a standing follower behind a sitting imam is valid and the prayer is correct.
