Nafl Behind Fard Imam: Validity and Proof
Ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that nafl prayer behind a fard imam is valid and explain the hadith proof that supports it.

Core Idea
A fard imam is of higher rank; a nafl follower can join him.

This lesson addresses a common situation: a person has already prayed fard at home but then arrives at a congregation. Can he join? The Hanafi school says yes, and the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ directly confirms this. Understanding the proof strengthens confidence in following the imam even with a different intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is joining a congregational prayer (the imam is praying fard) when the follower has already performed fard or intends nafl. The ruling from the text: it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text quotes a hadith from Jabir ibn Yazid where the Prophet ﷺ instructed two men to join the congregation even though they had already prayed at home, saying their second prayer would be nafl.
Hadith reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The Prophet's explicit statement 'for it will be a nafl for him' shows that following an imam in fard prayer can count as nafl for the follower, establishing the validity of differing intentions.
The key phrase is 'fainnaha lahu nāfilah'.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require the follower's intention to match the imam's. The Hanafi school differs based on this hadith, allowing the follower to have a different intention.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) فرض پڑھنے والا اعلی درجہ کا ہوتا ہے اور نفل پڑھنے والا ادنی درجہ کا، اس لئے نفل پڑھنے والا فرض پڑھنے والے کی اقتدا کر سکتا ہے
(۵) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن يزيد انه صلى مع رسول الله ، وهو غلام شاب فلما صلى اذا رجلان لم يصليا في ناحية المسجد فدعا بهما فجيئ بهما ترعد فرائصهما فقال ما منعكما ان تصليا معنا؟ قالا قد صلينا في رحالنا قال لا تفعلوا اذا صلى احدكم في رحله ثم ادرك الامام ولم يصل فليصل معه فانها له نافلة ـ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن صلی فی منزلہ ثم ادرک الجماعة یصلی معتصم ،ص۹۲، نمبر ٫۵۷۵رتر ندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل یصلی وحدہ ثم یدرک الجماعۃ ، ص ۵۲، نمبر ۲۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض پڑھنے والے کے پیچھے نفل نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
(4) The one performing fard is of a higher rank, and the one performing nafl is of a lower rank, therefore the one performing nafl can follow the one performing fard. (5) There is a hadith: From Jabir ibn Yazid that he prayed with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he was a young boy. When he prayed, there were two men who had not prayed in a corner of the mosque. He called them and they were brought trembling in fear. He said: 'What prevented you from praying with us?' They said: 'We prayed at our dwellings.' He said: 'Do not do that. When one of you prays at his dwelling then catches the imam and has not prayed, let him pray with him, for it will be a nafl for him.' (Abu Dawud, Book of One who prays at home then catches the congregation, p. 92, #575; Tirmidhi, Chapter about a man who prays alone then catches the congregation, p. 52, #219) This hadith indicates that one can pray nafl behind one who is praying fard.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling: a person who has already performed his fard prayer or intends to perform nafl can validly join a congregation where the imam is performing fard prayer. The reasoning is that the one performing fard is of higher rank, so following an imam of higher rank is valid. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told two men who had already prayed at home to join the congregation anyway, and that their second prayer would be considered nafl. This establishes that nafl prayer behind a fard-imam is permissible and valid in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer (voluntary)
فرض (fard): Obligatory prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He should not join because his obligation is fulfilled.
B) He should join and his prayer will be counted as nafl.
C) He must inform the imam of his intention first.
D) He can only join if the congregation is praying nafl.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates nafl prayer behind a fard imam based on the explicit hadith proof.

Imam's Invalid Prayer: Obligation to Repeat and Inform
Ruling and commentary on imam's invalid prayer requiring repetition and notification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an imam's prayer is found invalid and explain the obligation to inform the congregation.

Core Idea
When an imam's prayer is invalid, the followers' prayers are also invalid; the imam must repeat and inform them.

In congregational prayer, the validity of the follower's prayer depends entirely on the imam's prayer. If the imam later discovers his prayer was invalid—due to impurity, missed condition, or a nullifier—the imam must not only repeat his own prayer but also notify the congregation to the best of his ability, so they may repeat as well. This lesson examines the evidence for this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: 'اگر اپنے امام کی نماز باطل ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے تو نماز دہرالے۔ اور امام کو لازم ہے کہ قوم کو حتی الوسع اطلاع کر دے۔' The imam must repeat and must inform to the extent possible.
2
Understand Why Followers Must Repeat
The commentary states that the followers' prayer is also invalid. The proofs establish that the Prophet and Ali (ra) repeated with the people after discovering impurity.
The follower's prayer is a mirror of the imam's—if it breaks, the reflection breaks.
3
Examine the Evidence
Four proofs: (1) Mursal hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib; (2) Athar from Ibrahim; (3) Athar from Ali; (4) Hadith of Abu Hurairah showing the Prophet informed the congregation.
The mursal hadith is considered zanni al-thubut, but strengthened by multiple narrations.
4
Apply the Ruling
In a scenario where an imam finishes prayer and then realizes he was without wudu, he must repeat his prayer and inform those who prayed behind him to also repeat.
If informing is impossible (e.g., congregation dispersed), the obligation drops but his own repetition remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الامامة
(۴۹۴) وان ظهر بطلان صلوة امامه اعاد ويلزم الامام اعلام القوم باعادة صلوتهم بالقدر الممكن والے تھے۔
ترجمه : (۴۹۴) اور اگر اپنے امام کی نماز باطل ہونا ظاہر ہو جائے تو نماز دہرالے۔ اور امام کو لازم ہے کہ قوم کو حتی الوسع اپنی اپنی نمازوں کے اعادہ کرنے کی مختار روایت میں ہے کہ اطلاع کر دے۔
تشريح : اگر امام کو پتہ چل جائے کہ نماز فاسد ہو چکی ہے تو وہ نماز دہرالے، اور حتی الامکان مقتدی کو بھی اس کی اطلاع کر دے تا کہ وہ بھی اپنی نماز دہرالے، کیونکہ انکی نماز بھی فاسد ہو چکی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) مقتدی کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو چکی ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سعيد بن مسيب ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلي بالناس وهو جنب فاعاد واعادوا - ( دار قطنی ، باب صلوۃ الامام و ھو جب او محدث، ج اول ص ۱۳۵۴ نمبر ۱۳۵۴) اس حدیث مرسل سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے بھی نماز لوٹائی اور مقتدیوں نے بھی نماز لوٹائی (۲) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا فسدت صلوة الامام فسدت صلوة من خلفه . (كتاب الآثار لامام محمد ، باب ما يقطع الصلوۃ ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگی تو مقتدی کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ (۳) عن على انه صلى بالقوم وهو جنب فاعاد ثم امرهم فاعادوا ( سنن للبیھقی ، باب امامته الحب ج ثانی ص ۵۶۰، نمبر ۲۰۷۸ ردار قطنی ، باب صلوۃ الامام وھو جب اومحدث ، ج اول، ص۳۵۴ نمبر ۱۳۵۵) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی بھی نماز لوٹائیں گے، اور یہ بھی پتہ چلا کہ مقتدی کو اس کی اطلاع دے (۴) اس حدیث میں حضور نے اپنے جنبی ہونے کی اطلاع دی ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال اقيمت الصلاة فسوى الناس صفوفهم فخرج رسول الله فتقدم و هو جنب فقال على مكانكم فرجع فاغتسل ثم خرج و رأسه يقطر ماء فصلى بهم - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا قال الامام مکانکم حتی نرجع انتظر وه ، ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۶۴۰ مسلم شریف، باب متی یقوم الناس للصلاة ؟ ص ۲۴۵، نمبر ۶۰۵ /۱۳۶۷) اس حدیث میں نماز فاسد ہونے اطلاع دی۔
Chapter of Imamate. (494) And if the invalidity of the imam's prayer becomes apparent, he repeats it and it is incumbent upon the imam to inform the people to repeat their prayers to the extent possible. Translation: (494) And if the invalidity of one's imam's prayer becomes apparent, then repeat the prayer. And it is necessary for the imam to inform the people to the extent possible to repeat their prayers; in the preferred narration it says he should inform. Commentary: If the imam learns that the prayer has become invalid, then he repeats it, and as much as possible informs the follower so that he too repeats his prayer, because his prayer has also become invalid. Evidence: (1) The follower's prayer has also become invalid; the proof is this hadith: From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, led the people in prayer while in a state of major impurity (junub), so he repeated and they repeated. (2) From Ibrahim: 'When the imam's prayer becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' (3) From 'Ali that he led the people in prayer while in a state of major impurity, so he repeated and then commanded them to repeat. (4) In this hadith the Prophet informed them of his state of major impurity: From Abu Hurairah that the prayer was established and the people straightened their rows, then the Messenger of Allah came out and advanced, while in a state of major impurity, and said, 'Stay in your places,' so he went back, performed a full bath, then came out with his head dripping water and prayed with them. This hadith indicates informing about the invalidity of the prayer.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on imamate. It states that if it becomes known that the imam's prayer was invalid (e.g., due to lack of purity or a nullifying factor), the imam must repeat his prayer and inform the congregation to the best of his ability so they may also repeat. The commentary explains that the followers' prayers are also invalid because they followed an invalid imam. Four pieces of evidence are provided: (1) a mursal hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) once led prayer while in a state of major impurity and then repeated it along with the people; (2) an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stating that corruption of the imam's prayer corrupts the followers' prayer; (3) an athar that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) did the same; (4) a hadith from Abu Hurairah where the Prophet informed people of his impurity before repeating. These proofs establish the obligation of informing the congregation.

Key Terms
إمام (imam): The person leading the congregational prayer
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer
اعادة (i'adah): Repeating the prayer due to its invalidity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must the imam do if he discovers his prayer was invalid?
A) Only repeat his own prayer silently
B) Repeat his prayer and inform the congregation to the best of his ability
C) Repeat the prayer but not inform anyone
D) Cancel the congregation and pray alone

Key Takeaway
When the imam's prayer is invalid, his repetition and notification of the congregation are wajib, and the followers' prayers are automatically invalid and must be repeated.

Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer: The Condition of Strength
Section on valid excuses for missing congregation, with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for a valid excuse to miss congregational prayer and apply the hadith evidence to determine excusing strength.

Core Idea
Excuse must be strong; the Prophet attended despite severe illness, showing congregation's high importance.

This section explains that missing congregational prayer is not a trivial matter. The text enumerates eighteen recognized excuses but places a crucial condition: the excuse must be strong (qawi). A minor excuse does not justify absence. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) dragged his feet to the mosque, emphasizing the seriousness of congregation. Understanding this condition helps a Muslim balance the obligation of congregation with genuine hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Congregational prayer is wajib on men. The text opens a section on what drops this obligation.
Hanafi position: congregation is wajib, not sunnah.
2
List the Excuses
There are 18 recognized excuses. Memorize them (e.g., severe illness, heavy rain, fear for life or property).
The text does not list them all here, but they are known from other classical works.
3
Condition of Strength
The excuse must be strong (qawi). If minor, congregation cannot be missed.
This condition is crucial: a mere headache or slight inconvenience does not suffice.
4
Study the Hadith Proof
The Prophet attended despite severe illness, walking with support and his feet dragging on the ground. This sets the benchmark for 'strong excuse'.
Hadith from Bukhari #664.
5
Apply the Rule
Given a scenario, decide if the excuse is strong enough to miss congregation by comparing to the Prophet's condition.
E.g., mild cold vs. high fever with difficulty walking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : جماعت ساقط ہونے کے بیان میں
ضروری نوٹ : یہ اٹھارہ اعذار ہیں جنکی موجودگی میں جماعت چھوڑ دینے کی گنجائش ہے، اور اگر وہ جماعت کا پابند تھا تو ان شاء اللہ جماعت کا ثواب بھی ملے گا۔ لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ یہ اعذارقوی ہوں تب گنجائش ہوگی ، اورتھوڑا بہت عذر ہے تو جمات چھوڑنے کی گنجائش نہیں۔
وجہ : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پاؤں گھسیٹتے ہوئے حضور مسجد میں تشریف لے گئے جماعت کی اتنی اہمیت ہے،حدیث یہ ہے۔
كنا عند عائشة فذكرنا المواظبة على الصلاة و التعظيم لها ..... فوجد النبي من نفسه خفة فخرج يهادى بين رجـلیـن كـانـی انـظـر رجليه يخطان الارض من الوجع - ( بخاری شریف ، باب حد المرض ان يشهد الجماعة ، ص ۱۰۸، نمبر ۶۶۴)
اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اتنا مرض ہو کہ زمین پر پاؤں گھسیٹ کر چل سکتا ہو تب بھی جماعت میں جانا چاہئے ، اس سے زیادہ ہو تب غیر حاضر ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔
Section: On what causes congregation to be dropped.
Important note: There are eighteen excuses in the presence of which there is leeway to leave the congregation, and if he was regular in congregation, then insha'Allah he will receive the reward of congregation. But the condition is that these excuses should be strong; then there is leeway. If the excuse is minor, there is no leeway to leave the congregation.
Reason: In this hadith, the Prophet went to the mosque dragging his feet, such is the importance of congregation. The hadith is: 'We were with 'A'ishah and we mentioned perseverance in prayer and reverence for it... The Prophet felt some lightness, so he went out walking between two men, as if I saw his feet making lines on the ground from pain.' (Bukhari, chapter on the limit of illness to attend congregation, p. 108, #664)
This hadith indicates that if the illness is such that one can drag his feet on the ground, he should still go to the congregation. If it is more severe than that, then he is allowed to be absent.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a new section on the excuses that allow missing congregational prayer. It states that there are eighteen recognized excuses. If the excuse is strong (like severe illness, rain, fear, etc.), then one may leave the congregation without sin, and if such a person normally attends, he may still receive the reward by intention. However, if the excuse is trivial, it is not permissible to miss the congregation. The evidence is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) attended the mosque despite being so ill that he had to walk supported between two men and his feet dragged on the ground. This shows the great emphasis on congregation and that only a severe excuse (greater than that) justifies absence.

Key Terms
اعذار (a'dhar): Excuses that permit missing congregational prayer
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer (specifically the obligatory prayers performed in congregation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition is required for the 18 excuses to allow missing congregational prayer?
A) The excuses must be listed in the Quran
B) The excuses must be strong (قوی)
C) The person must have made up the missed prayer later
D) The person must inform the imam

Key Takeaway
A strong excuse is required to legitimately miss congregational prayer; the Prophet's own practice sets the benchmark.

Ruling When Imam's Prayer is Invalid Due to Janabah
Ruling with two hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that followers must repeat their prayer if the imam was in a state of janabah, and identify the two hadith proofs that support this ruling.

Core Idea
If the imam’s prayer is invalid due to janabah, the followers’ prayer is also invalid and must be repeated.

In congregational prayer, the follower’s prayer is tied to the imam’s validity. This lesson examines a specific case: when the imam leads the prayer while being junub (in major impurity). The Hanafi school rules that both the imam’s and the followers’ prayers are invalid and must be repeated. We will explore the textual proofs from the Prophet’s sunnah and the effect of Sayyiduna Ali.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Carefully read the opening statement: 'If the imam’s prayer becomes invalid, the follower’s prayer also becomes invalid.' Identify that this is a ruling about the consequence of the imam’s invalidity on the muqtadi.
The ruling is categorical: both prayers are batil, regardless of the follower’s knowledge.
2
Identify the First Proof (Athar of Ali)
Read the athar from Sayyiduna Ali: he prayed while junub, then repeated his prayer and ordered the congregation to repeat. Ask: What does this tell us about the followers’ obligation?
The command to repeat shows that the followers’ prayer was also invalid.
3
Analyse the Second Proof (Hadith of Abu Hurairah)
Read the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: the Prophet realized he was junub, asked the people to stay, performed ghusl, and then led the prayer again. Consider: Why did the Prophet inform them? What does his action imply about the first prayer?
The Prophet’s repetition indicates the first attempt was invalid, and the followers were required to wait and repeat with him.
4
Extract the Dalalah
For each proof, determine how it proves the ruling. In the athar, the command to repeat shows dependence. In the hadith, the Prophet’s action of leaving and returning shows that the followers could not continue and had to start anew.
Both proofs establish that the follower’s prayer is contingent on the imam’s validity.
5
Note the Intra-Madhhab Agreement and Cross-Madhhab Difference
Observe that Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad all agree. Then note that the Shafi‘i school differs: they consider the follower’s prayer valid if the follower was unaware. This difference has practical consequences.
Understanding the ikhtilaf helps in applying the correct ruling in multi-madhhab contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگی تو مقتدی کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ (۳) عن على انه صلى بالقوم وهو جنب فاعاد ثم امرهم فاعادوا ( سنن للبیھقی ، باب امامته الحب ج ثانی ص ۵۶۰، نمبر ۲۰۷۸ ردار قطنی ، باب صلوۃ الامام وھو جب اومحدث ، ج اول، ص۳۵۴ نمبر ۱۳۵۵) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی بھی نماز لوٹائیں گے، اور یہ بھی پتہ چلا کہ مقتدی کو اس کی اطلاع دے (۴) اس حدیث میں حضور نے اپنے جنبی ہونے کی اطلاع دی ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال اقيمت الصلاة فسوى الناس صفوفهم فخرج رسول الله الله فتقدم و هو جنب فقال على مكانكم فرجع فاغتسل ثم خرج و رأسه يقطر ماء فصلى بهم - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا قال الامام مکانکم حتی نرجع انتظر وه ، ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۶۴۰ مسلم شریف، باب متی یقوم الناس للصلاة ؟ ص ۲۴۵، نمبر ۶۰۵ /۱۳۶۷) اس حدیث میں نماز فاسد ہونے اطلاع دی۔
Chapter: If the imam's prayer becomes invalid, then the follower's prayer will also become invalid. (3) From Ali that he led people in prayer while in a state of janabah, so he repeated (the prayer) and ordered them to repeat (al-Bayhaqi, Sunan, chapter on imamate of a junub, vol. 2 p. 560, no. 2078; al-Daraqutni, chapter on prayer of an imam while junub or with hadath, vol. 1 p. 354, no. 1355). From this effect it is known that the followers will also repeat the prayer, and it is also known that the follower should inform him. (4) In this hadith, the Prophet informed of his janabah. From Abu Hurairah: the iqamah was given, and the people straightened their rows; the Messenger of Allah came out and stepped forward while in janabah. He said, 'Stay in your places,' then he went back and performed ghusl, then came out with water dripping from his head and led them in prayer. (Bukhari, chapter: if the imam says 'stay in your places' until we return, wait... p. 105, no. 640; Muslim, chapter: when do people stand for prayer? p. 245, no. 605/1367) In this hadith, informing of the invalid prayer.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from the Hanafi madhhab that if the imam’s prayer is invalid due to janabah or lack of wudu, the followers must also repeat their prayer. The author provides two proofs: first, the effect (athar) of Sayyiduna Ali where he prayed while junub and then ordered the congregation to repeat after his own repetition. Second, the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet, realizing he was junub, left the prayer, performed ghusl, and then led the prayer again, thus informing the followers of the invalidity. The commentary clarifies that the follower must also inform the imam if they discover an issue. This ruling is based on the principle that the follower’s prayer is contingent on the imam’s prayer; if the imam’s prayer is batil, so is the follower’s. Note: This is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli).

Key Terms
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl before prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): Follower in congregational prayer, bound by the imam's prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a proof cited in this passage for the ruling that followers must repeat if the imam was junub?
A) The effect of Ali leading prayer while junub and ordering repetition.
B) The hadith of Abu Hurairah describing the Prophet's action.
C) A Quranic verse about janabah.
D) The consensus of the Hanafi imams.

Key Takeaway
If the imam's prayer is invalid due to janabah, the followers' prayer is also invalid and must be repeated, as proven by the actions of Ali and the Prophet.

Valid Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer
Listing nine excuses with hadith proofs from Thamaratun Najah commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state nine valid excuses that lift the obligation of jama'ah and cite the hadith evidence for rain, cold, fear, darkness, imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation, and illness.

Core Idea
Jama'ah drops when genuine hardship prevents easy access to the mosque — rain, cold, fear, darkness, and physical incapacities.

Congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a heavy duty (wajib) for able men in the Hanafi school, but the Shari'ah does not intend hardship. The Prophet ﷺ provided clear concessions for those facing genuine difficulty. This lesson presents nine excuses explicitly supported by hadith, showing how the Law balances obligation with mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Recognize that the passage assumes jama'ah is an obligation (wajib) and then specifies conditions that lift it. This is typical Hanafi reasoning: ruling first, then exceptions.
The Arabic verb 'yasquṭu' (falls) implies the obligation was active before the excuse.
2
List the excuses from the text
Extract the nine excuses: rain, cold, fear, darkness, imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand/foot, and severe illness. Note that the text says there are eighteen, so the remaining nine are covered elsewhere.
The commentary distinguishes severe illness from mild illness.
3
Match each excuse to its hadith proof
For the first four (rain, cold) go to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar; for fear and also illness, the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. For imprisonment, the precedent of Abu Lubaba; for blindness, the hadith of 'Itban ibn Malik; for paralysis and amputation, the hadith of the bulky Ansari man.
Each hadith shows a specific concession granted by the Prophet ﷺ.
4
Derive the governing principle
All excuses share a common illa (effective cause): significant hardship (mashaqqah) in attending the mosque. The principle is that necessity overrides the obligation of attendance.
The commentary hints that slight illness does not excuse, only severe difficulty.
5
Note the intra-madhhab nuance
While the Hanafi mufta bihi holds jama'ah as wajib, some Hanafis and most other schools consider it sunnah muakkadah. The list then applies to those who follow the wajib position, and for the sunnah view it indicates recommended permission to skip.
This nuance affects the weight of the concession but not the validity of the excuses themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يسقط الجماعة. يسقط حضور الجماعة بواحد من ثمانية عشر شيئا. (٤٩٥) مطر و برد وخوف و ظلمة. ترجمه: (٤٩٥) [۱] بارش - [۲] سخت جاڑا .[۳] خوف۔[۴] سخت تاریکی۔ تشریح : تیز بارش ہو، یا سخت جاڑا ہو، یا سخت خوف ہو کہ باہر نکلوں گا تو دشمن تکلیف پہنچائیں گے یا کوئی اہم چیز ضائع ہو جائے گی ، یا سخت اندھیرا ہو تو اس کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ جماعت میں شریک نہ ہو اور گھر پر نماز پڑھ لے۔ وجه : (۱) بارش اور جاڑے کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے ۔ ان ابن عمر اذن بالصلاة في ليلة ذات برد و ريح ثم قال الا صلى الله صلوا في الرحال ، ثم قال ان رسول الله له كان يأمر المؤذن اذا كانت ليلة ذات برد و مطر يقول الا صلوا في الرحال - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الرخصة في المطر والعلة ان یصلی فی رحلہ ص ۱۰۹ نمبر ۶۶۶ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بارش اور تیز سردی میں نماز گھر میں پڑھے۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الا الله من سمع المنادى فلم يمنعه من اتباعه عذر قـالـوا مـا العذر؟ قال خوف او مرض ، لم تقبل منه الصلاة التي صلی. (ابوداود شریف، باب التشدید فی ترک الجماعة ، ص ۹۱ نمبر (۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خوف یا مرض کی وجہ سے جماعت چھوڑنا جائز ہے۔ (٤٩٦) و حبس و عمى و فلج و قطع يد ورجل وسقام. ترجمه : (٤٩٦) [۵] قید ہو [ ۶ ] نابینا ہونا۔ [۷] فالج [۸] ہاتھ پاؤں کٹے ہوں، [9] بیماری ہو۔ تشریح : آدمی قید میں ہو تو وہ جماعت میں آہی نہیں سکتا ہے اس لئے اس سے جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گی ، نابینا ہو جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ فالج پڑا ہو تو جماعت میں بغیر کسی کے سہارے کے نہیں آسکے گا اور دوسرے کے سہارے پر جماعت واجب نہیں ہوتی اس لئے جماعت ساقط ہو گی ۔ یہی حال ہاتھ پاوں کٹے ہوئے کا ہے، اسی طرح آدمی اتنا بیمار ہو کہ جماعت میں آنا مشکل ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہوگی، اور اگر اتنی بیماری ہے کہ آسانی سے جماعت میں آسکتا ہے تو جماعت ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) قید سے جماعت ساقط ہو ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ ثم غزا رسول الله تبوكا و هي غزوة العسرة ... ففزع ابو لبابة فارتبط بسارية التوبة التي عند باب ام سلمة زوج النبي علي سبعا بين يوم و ليلة في حر شديد لا يأكل فيهن و لا يشرب قطرة - ( دلائل النبوة للمتقی ، باب حدیث ابولبابہ ، ج خامس جی ۲۷۰ ) اس حدیث میں حضرت ابولبابہ نے اپنے آپ کو قید کیا جسکی وجہ سے جماعت ساقط ہوگئی۔ (۲) نابینا ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان عتبان بن مالک و هـو مـن اصحاب النبي ... انه اتى رسول الله فقال يا رسول الله اني قد انكرت بصری و انا اصلی لقومی و اذا كانت الامطار سال الوادي الذي بيني و بينهم و لم استطع ان آتی مسجدهم فاصلی لهم ووددت انک یا رسول الله ! تأتى فتصلى فی مصلی اتخذه مصلی ( مسلم شریف ، باب الرخصة فى التخلف عن الجماعة لعذر ، ص ۲۵۶، نمبر ۷ ۱۴۹۶/۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آنکھ میں کمزوری ہو تو جماعت چھوڑ سکتا ہے۔ یہ بھی ہے کہ کیچڑ اور پانی اتنا ہو کہ جا نہ سکا ہو تو جماعت چھوڑنے کی گنجائش ہے۔ (۳) فالج پڑا ہوا ہو یا ہاتھ پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمعت انسا يقول قال رجل من الانصار اني لا استطيع الصلاة معک و كان رجلا ضخما فصنع للنبى طعاما فدعاه الى منزله فبسط له حصيرا و نضح طرف الحصير فصلى عليه
Section on what makes jama'ah drop. The attendance of jama'ah drops by one of eighteen things: (495) rain, cold, fear, darkness. Translation: (495) [1] rain - [2] severe cold - [3] fear - [4] severe darkness. Explanation: Heavy rain, or severe cold, or severe fear that if I go out the enemy will harm me or some important thing will be lost, or severe darkness, then there is allowance that he does not join the congregation and prays at home. Proof: (1) For rain and cold, this hadith: Indeed Ibn 'Umar gave the call to prayer on a night of cold and wind, then said: 'Pray in your dwellings.' Then said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to order the mu'adhdhin when there was a night of cold and rain to say: Pray in your dwellings.' (Bukhari, chapter on permission in rain and illness to pray in one's dwelling, p. 109 no. 666). This hadith says to pray at home in rain and intense cold. (2) From Ibn 'Abbas: He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever hears the caller and nothing prevents him from following him except an excuse...' They said: What is the excuse? He said: 'Fear or illness, the prayer he performed is not accepted.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on severity in leaving jama'ah, p. 91 no. 55). This hadith says that leaving jama'ah due to fear or illness is permissible. (496) and imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand and foot, and sickness. Translation: (496) [5] imprisoned [6] blind [7] paralyzed [8] amputated hands and feet, [9] sick. Explanation: If a person is imprisoned, he cannot come to jama'ah at all, so jama'ah drops for him. If blind, jama'ah drops. If paralyzed, he cannot come without support, and jama'ah is not obligatory with someone else's support, so jama'ah drops. The same for amputated hands and feet. Similarly, if a person is so sick that coming to jama'ah is difficult, then jama'ah drops; but if the illness is such that he can come easily, jama'ah does not drop. Proof: (1) For jama'ah dropping due to imprisonment, this hadith: Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) campaigned to Tabuk, and it was the campaign of hardship... Abu Lubaba was alarmed and tied himself to the pillar of repentance near the door of Umm Salamah, wife of the Prophet, for seven days and nights in severe heat, not eating or drinking a drop. (Dala'il al-Nubuwwa, chapter on hadith of Abu Lubaba, vol. 5 p. 270). In this hadith, Abu Lubaba imprisoned himself, so jama'ah dropped. (2) For blindness, this hadith: 'Itban ibn Malik, who was among the companions of the Prophet... came to the Messenger of Allah and said: O Messenger of Allah, my sight has weakened, and I lead my people in prayer, and when it rains, the valley between me and them floods, and I cannot come to their mosque to lead them, and I wish that you, O Messenger of Allah, would come and pray in a place I have taken as a prayer place.' (Muslim, chapter on permission to miss jama'ah due to an excuse, p. 256 no. 1496/65). This hadith says that if there is weakness in the eyes, one can leave jama'ah. It also says that if there is so much mud and water that one cannot go, there is allowance to leave jama'ah. (3) For paralysis or amputation, this hadith: I heard Anas say: A man from the Ansar said: I cannot pray with you, and he was a bulky man. So he made food for the Prophet and invited him to his home, spread a mat for him, sprinkled water on its edges, and prayed on it.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from Thamaratun Najah, an Urdu commentary on the Hanafi matn Nur al-Idah. It addresses the excuses that lift the obligation of attending congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah). The author lists eighteen reasons, though only the first nine are detailed here. The primary ruling is that jama'ah is a duty (wajib) for able men, but these excuses make it permissible to pray individually at home. The first four excuses (rain, severe cold, fear, darkness) are supported by two hadith: one from Ibn 'Umar showing the Prophet allowed praying at home due to cold/rain, and another from Ibn 'Abbas mentioning fear and illness as valid excuses. The next five excuses (imprisonment, blindness, paralysis, amputation, illness) are each supported by hadith or precedent. The pattern is that any condition preventing easy access to the mosque excuses jama'ah. Note the distinction: slight illness does not excuse, only one causing significant difficulty.

Key Terms
جماعة (jamā‘ah): Congregational prayer performed by two or more persons following an imam.
يسقط (yasquṭu): The obligation to attend falls or becomes non-obligatory.
وجه (wajh): Proof or evidence from hadith.
عذر (ʿudhr): A legitimate excuse that lifts a legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas cited in the passage, which two excuses are explicitly mentioned by the Prophet?
A) Rain and cold
B) Fear and illness
C) Blindness and paralysis
D) Imprisonment and darkness

Key Takeaway
Jama'ah is a heavy duty, but the Prophet ﷺ provided clear concessions for genuine hardship — know them to avoid sin and embrace mercy.

Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer
Listing and proving excuses that drop jama'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four excuses that drop the obligation of jama'ah and explain the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib, but genuine physical hardship excuses attendance.

In this passage, the author lists four specific excuses—inability to walk, deep mud, lameness, and extreme old age—that lift the wajib of attending jama'ah. The ruling is supported by the hadith of 'Itban ibn Malik, where the Prophet granted permission to stay home due to rain and mud, and the hadith of Anas regarding illness. Understanding these excuses helps differentiate between a genuine concession and negligence.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
Recognize that jama'ah is wajib for men in the Hanafi school. The passage then lists exceptions that drop this obligation.
2
List the four excuses
Identify the excuses: iqaad (inability to walk), wahal (mud), zamānah (lameness), shaykhūkha (extreme old age).
These are the only excuses explicitly mentioned in this matn.
3
Locate the primary proof
Find the hadith of 'Itban ibn Malik. The Prophet permitted him to pray at home due to the valley flooding, proving that mud and water make jama'ah non-obligatory.
The hadith is from Muslim, no. 1496/657.
4
Extract the operative cause (illa)
The common factor is genuine difficulty (haraj) in reaching the mosque. All listed excuses share this characteristic.
This is why old age and lameness are included by analogy.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
Understand that any condition that creates similar difficulty (e.g., severe illness, heavy rain turning streets into mud) also excuses attendance.
The text also cites the hadith of Anas for illness.

Chapter on what drops the obligation of congregational prayer. (497) One who is unable to walk, mud, lameness, and old age. (Bukhari, Chapter: Did the Imam pray with those present? p.109, no.670 / Muslim, Chapter: Permission to stay behind from congregation due to excuse, p.256, no.1496/657) In this hadith, permission is given for a constrained person to pray at home. (4) If there is illness, then this hadith: Anas said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) did not come out for three [days]; the prayer was established; Abu Bakr went forward... Then he said: O Prophet of Allah, [something about the curtain]; he raised it; when the face of the Prophet (peace be upon him) became visible, we had not seen a sight more amazing than the face of the Prophet (peace be upon him) when it became visible to us. The Prophet gestured with his hand to Abu Bakr to go forward, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) lowered the curtain, and he was not able to [see?] until he died. (Bukhari, Chapter: The people of knowledge and virtue are most entitled to lead, p.110, no.68) In this hadith, it is that if there is severe illness, do not attend the congregation. Translation: (497) [10] One who sits and cannot walk. [11] Mud. [12] Lameness. [13] Old age. Explanation: For one who is seated and cannot walk, congregational prayer is dropped. If there is so much mud that walking in it is difficult, congregational prayer is dropped; similarly, if there is water, similarly, if very old such that walking is difficult, then congregational prayer is dropped. Evidence: (1) If there is mud, congregational prayer is dropped; its proof is this hadith: 'Itban ibn Malik, who was among the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and was among those who witnessed Badr from the Ansar, came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: O Messenger of Allah, I have lost my eyesight, and I lead my people in prayer; when there is rain, the valley between me and them flows, and I cannot come to their mosque to lead them in prayer. I wish that you, O Messenger of Allah, would come and pray in a place that I may take as a place of prayer.' (Muslim, Chapter: Permission to stay behind from congregation due to excuse, p.256, no.1496/657) In this hadith, it is that if there is so much mud and water that one cannot come, then there is concession to leave the congregation. The remaining proof has already passed. Vocabulary: 'barad': cold, snowfall; 'habs': imprisonment; 'falaj': paralysis; 'suqam': illness; 'iqaad': derived from 'qa'ada', to sit, here meaning sitting such that one cannot walk; 'wahal': mud; 'zamānah': lameness; 'shaykhūkha': old age.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the obligation of congregational prayer (jama'ah) is lifted for individuals who have certain valid excuses. The excuses mentioned are: being unable to walk (iqaad), presence of deep mud (wahal), lameness (zamānah), and extreme old age (shaykhūkha). The author provides textual evidence from the hadith of 'Itban ibn Malik, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted him to pray at home due to rain and mud. Additionally, the hadith of Anas indicates that severe illness excuses one from attending. In the Hanafi school, jama'ah is considered a wajib obligation, but these excuses make it permissible to miss it without sin. The author also clarifies that if the excuse is genuine, the person still receives the reward of jama'ah (as will be mentioned later). The vocabulary section clarifies key terms.

Key Terms
اقعاد (iqaad): Being unable to walk; one who sits permanently due to a condition.
وحل (wahal): Deep mud that makes walking difficult.
زمانة (zamānah): Lameness; a chronic condition causing difficulty in walking.
شيخوخة (shaykhūkha): Extreme old age that prevents walking to the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is wajib, but genuine difficulty in reaching the mosque due to physical incapacity, mud, lameness, or extreme old age drops the obligation.

Excuse for Studying Important Fiqh During Congregation
Ruling: Study of an important irrecoverable fiqh issue excuses from jama'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which studying a fiqh issue with the congregation excuses one from jama'ah and apply them to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Preserving irreplaceable knowledge can excuse from jama'ah.

This lesson examines a specific concession in Hanafi fiqh: when a person is engaged in studying a critical fiqh issue with a teacher or group, and missing that study would mean losing that knowledge permanently, the obligation of congregational prayer is lifted. However, this is a narrow dispensation, not a blanket exemption for all study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, note that the act in question is the omission of congregational prayer (jama'ah) due to being engaged in fiqh study. The ruling is that jama'ah is dropped (saqit) under specific conditions.
Congregational prayer is normally wajib for men in the Hanafi school.
2
Extract the conditions
The passage gives two conditions for the excuse: (1) the fiqh issue being studied is 'important' (muhim), and (2) if one stops studying, it would be difficult or impossible to obtain that knowledge again. Both must be present.
The text uses 'khauf' (fear) of losing it, indicating a genuine risk.
3
Apply the negation
If either condition fails—the issue is not important, or the knowledge can be recovered later—then the excuse does not apply, and jama'ah remains obligatory.
This protects against frivolous excuses.
4
Consider the proof basis
The ruling is derived from the broader principle that necessity permits omission of a wajib. The preservation of beneficial knowledge is considered a valid necessity when it would otherwise be permanently lost.
The source does not cite a specific hadith but relies on Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٣٩٨) [١٤] جماعت کے ساتھ فقہ کی تکرار کر رہا ہو اور چھوڑ دینے سے اس کے فوت ہونے کا خطرہ۔ تشریح : جماعت کے ساتھ ایسے اہم مسئلے کی تکرار کر رہا ہو کہ اس کے فوت ہونے سے دوبارہ حاصل ہونا مشکل ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہوگی ، لیکن اگر مسئلہ اتنا اہم نہ ہو ، یا دوبارہ حاصل ہونے کی امید ہو تو جماعت ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔
Translation: (398) [14] He is repeating fiqh with the congregation and there is fear of losing it if left. Explanation: If one is repeating an important issue with the congregation such that if he leaves, it would be difficult to obtain again, then congregational prayer is dropped. But if the issue is not so important, or there is hope of obtaining it again, then congregational prayer is not dropped.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage addresses the excuse of being engaged in the study of a significant fiqh issue with the congregation. The ruling is that if the issue is critical and missing it would cause permanent loss (e.g., from a teacher who rarely teaches it), then it is permissible to miss the congregational prayer in order to complete the study. However, if the issue is of lesser importance or can be learned later, then one must attend the prayer. This shows that the Hanafi school balances religious obligations; preserving beneficial knowledge may take precedence over a communal obligation when necessary.

Key Terms
تكرار فقه (takrār fiqh): Repetition or study of a fiqh issue with the congregation (probably meaning with a teacher or group).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does studying fiqh with the congregation excuse one from jama'ah?

D) Never, because prayer takes precedence

Key Takeaway
The excuse from jama'ah for studying fiqh requires both importance of the subject and genuine irrecoverability of the learning opportunity.

Excuse for Missing Congregation: Presence of Food and Intense Hunger
Ruling with proof from hadith on eating before congregation when hungry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when intense hunger excuses one from congregational prayer and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Intense hunger that destroys khushu' makes it permissible to eat before prayer, even if it means missing congregation.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: you are about to pray Maghrib in congregation, but dinner is served and you are very hungry. Does the obligation of jama'ah still apply? The Hanafi school, based on clear prophetic instructions, gives precedence to eating first when hunger would prevent proper focus in prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the three hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling and exception
Congregational prayer (jama'ah) is normally wajib in the Hanafi school. Identify the default ruling and note the specific condition that lifts this obligation.
The condition is extreme hunger that would destroy khushu'.
2
State the exception condition precisely
The passage distinguishes between intense hunger that eliminates khushu' and milder hunger. Only the former excuses jama'ah. Understand the threshold.
Khushu' is mental focus and humility in prayer.
3
Examine the three hadith proofs
The author cites three hadith. The first two contain explicit commands to start with dinner before Maghrib prayer. The third shows the Prophet stopping to eat quickly when called to prayer. Analyze how each supports the ruling.
The hadith are from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Given a situation, decide whether the excuse applies based on hunger level. Practice distinguishing between extreme and non-extreme cases.
If you can still concentrate in prayer, the obligation remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٤٩٩) [١٥] کھانا موجود ہو اور دل بہت چاہتا ہو۔ تشریح : کھانا موجود ہو اور بھوک اتن لگی ہو کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے سے خشوع وخضوع ختم ہو جائے گا تو جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گی، اور اگر اتنی شدید بھوک نہیں ہے تو جماعت ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (١) عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الا الله قال اذا قدم العشاء فابدوبه قبل ان تصلوا صلاة المغرب و لا تعجلوا عن عشائكم - ( بخاری شریف، باب حضر الطعام وا قیمت الصلاة ، ص ١٠٩ نمبر ٦٧٢ مسلم شریف ، باب كراهية الصلاة بحضرة الطعام الخ ، ص ٢٢٦، نمبر ١٢٤٢٫٥٥٧) اس حديث میں ہے کہ سخت بھوک ہو اور کھانا حاضر ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ (٢) سمعت عائشة عن النبى الله الله انه قال اذا وضع العشاء و اقيمت الصلاة فابدوا بالعشاء - ( بخاری شریف، باب حضر الطعام واقیمت الصلاۃ ص ١٠٩ نمبر (٦٧) اس حديث میں ہے کہ سخت بھوک ہوا اور کھانا حاضر ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ (٣) عمر بن أمية ان اباه قال رأيت رسول الله له ياكل ذراعا يحتز منها فدعى الى الصلوة فقام فطرح السكين فصلى و لم يتوضا - ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا دعی الامام الى الصلاۃ و بیده ما یاکل ص ١١٠، نمبر ٦٧٥) اس حديث میں ہے کہ اگر ضرورت پوری ہو چکی ہو تو جماعت کے لئے جانا چاہئے۔
Translation: (499) [15] Food is present and the heart strongly desires it. Explanation: If food is present and one is so hungry that praying with the congregation would eliminate khushu' (humility), then congregational prayer is dropped. But if the hunger is not that severe, then congregational prayer is not dropped. Evidence: (1) Anas ibn Malik narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When dinner is served, start with it before you pray the Maghrib prayer, and do not rush from your dinner.' (Bukhari, Chapter: When food is present and the prayer is established, p.109, no.672; Muslim, Chapter: Dislike of prayer in the presence of food, etc., p.226, no.1242/557) In this hadith, it is that if there is severe hunger and food is present, then congregational prayer is dropped. (2) I heard 'Aisha from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'When dinner is placed and the prayer is established, start with dinner.' (Bukhari, Chapter: When food is present and the prayer is established, p.109, no.67) In this hadith, it is that if there is severe hunger and food is present, then congregational prayer is dropped. (3) 'Umar ibn Umayyah said that his father said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) eating a forearm, cutting from it; he was called to prayer, so he stood up, threw the knife, prayed, and did not perform ablution. (Bukhari, Chapter: When the Imam is called to prayer while there is something in his hand that he is eating, p.110, no.675) In this hadith, it is that if the need is fulfilled, then one should go to the congregation.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses the excuse of having food present and being intensely hungry. The ruling is that if hunger is so severe that one cannot focus in prayer (khushu'), then it is permissible to eat first and miss the congregation. The author provides three hadith proofs. The first two command eating before the Maghrib prayer when dinner is served, indicating that the prayer should not be performed while the mind is distracted by hunger. The third hadith shows that if one is already eating and the call to prayer is given, one may finish the meal quickly but should not delay excessively. In the Hanafi school, this is based on the principle that the prayer requires presence of heart; if hunger prevents that, it is better to eat first.

Key Terms
خشوع وخضوع (khushū' wa khudū'): Humility and submissiveness in prayer; the required state of concentration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray first, then eat quickly
B) Eat first, then pray
C) Perform both simultaneously
D) Skip dinner and pray

Key Takeaway
Extreme hunger that undermines concentration in prayer makes it permissible to eat before praying, even if it means missing the congregation.

Excuses for Missing Jama'ah: Travel, Nursing, and Wind
Ruling that preparing for travel, nursing the sick, and strong wind at night excuse from jama'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three excuses for missing jama'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Urgent travel preparation, essential nursing, and severe night wind exempt one from congregational prayer.

In the Hanafi school, attending jama'ah is wajib for men who are not excused. However, certain genuine necessities – such as imminent travel, caring for a sick person, or extreme weather – lift the obligation. This lesson examines these three excuses and the evidence from hadith.

Guided Path
1
List the three excuses
Identify the three scenarios mentioned: preparation for travel, nursing a sick person, and strong wind at night. Note that the wind is specified as at night and strong, not a light day breeze.
2
Understand the conditions for each excuse
For travel: the travel must be imminent and one is engaged in preparation. For nursing: one must be actively caring for a sick person, and the care must be essential. For wind: it must be strong and at night; a mild day wind does not excuse if one can still attend.
3
Examine the hadith evidence for nursing
The hadith from 'Aisha (Bukhari 664) describes the Prophet (peace be upon him) being supported by two men due to illness. This indicates that those who were busy caring for him were excused from congregation.
The hadith is cited as indirect evidence: the attendants of the Prophet were occupied with his care.
4
Derive the ruling
These excuses make it permissible to miss the wajib of jama'ah. The Hanafi school holds that the obligation is lifted due to genuine necessity, not that the act becomes invalid.
The ruling is a concession (rukhsah), not a license to ignore jama'ah without cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٥٠٠) [١٦] سفر کی تیاری۔ [١٧] مریض کی تیمارداری ۔ [١٨] شب میں سخت آندھی ہو نہ کہ دن میں ۔ تشریح : سفر بالکل سامنے ہو اور اس کی تیاری میں ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ یا بیمار پر یشان ہو اور آدمی اس کی تیمارداری کر رہا ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ رات میں آندھی ہو تو جماعت ساقط ہو جائے گی ، البتہ دن میں ہلکی پھلکی آندھی ہو اور جماعت میں شریک ہوسکتا ہو تو جماعت ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (١) مریض کی تیمارداری کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ كنا عند عائشة فذكرنا المواظبة على الصلاة و التعظيم لها..... فوجد النبي من نفسه خفة فخرج يهادى بين رجلين كاني انظر رجليه يخطان الارض من الوجع ( بخاری شریف ، باب حد المرض ان يشهد الجماعة ، ص ١٠٨، نمبر ٦٦٤) اس حديث میں ہے کہ دو آدمی حضور " کو لیجا رہے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو تیمار داری میں ہو اس کی جماعت ساقط ہوگی۔
Translation: (500) [16] Preparation for travel. [17] Nursing a sick person. [18] Strong wind at night, not during the day. Explanation: If travel is imminent and one is engaged in preparation, then congregational prayer is dropped. Or if one is anxious about a sick person and is nursing him, then congregational prayer is dropped. If there is wind at night, then congregational prayer is dropped. However, if there is a light wind during the day and one can still attend the congregation, then congregational prayer is not dropped. Evidence: (1) For nursing a sick person, the hadith is: We were with 'Aisha and we mentioned consistency in prayer and reverence for it... then the Prophet (peace be upon him) felt some lightness, so he went out walking between two men, as if I see his feet dragging on the ground from pain. (Bukhari, Chapter: The extent of illness for attending the congregation, p.108, no.664) In this hadith, it is that two men were taking the Prophet (peace be upon him), indicating that one who is engaged in nursing (i.e., the attendants) will have his congregation dropped.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage lists three additional excuses: being occupied with travel preparations, nursing a sick person, and a strong wind at night. The author specifies that the wind must be at night and severe; daytime wind of mild intensity does not excuse. The hadith evidence for nursing is from the incident where the Prophet (peace be upon him) was too ill to walk alone, suggesting that those who are busy caring for the sick are excused. Similarly, travel preparations that are urgent and cannot be delayed are a valid excuse. The Hanafi school considers these as genuine necessities that allow one to miss the congregation without sin.

Key Terms
تيمارداري (tīmārdārī): Nursing or caring for a sick person.
جماعت (jamā'at): Congregational prayer, specifically the five daily prayers in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Strong wind at night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes three specific excuses – travel preparation, nursing, and severe night wind – that lift the wajib of jama'ah.

Preservation of Reward for Missing Jama'ah Due to Valid Excuses
Conclusion ruling that valid excuses preserve reward

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a person who misses jama'ah due to a valid excuse still receives the full reward of congregation, and identify the underlying principle of intention and obstacle.

Core Idea
A valid excuse preserves the reward of jama'ah even when the action is missed.

In this brief concluding ruling, we learn an important mercy-based principle: when a genuine obstacle prevents a believer from attending congregational prayer, the reward is not lost. This teaching encourages community members to prioritize jama'ah while providing comfort for those with legitimate hardships. Let us examine the ruling and its conditions carefully.

Guided Path
1
Recall the valid excuses
Previously learned excuses such as inability to walk, deep mud, old age, presence of food, travel, nursing, etc.
These are from the earlier part of the chapter.
2
Confirm the excuse is genuine
The intention to attend jama'ah must be present, but a genuine obstacle prevents it.
Mere laziness or negligence does not count.
3
Apply the ruling
If the excuse is valid, the person still receives the full reward of jama'ah, as stated in the text.
This is based on mercy and intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Translation: (501) If due to these aforementioned permissible excuses the congregational prayer is missed, then he will still receive the reward of congregation.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This brief passage concludes the chapter by stating an important principle: when a person misses the congregational prayer due to any of the valid excuses listed earlier (inability to walk, mud, old age, food, travel, nursing, etc.), they are still entitled to the full reward of jama'ah. This is based on the mercy of Allah, as the intention and effort to attend are present, but a genuine obstacle prevents it. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the reward is not lost due to the excuse.

Key Takeaway

Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer
Lists excuses exempting from jama'ah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the excuses that drop wajib jama'ah, state the condition for each, and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Valid excuses drop wajib of jama'ah but still earn its reward.

Congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a strong obligation (wajib) for men in the Hanafi school. However, Islam recognizes human necessities. This passage from classical fiqh enumerates specific excuses that make it permissible to miss jama'ah without sin. Study these excuses carefully—they are not loopholes but mercy from Allah.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling on jama'ah
In Hanafi fiqh, jama'ah for the five daily prayers is wajib for men. Know this baseline.
Wajib is less than fard but still obligatory.
2
List the valid excuses from the text
The passage mentions: (1) craving for food with severe hunger and food present; (2) preparation for imminent travel; (3) nursing a sick patient; (4) severe wind at night.
The wind excuse is only at night, not daytime.
3
Identify the condition for each excuse
Hunger must be severe, travel must be imminent, nursing must be active, wind must be severe and at night. Light wind or minor hunger does not excuse.
The text explicitly differentiates day and night wind.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The Prophet (saw) commanded eating dinner before Maghrib prayer when food is served, indicating precedence of necessity. The hadith on nursing shows the Prophet himself was supported due to illness, implying permission for caregivers.
These ahadith are from Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Note the reward for missing jama'ah with excuse
The passage says one who misses jama'ah due to a valid excuse still receives the full reward of congregational prayer.
This encourages attending when possible, but relieves when unable.

Chapter on what drops congregational prayer. (500) Himself craving, and intention of travel, and standing to nurse a patient, and severe wind at night not daytime. (501) And if one misses congregational prayer due to a valid excuse from its permitted reasons, he receives its reward. Evidence: (1) From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When dinner is presented, begin with it before you pray Maghrib, and do not rush from your dinner.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith indicates that when there is severe hunger and food is present, congregational prayer is dropped. (2) I heard Aisha from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'When dinner is served and the prayer is established, begin with dinner.' (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that when there is severe hunger and food is present, congregational prayer is dropped. (3) Umar ibn Umayyah that his father said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) eating a shoulder, cutting from it, then he was called to prayer, so he stood up, threw the knife, prayed, and did not perform wudu.' (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that if the need has been fulfilled, he should go for congregational prayer. Translation: (500) [16] Preparing for travel. [17] Nursing a patient. [18] Severe wind at night, not daytime. Explanation: If travel is imminent and one is preparing, congregational prayer is dropped. Or if one is anxious about a patient and is nursing him, congregational prayer is dropped. If there is wind at night, congregational prayer is dropped; however, if during the day there is a light wind and he can attend congregational prayer, it is not dropped. Evidence: (1) For nursing a patient, this hadith: 'We were with Aisha and we mentioned persevering in prayer and revering it... Then the Prophet found some lightness from himself and went out, supported between two men, as if I saw his feet dragging on the ground from pain' (Bukhari). This hadith indicates that two men were taking the Prophet, showing that one who is nursing his congregational prayer is dropped. Translation: (501) If due to these mentioned valid excuses, the congregational prayer is missed, he still receives its reward.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. It lists three valid excuses that drop the obligation of congregational prayer (jama'ah). The excuses are: (1) craving within oneself (intense hunger) such that food is present; (2) intending travel and being in the midst of preparation; (3) nursing a sick person; (4) severe wind at night (not daytime, as daytime wind is not an excuse). The author then provides textual evidence. For the first two, hadith from Anas and Aisha show that if dinner is served and one is hungry, one should eat first, thus missing jama'ah is permitted. For nursing, a hadith from Aisha describes the Prophet being supported due to illness, implying that nursing a patient can excuse one. The passage also notes that even if jama'ah is missed for a valid excuse, the person still receives the reward of jama'ah. The commentary clarifies that the exemption is only for severe hunger, imminent travel, or severe night wind; light daytime wind does not excuse.

Key Terms
جماعة (jamā‘ah): Congregational prayer performed in a group, which in Hanafi fiqh is wajib for men.
ساقط (sāqiṭ): Dropped, meaning the obligation of jama'ah is no longer required due to a valid excuse.
عذر (‘udhr): A legitimate excuse that permits one to miss a religious obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Hanafi Hierarchy for Choosing an Imam
Ruling on the hierarchy of imamah qualifications with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of those most entitled to lead congregational prayer and apply it to a congregation scenario.

Core Idea
Knowledge of fiqh takes precedence over recitation in choosing an imam.

Choosing the most qualified imam is a stressed sunnah, but the prayer remains valid even if a less qualified person leads. The Hanafi school has a detailed hierarchy starting with the householder, appointed imam, and ruler, then the most knowledgeable in fiqh, followed by recitation, piety, age, and other qualities. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exceptions to the default hierarchy
Before the general criteria, the text establishes that a householder, an appointed imam, and a ruler are more entitled to lead than others. Recognize these as overriding priorities.
The hadith 'la tu'ammanna rajulan fi ahlihi' is the basis for the householder's priority.
2
State the primary criterion after exceptions: knowledge (fiqh)
When none of the three exceptions are present, the most knowledgeable in fiqh is the most entitled. This is the key Hanafi position that distinguishes it from other schools.
Knowledge here means understanding of Islamic rulings (al-‘ālim).
3
Sequence the secondary criteria
After knowledge, the priority goes to: best reciter, most pious, oldest, best character, most handsome, noblest lineage, best voice, cleanest clothes. Each applies only when the previous criterion is equal.
This sequence is derived from the hadith and practice of the Companions.
4
Examine the key hadith proofs
The text cites several hadith, including the famous one from Abu Mas‘ud al-Ansari. Focus on how each hadith establishes a specific priority, especially the one that places fafqah (understanding) above qirā’ah.
The hadith from ‘Uqbah ibn ‘Amr explicitly says: '…then the most learned in religion… then the most versed in the Quran.'
5
Contrast with the Shāfi‘ī position
The Shāfi‘ī school prioritizes recitation (qirā’ah) over knowledge (fiqh). Understand the practical difference: in a choice between a scholar and a hafiz, the Hanafi would choose the scholar, the Shāfi‘ī would choose the hafiz.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf; both positions have their proofs.

ترجمه : (۵۰۳) پھر زیادہ اچھی طرح قرآن پڑھنے والا ، پھر زیادہ عمر والا ، پھر زیادہ اچھے اخلاق والا ، پھر زیادہ اچھی صورت والا، پھر زیادہ شریف نسل والا، پھر زیادہ اچھی آواز والا، پھر زیادہ پاکیزہ کپڑے والا مستحق ہوگا۔
تشريح : اگر مجلس میں سب مسئلے کے جاننے کے اعتبار سے برابر ہوں تو پھر زیادہ حقدار اچھا قرآن پڑھنے والا ہے، وہ بھی سب برابر درجے کا ہو تو جو زیادہ عمر والا ہو وہ حقدار ہے۔ لیکن عمر کے اعتبار سب برابر ہوں تو جو زیادہ اچھے اخلاق والا ہو وہ حقدار ہے۔ اخلاق میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جو زیادہ خوبصورت ہو وہ حقدار ہے، اور اس میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جو نسب کے اعتبار سے زیادہ شریف ہوں اس کا حق ہے۔ اور اس میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جسکی آواز اچھی ہو اس کا حق ہے ، اور اس میں بھی سبھی برابر ہوں تو [؟]
Section on the most entitled to imamah and arrangement of rows. (502) When among those present there is no owner of the house nor an appointed imam nor a person of authority, then the most knowledgeable is most entitled. Section: About who is most entitled to imamah and arrangement of rows. Translation: (502) When among the attendees there is no householder, appointed imam, or ruler, then the most deserving of imamah is the one most knowledgeable of issues. Explanation: If someone is in a house and among the household there is someone qualified for imamah, that person is more entitled, unless he permits another to lead. Or if it is a mosque and there is an appointed imam, he is more entitled. Or if there is a high-ranking government official who is qualified, he has the right. But if none of these are present, the most entitled is the one most knowledgeable of issues. Proofs: (1) The householder is more entitled, the evidence is this hadith: from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The one most versed in the Book of Allah should lead the people. If they are equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. If they are equal in the Sunnah, then the one who emigrated first. And in another hadith: If they are equal in emigration, then the oldest in age. And a man should not lead in another's house nor in his dominion, nor sit on his seat of honor unless he permits you or with his permission.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Imamah, p.271; Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Imamah, p.94) This hadith indicates that a man should not lead prayer in another's house, meaning the householder is more entitled. Also, 'nor in his dominion' means the ruler is more entitled. (2) From the practice of a Companion: Abu Sa'id prepared food and invited Abu Dharr, Hudhayfah, and Ibn Mas'ud. When prayer time came, Abu Dharr stepped forward to lead them. Abu Hudhayfah said to him, 'Go back, the owner of the house is more entitled to lead.' Abu Dharr asked Ibn Mas'ud, 'Is that so?' He said yes, so Abu Dharr stepped back. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab al-Rajul ya'ti fi rib'ihi, vol.2, p.260, no.3829) This athar shows the householder is more entitled. (3) From Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah said to us, 'Your brother an-Najashi has died, so stand and pray over him.' We stood and lined up as they line up for the deceased and prayed over him as they pray over the deceased. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi salat al-nabi 'ala al-Najashi, p.201; Bukhari, Bab al-salat 'ala al-jana'iz bil-musalla wal-masjid, p.177) The Prophet was the leader of all, so he led the prayer. (4) The governor and ruler are more entitled to lead prayer, evidence is this athar: I heard Abu Hazim say: I was present on the day al-Hasan ibn 'Ali died, and I saw al-Husayn ibn 'Ali saying to Sa'id ibn al-'As, while poking his neck, 'Step forward, were it not that it is a sunnah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala al-wali ahaqq bi-salat 'ala al-mayyit min al-waly, vol.4, p.46; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab man ahaqq bi-salat 'ala al-mayyit, vol.3, p.302) In this athar, al-Husayn was the guardian of al-Hasan, but he made Sa'id ibn al-'As lead the funeral prayer because he was the governor. al-Husayn said it is sunnah, so the governor and ruler are more entitled than the guardian. (5) The appointed imam is more entitled, evidence is this saying of a Companion: from 'Ali: The imam is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer. I went with Ibrahim to a funeral, and he was the guardian, so he sent word to the imam of the district who led the prayer. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol.2, p.283; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, vol.3, p.302) This athar shows that the mosque imam is entitled. (6) The one more knowledgeable of the Sunnah is entitled, evidence is this hadith: from Abu Musa: The Prophet fell ill and his illness worsened, so he said, 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' (Bukhari, Bab ahl al-'ilm wal-fadl ahaqq bil-imamah, p.110; Muslim, Bab istikhlaf al-imam idha 'arada lahu 'udhr, p.177) (7) From Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Let those of you who are possessors of understanding and wisdom be close to me, then those next to them, then those next to them.' (Muslim, Bab taswiyat al-sufuf, p.184; Abu Dawud, Bab man yastahibbu an yali al-imam fi al-saff, p.105) This hadith indicates that the intelligent should be near the imam to assist him when needed; it does not say the reciter should be near. (8) From 'Uqbah ibn 'Amr: The Messenger of Allah said, 'The imam of the people is the one who emigrated first. If they are equal in emigration, then the most learned in religion. If they are equal in religion, then the one most versed in the Quran.' (Darqutni, Bab man ahaqq bil-imamah, vol.1, p.284; Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab al-salat, vol.1, p.370) This gives priority to fiqh over recitation. Nevertheless, if someone less virtuous leads, the prayer is valid. Translation: (503) Then the one who recites the Quran best, then the more pious, then the older, then the better in character, then the better in appearance, then the nobler in lineage, then the better in voice, then the cleaner in clothes. Explanation: If in the gathering all are equal in knowledge of issues, then the more entitled is the one who recites Quran better. If they are equal in recitation, then the older. If equal in age, then the better in character. If equal in character, then the more handsome. If equal in appearance, then the nobler in lineage. If equal in lineage, then the better in voice. If equal in voice, then the cleaner in clothes.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs on the hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead prayer (imamah). The text begins by stating the ruling: when there is no householder, appointed imam, or ruler present, the most knowledgeable in fiqh is the most entitled. Then it provides a detailed explanation and eight proofs from hadith and athar. The proofs establish priority for: householder, ruler, appointed imam, and the most knowledgeable. The text emphasizes that knowledge (fiqh) takes precedence over recitation, as seen in hadith 8. The second part (503) gives the order after knowledge: recitation, piety, age, character, appearance, lineage, voice, and cleanliness. This order applies when the previous qualifications are equal. The commentary notes that if a less qualified person leads, the prayer is still valid.

Key Terms
الأحق بالإمامة (al-aḥaqq bil-imāmah): The person most entitled to lead the congregational prayer based on a hierarchy of qualifications.
الاعلم (al-a‘lam): The one most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer and other Islamic issues (fiqh).
الاقرأ (al-aqra’): The one who recites the Quran best in terms of tajweed and memorization.
الاورع (al-awra‘): The one who is most pious and cautious in avoiding sins and doubtful matters.
الاسن (al-asann): The oldest in age.
ذو سلطان (dhū sulṭān): A person in authority, such as a ruler, governor, or official.
صاحب منزل (ṣāḥib manzil): The owner or primary resident of a house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the rule if a person who is not the most qualified leads the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but it is disliked (makruh) to avoid the sunnah.
C) The prayer is valid and there is no problem.
D) The prayer is null unless the most qualified person permits.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes fiqh knowledge over recitation in imamah, but the hierarchy is a stressed sunnah, not a condition of validity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Order of Precedence for Leading Prayer
Establishes hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead prayer and explain the primary evidence for each level.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command to let the most learned lead: knowledge of Quran and Sunnah trumps age and piety.

When a congregation gathers for prayer, who should lead? This is not just a matter of convenience; the Prophet (ﷺ) established a specific order of precedence based on knowledge and merit. The Hanafi school has codified this hierarchy, supported by multiple hadith and the practice of the Companions. This lesson unpacks that hierarchy and the evidence behind each criterion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary criteria
List the qualities mentioned in the matn: al-afqah (most knowledgeable), al-aqra' (best reciter), al-awra' (most pious), al-acem (oldest), etc.
The matn begins with the ruler/leader, then the mosque imam, then the list.
2
Understand the hierarchy
Note that the state ruler (sultan) is most entitled, then the mosque imam, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah (al-afqah), then the best reciter, then the most pious, then the eldest, and so on.
The hierarchy is a recommendation, not a requirement for validity.
3
Examine the key hadith
Study the hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: 'The one who recites the Book of Allah most should lead... if equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah... if equal, then the earliest in hijrah... if equal, then the oldest.'
This hadith is the primary proof for the order.
4
Reconcile apparent contradictions
Some hadith prioritize recitation (e.g., 'Amr ibn Salama), others prioritize age (e.g., Malik ibn al-Huwayrith). The Hanafi school reconciles by placing knowledge of the Sunnah above recitation, based on the hadith of Abu Bakr's appointment and the hadith from 'Uqba ibn 'Amr.
The order is: knowledge of Sunnah > recitation > piety > age > etc.
5
Apply the ruling
Recognize that if a less-preferred person leads, the prayer is valid (sahih). The hierarchy is a sunnah muakkadah, not a condition of validity.
The passage explicitly states: 'تاہم کسی غیر افضل نے امامت کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی' (if a less virtuous one leads, the prayer is valid).

بالصلوۃ علی لمبیت من الولی ، ج رابع ص ۴۶ نمبر۶۸۹۴ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من أحق بالصلوۃ علی المیت، ج ثالث ، ص ۳۰۲ نمبر ۶۳۹۶) اس اثر میں حضرت حسینؓ حضرت حسنؓ کے ولی تھے۔ لیکن سعید بن عاص کو نماز جنازہ کے مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب من أحق بالصلوۃ علی المیت ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۰۲، نمبر ۶۳۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسجد کا امام نماز کا حقدار ہے۔ (۶) سنت کو زیادہ جاننے والا امامت کا حقدار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی موسی قال مرض النبي فاشتد مـرضـه فـقـال مـروا ابا بكر فليصل بالناس - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اہل العلم والفضل احق بالامامة ص ۱۱۰ نمبر ۶۷۸ مسلم شریف، باب استخلاف الامام اذا عرض لہ عذر ص ۱۷۷، نمبر ۹۳۶/۴۱۸) (۶) عن ابن مسعود قال قال رسول الله لـيـلـنـي مـنـكـم اولوا الاحلام والنهى ثم الذين يلونهم ثلاثا (مسلم شریف ، باب تسویۃ الصفوف واقامتها فضل الاول فالاول، ص ۱۸۴، نمبر ۱۷۹۷۴/۴۳۲ بود او د شریف ، حضور کے قریب ہونا چاہیئے (۸) حدیث میں ہے عن عقبة بن عمرو قال قال رسول الله له يوم الناس اقدمهم هجرة وان كانوا فى الهجرة سواء فافقههم فى الدين وان كانوا في الدين سواء فاقرؤهم للقرآن ( دار قطنی ، باب من احق بالا مامته ، ج اول ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۰۷۲ مستدرک للحاکم، کتاب الصلوۃ، ج اول ص۳۷۰، نمبر ۸۸۶) اس میں بھی افتقہ کو زیادہ حق امامت دیا گیا ہے۔ ۔ تاہم کسی غیر افضل نے امامت کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ ترجمه : (۵۰۳) پھر زیادہ اچھی طرح قرآن پڑھنے والا ، پھر زیادہ عمر والا ، پھر زیادہ اچھے اخلاق والا ، پھر زیادہ اچھی صورت والا، پھر زیادہ شریف نسل والا، پھر زیادہ اچھی آواز والا، پھر زیادہ پاکیزہ کپڑے والا مستحق ہوگا۔ تشريح : اگر مجلس میں سب مسئلے کے جاننے کے اعتبار سے برابر ہوں تو پھر زیادہ حقدار اچھا قرآن پڑھنے والا ہے، وہ بھی سب برابر درجے کا ہو تو جو زیادہ عمر والا ہو وہ حقدار ہے۔ لیکن عمر کے اعتبار سب برابر ہوں تو جو زیادہ اچھے اخلاق والا ہو وہ حقدار ہے۔ اخلاق میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جو زیادہ خوبصورت ہو وہ حقدار ہے، اور اس میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جو نسب کے اعتبار سے زیادہ شریف ہوں اس کا حق ہے۔ اور اس میں بھی سب برابر ہوں تو جسکی آواز اچھی ہو اس کا حق ہے ، اور اس میں بھی سبھی برابر ہوں تو ثمرة النجاح جلد ا ۳۳۷ فصل في الاحق بالامامة الاحسن صوتا ثم الانظف ثوبا (۵۰۴) فان استووا يقرع او الخيار للقوم فان اختلفوا فالعبرة بما کپڑے کے اعتبار سے عمدہ ہو اس کا حق ہے، انتخاب کرنے میں یہ ترتیب ہے کیونکہ اس سے نمازیوں کے دلوں میں اہمیت ہوتی ہے وجه : (۱) گھر والا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی مسعود الانصاري قال قال رسول الله الله يؤم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله فان كانوا في القراءة سواء فاعلمهم بالسنة فان كانوا في السنة سواء فاقدمهم هجرة. وفي حديث آخر فان كانوا فى الهجرة سواء فليؤمهم مامته ، ص۹۴ نمبر ۵۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قاری کو زیادہ حق ہے لیکن دوسری حدیث سے ثابت کیا کہ اعلم بالسنہ کو زیادہ حق ہے اس لئے اس کے بعد قاری امامت کا زیادہ حقدار ہوگا ۔ پھر زیادہ عمر والا ۔(۲)حدیث میں
