داود شریف ، باب من احق بالا مامته ، ص ۹۴ نمبر (۵۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جسکو قرآن زیادہ آتا ہو اسکو امامت کا زیادہ حق ہے ۔(۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پر ہیز گار زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ عن مرثد بن ابی مرثد الغنوى و كان بدريا قال : قال رسول الله الله : ان سركم أن تقبل صلوتكم فليوء مكم خياركم فانهم وفدكم فيما بينكم و بين ربكم عزوجل - ( مستدرک للحاکم ، ذکر مناقب مرثد بن ابی مرثد الغنوی ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۴۶، نمبر ۴۹۸۱ رسنن بیھقی ، باب اجعلو المتکم خیارکم ، ج ثالث ص ۱۲۹، نمبر ۵۱۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اپنے میں سے اچھے لوگ کو امام بناؤ تو نماز قبول ہوگی۔ (۴) عن مالک بن الحويرث قال قدمنا على النبي عل ... قال ... فاذا حضرت الصلوة فليؤذن لكم احدكم وليؤمكم اكبركم ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا استووا فی القراءة فليو مهم اكبرهم، ص۹۴، نمبر ۶۸۵ / مسلم شریف ، باب من احق بالا مامته ،ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۱۵۳۵/۶۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کبھی ہجرت اور قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو عمر کے اعتبار سے جو زیادہ ہو اس کو امامت کا حق ہے۔(۵) عن ابی مسعود الانصارى يقول قال لنا رسول الله عله : يؤم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله و أقدمهم قرأة فان كانت قرأتهم سواءً فليوء مهم أقدمهم هجرة فان كانوا في الهجرة سواءً فليوء مهم أكبرهم سناً (مسلم شریف ، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۵۳۴/۶۷۳ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ۹۴ نمبر ۵۸۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سب میں برابر ہوں تو جو عمر میں بڑے ہوں وہ امامت کا حقدار ہیں۔ (1) اچھی آواز والے کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس قال قال رسول الله لا لا لا اله لكل شيء حلية وحلية القرآن الصوت الحسن ۔ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب صوت الحسن ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۹ نمبر ۴۱۸۴)
Chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer. (503) Then the best Quran reciter, then the most pious, then the eldest, then the best in character, then the best in appearance, then the noblest in lineage, then the one with the best voice, then the one with the cleanest clothes. And if there is something between them (a dispute) – (Reference to athar: The ruler is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer than the guardian. In this athar, Husayn was the guardian of Hasan, but they put forward Sa'id ibn al-'As because he was the ruler and commander. Husayn said this is the Sunnah, so the ruler and commander are more entitled to lead prayer than the guardian.) (5) The mosque imam is more entitled. Its proof is the saying of the companion: 'Ali said: The imam is more entitled to lead the funeral prayer. I went with Ibrahim to a funeral and he was its guardian, but he sent to the imam of the neighbourhood who led it. (References) From this it is known that the imam of the mosque is entitled to lead the prayer. (6) The one more knowledgeable in the Sunnah is entitled to imamah. Its proof is this hadith: Abu Musa said: The Prophet fell ill and his illness worsened. He said: Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer. (Bukhari and Muslim) (6) Ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah said: Let those who are possessors of wisdom and understanding stand nearest to me, then those who follow them – three times. (Muslim) From this hadith it is known that the intelligent and wise should be near the imam so that they can take over imamah when needed. It does not say that the reciter should be near him. (8) In a hadith: 'Uqba ibn 'Amr said: The Messenger of Allah said: The people should be led by the one who is earliest in hijrah, and if they are equal in hijrah, then the most knowledgeable in the religion, and if they are equal in religion, then the one with the most Quran recitation. (Darqutni and Hakim) In this also, knowledge is given more right to imamah. However, if a less virtuous one leads, the prayer is valid. Translation: (503) Then the one who recites the Quran better, then the older, then the better in character, then the better in appearance, then the nobler in lineage, then the better in voice, then the one with cleaner clothes is more entitled. Explanation: If the assembly is equal in knowledge of the issue, then the better Quran reciter is more entitled. If they are equal in that, then the older is entitled. If equal in age, then the better in character. If equal in character, then the better looking. If equal in that, then the nobler in lineage. If equal in that, then the better voiced. If equal in that, then the one with cleaner clothes is more entitled. If they are equal in all, then lots are drawn or the people choose. If they differ, then the consideration is based on what? (504) Then the better in voice, then the cleaner in clothes. If they are equal, lots are drawn or the choice is for the people. If they differ, then the consideration is based on what? The face (reason): (1) The head of household is more entitled. Its proof is this hadith: Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari said: The Messenger of Allah said: The one who recites the Book of Allah most should lead the people. If they are equal in recitation, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. If they are equal in knowledge of the Sunnah, then the one earliest in hijrah. In another hadith: If they are equal in hijrah, then the oldest among them should lead them. And do not lead a man in his own household or in his authority, and do not sit on his seat of honour in his house unless he gives you permission or by his leave. (Muslim and Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that the reciter has more right, but another hadith establishes that the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah has more right. Therefore, after him, the reciter is more entitled to imamah, then the older. (2) Hadith: 'Amr ibn Salama said: ... when the prayer time comes, let one of you give the adhan and let the one who has most Quran lead you. (Bukhari and Abu Dawud) This hadith says that the one with more Quran has more right to imamah. (3) This hadith says that the pious is better. Murshid ibn Abi Murshid al-Ghanawi, who was a Badri, said: The Messenger of Allah said: If you wish your prayer to be accepted, let your best ones lead you, for they are your representatives between you and your Lord. (Hakim and Bayhaqi) This hadith says: Make your best ones your imam, then the prayer will be accepted. (4) Malik ibn al-Huwayrith said: We came to the Prophet ... He said: ... When the prayer time comes, let one of you give the adhan and let the oldest lead you. (Bukhari and Muslim) From this hadith it is known that if they are equal in hijrah and recitation, then the older has the right to imamah. (5) Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari said: The Messenger of Allah said to us: The one who recites the Book of Allah most should lead the people, and the one with the most advanced recitation. If their recitation is equal, then the one earliest in hijrah; if they are equal in hijrah, then the oldest. (Muslim and Abu Dawud) This hadith states that if all are equal, then the oldest is entitled to imamah. (1) The one with the good voice is given preference. For this, there is this hadith: Anas said: The Messenger of Allah said: Everything has an adornment, and the adornment of the Quran is the beautiful voice. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm ma'a al-dalil) establishing the hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead prayer (imamah) in the Hanafi school. The author first presents a concise list (matn) of the order of precedence: after the ruler/leader, the next most entitled is the best Quran reciter, then the most pious, then the eldest, then the best in character, then the best in appearance, then the noblest in lineage, then the best in voice, then the cleanest in clothing. If all are equal, lots are drawn or the congregation chooses. The author then provides detailed proofs from hadith and athar (sayings of the Companions) to support each aspect of this hierarchy. Key points: (1) The ruler (wali/amir) is most entitled to lead funeral prayer, as evidenced by the practice of Husayn ibn Ali deferring to the governor Sa'id ibn al-'As. (2) The mosque imam is more entitled than the guardian of the deceased based on a saying of Ali. (3) Knowledge of the Sunnah takes precedence over Quranic recitation, as demonstrated by the Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr. (4) The hadith from 'Uqba ibn 'Amr places fiqh (understanding) before recitation. (5) The hadith from Abu Mas'ud and others emphasize the order: knowledge of Quran, then Sunnah, then hijrah, then age. (6) Beautiful voice is a desirable quality based on a hadith. The passage also notes that if a less virtuous person leads, the prayer is valid—it is a recommendation (sunnah), not an obligation.

Key Terms
الاقرأ (al-aqra'): The one who has the best Quran recitation, meaning most correct and fluent.
الاورع (al-awra'): The most pious and God-fearing, one who avoids doubtful matters.
الامامة (al-imamah): Leadership of prayer, specifically standing in front of the congregation to lead them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi hierarchy presented in the passage, who should lead prayer if the most knowledgeable person (al-afqah) is absent?
A) The best reciter (al-aqra')
B) The most pious (al-awra')
C) The oldest
D) The best in character

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the imamah should be given to the most learned in Islamic knowledge, then to the best reciter, then to piety, age, and other qualities, but the prayer remains valid even if a less preferred person leads.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Priority Order for Leading Prayer (Imamah)
Rulings on priority of imam and procedure when equal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of qualifications for the imam and explain the procedure when candidates are equal in merit.

Core Idea
Imam chosen by best voice then cleanest clothes; if equal, lots or congregation decides.

This passage establishes a clear priority for selecting the imam in congregational prayer. The Prophet (peace be upon him) provided a hierarchy based on Quranic recitation, knowledge of Sunnah, precedence in hijrah, and age. The Hanafi school adds considerations of voice and cleanliness. When candidates are equal, the congregation may choose or cast lots, and the majority opinion prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first two qualifications
The text states: the one with the best voice, then the one with the cleanest clothes. These are additional qualities beyond the basic criteria from hadith.
Voice and cleanliness are part of Hanafi preference, not found in the main hadith.
2
Explain the procedure when equal
If candidates are equal in all merits, lots are cast or the congregation chooses. If the congregation disagrees, the majority opinion is followed.
Lots are a valid method in Hanafi law for resolving equal claims, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice with his wives.
3
Note the ruling if a less deserving is appointed
The text says 'they have done wrong' (sa'u) but the prayer remains valid. This means it is not sinful but it is blameworthy.
This indicates the preference is recommended (sunnah) not obligatory.
4
Relate the key hadith proofs
The hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari gives the hierarchy: most Quranic, then most knowledgeable of Sunnah, then earliest in hijrah, then oldest. Other hadith emphasize the best and most pious.
The Hanafi combination of these hadith yields the stated order.

فصل في الاحق بالامامة الاحسن صوتا ثم الانظف ثوبا (٥٠٤) فان استووا يقرع او الخيار للقوم فان اختلفوا فالعبرة بما اختاره الاكثر (٥٠٥) وان قدموا غير الاولى فقد اساءوا (٥٠٦) وكره امامة العبد والاعمى والدهقان وولد الزنا اذا كان جاهلا والفاسق والمبتدع. وجه : (١) عن ابي مسعود الانصاري قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: يؤم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله فان كانوا في القراءة سواء فاعلمهم بالسنة فان كانوا في السنة سواء فاقدمهم هجرة. وفي حديث آخر فان كانوا فى الهجرة سواء فليؤمهم اكبرهم سنا و لا تؤمن الرجل في اهله و لا في سلطانه و لا تجلس على تكرمته في بيته الا ان يأذن لك او باذنه. (مسلم شريف، باب من احق بالا مامتہ، ص ٢٧١، نمبر ١٥٣٤/١٥٣٢/٦٧٣ ابو داؤد شريف، باب من احق بالا مامته، ص٩٤ نمبر ٥٨٤) اس حديث میں ہے کہ قاری کو زیادہ حق ہے لیکن دوسری حديث سے ثابت کیا أن اعلم بالسنہ کو زیادہ حق ہے اس لئے اس کے بعد قاری امامت کا زیادہ حقدار ہوگا۔ پھر زیادہ عمر والا۔ (٢) حديث میں ہے۔ عن عمرو بن سلمة قال: لي أبو قلابة ..... فاذا حضرت الصلوة فليؤذن احدكم و ليؤمكم اكثركم قرآنا - (بخاری شريف، باب [باب مقام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بمكة زمن الفتح ص ٧٢٨ نمبر ٢٤٣٠ ابو داود شريف، باب من احق بالا مامته، ص ٩٤ نمبر ٥٨٥) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جسکو قرآن زیادہ آتا ہو اسکو امامت کا زیادہ حق ہے۔ (٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پرہیز گار زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ عن مرثد بن ابی مرثد الغنوى و كان بدريا قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ان سركم أن تقبل صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم فانهم وفدكم فيما بينكم و بين ربكم عزوجل - (مستدرک للحاکم، ذکر مناقب مرثد بن أبی مرثد الغنوی، ج ثالث، ص ٢٤٦، نمبر ٤٩٨١ سنن بیھقی، باب اجعلوا ائمتکم خیارکم، ج ثالث ص ١٢٩، نمبر ٥١٣٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اپنے میں سے اچھے لوگوں کو امام بناؤ تو نماز قبول ہوگی۔ (٤) عن مالک بن الحويرث قال قدمنا على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ... قال ... فاذا حضرت الصلوة فليؤذن لكم احدكم وليؤمكم اكبركم (بخاری شریف، باب اذا استووا فی القراءة فليؤمهم اكبرهم، ص٩٤، نمبر ٦٨٥ / مسلم شریف، باب من احق بالا مامته، ص ٢٣٧، نمبر ١٥٣٥/٦٧٤) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کبھی ہجرت اور قرأت میں برابر ہوں تو عمر کے اعتبار سے جو زیادہ ہو اس کو امامت کا حق ہے۔ (٥) عن ابی مسعود الانصارى يقول قال لنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يؤم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله و أقدمهم قرأة فان كانت قرأتهم سواءً فليؤمهم أقدمهم هجرة فان كانوا في الهجرة سواءً فليؤمهم أكبرهم سناً (مسلم شريف، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ٢٣٦ نمبر ١٥٣٤/٦٧٣ / ابو داؤد شريف، باب من احق بالا مامته ص ٩٤ نمبر ٥٨٢) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سب میں برابر ہوں تو جو عمر میں بڑے ہوں وہ امامت کا حقدار ہیں۔ (٦) اچھی آواز والے کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن أنس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لكل شيء حلية و حلية القرآن الصوت الحسن. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صوت الحسن، ج ثانی ص ١٣١٩ نمبر ٤١٨٤) (٥٠٤) اگر سب برابر درجہ والے ہوں تو قرعہ ڈالے، یا قوم جسے اختیار کرے۔ اگر آپس میں اختلاف ہو تو کثرت رائے کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ وجه: مشکل کام میں قرعہ ڈالے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أراد سفرا أقرع بين نسائه فأيتهن خرج سهمها خرج بها معه - (بخاری شریف، باب القرعة في المشکلات، ص ٤٣٨، نمبر ٢٦٨٨) (٥٠٥) اگر غیر اولی آدمی کو مقدم کیا تو اچھا نہیں کیا۔ تشریح: اگر غیر اولی کو امام بنا دیا تو نماز ہو جائے گی اس میں کوئی کراہیت نہیں ہے، البتہ اچھا نہیں کیا، کیونکہ حقدار کو حق نہیں دیا (٥٠٦) اور غلام اور نابینا اور دہقانی اور ولد زنا جو جاہل ہو اور فاسق اور بدعتی کی امامت مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح: یہ وہ لوگ ہیں جن سے عام حالات میں لوگ کراہیت کرتے ہیں اس لئے ان کی امامت مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر یہ پڑھے لکھے لوگ ہوں اور معاشرہ میں معزز ہوں تو ان کی امامت مکروہ نہیں، یا کوئی دوسرا آدمی امامت کے لائق نہیں ہے تو بھی ان کی امامت مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ نابینا آدمی کو نظر نہیں آتا اس لئے نجاست سے احتیاط نہیں کر پاتا اس لئے اس کی امامت مکروہ ہے۔ تاہم امامت کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ وجه: (١) عن مرثد بن ابی مرثد الغنوى و كان بدريا قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ان سركم أن تقبل صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم فانهم وفدكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم عزوجل - (مستدرک للحاکم، ذکر مناقب مرشد بن ابی مرثد الغنوی، ج ثالث، ص ٢٤٦، نمبر ٤٩٨١ سنن بیھقی، باب اجعلوا ائمتکم خیارکم، ج ثالث، ص ١٢٩، نمبر ٥١٣٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اپنے میں سے اچھے لوگوں کو امام بناؤ تو نماز قبول ہوگی۔ (٢) سالت ابراهیم عن ولد الزنا و الاعرابي و العبد
Chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer: The one with the best voice, then the one with the cleanest clothes (504). If they are equal, then lots are cast or the people choose. If they differ, then consideration is given to what the majority chose (505). If they put forward other than the first, they have done wrong (506). It is disliked to lead prayer for a slave, a blind person, a peasant, an illegitimate child if ignorant, a sinful person, and an innovator. Evidence: (1) From Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari that the Prophet said: The most qualified to lead the people in prayer is the one who recites the Book of Allah most. If they are equal in recitation, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. If they are equal in the Sunnah, then the earliest in Hijrah. In another hadith: If equal in Hijrah, then the oldest in age. Do not lead a man in his own household or in his authority, and do not sit on his cushion in his house except with his permission. (Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 271, no. 1534/1532/673; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 94, no. 584). This hadith indicates that the reciter has more right, but another hadith proves that the most knowledgeable of Sunnah has more right, so after that the reciter has more right. Then the older. (2) Hadith from 'Amr ibn Salamah: When the prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan, and let him lead you who has the most Quran. (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's station in Mecca at the time of conquest, p. 728, no. 2430; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 94, no. 585). This hadith shows that the one with more Quran has more right to lead. (3) This hadith says that the pious one is better. From Murshid ibn Abi Murshid al-Ghanawi: The Prophet said: If you desire that your prayer be accepted, then let your best men lead you, for they are your delegation between you and your Lord. (Mustadrak al-Hakim, mention of Murshid's merits, vol. 3, p. 246, no. 4981; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on make your imams the best among you, vol. 3, p. 129, no. 5133). This hadith says to appoint good people as imams so prayer is accepted. (4) From Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: The Prophet said: When the prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan, and let the oldest among you lead you. (Bukhari, chapter on if equal in recitation, let the oldest lead, p. 94, no. 685; Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 237, no. 1535/674). This hadith shows that if equal in Hijrah and recitation, the older has the right to lead. (5) From Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: The Prophet said: The most qualified to lead is the one who recites the Book of Allah most and is earliest in recitation. If equal in recitation, then the earliest in Hijrah. If equal in Hijrah, then the oldest in age. (Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 236, no. 1534/673; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 94, no. 582). This hadith says if all equal, the older has the right. (6) Priority is given to those with a good voice; evidence: from Anas: The Prophet said: Everything has an adornment, and the adornment of the Quran is a good voice. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on good voice, vol. 2, p. 1319, no. 4184). (504) If all are equal in rank, then lots are cast or the people choose. If they differ, the majority opinion is considered. Evidence: For difficult matters, lots are drawn; hadith from 'A'ishah: When the Prophet intended a journey, he would draw lots among his wives, and the one whose lot came out would go with him. (Bukhari, chapter on lots in difficulties, p. 438, no. 2688). (505) If they put forward someone other than the first, they have done wrong. Explanation: If they appoint a non-first, the prayer is valid with no dislikedness, but it is not good because the rightful person was not given his right. (506) It is disliked for a slave, blind, peasant, illegitimate child if ignorant, sinful, and innovator to lead prayer. Explanation: These are people from whom people generally dislike (to be led), so their imamah is disliked. But if they are educated and respected in society, their imamah is not disliked, or if no one else is fit for imamah, then it is not disliked. A blind person cannot see, so he cannot be careful about impurity, therefore his imamah is disliked. However, if he leads, prayer is valid. Evidence: (1) From Murshid ibn Abi Murshid al-Ghanawi: The Prophet said: If you desire that your prayer be accepted, then let your best men lead you... (same as above) (2) I asked Ibrahim about the illegitimate child, the Bedouin, and the slave.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a legal exposition on who is most entitled to lead the congregational prayer (imamah). The author presents a series of rulings with supporting hadith. The first ruling establishes a priority order: the imam should be chosen based on one who has the best voice, then the cleanest clothes. If multiple candidates are equal, the matter is resolved by casting lots or by the choice of the congregation. If the congregation disagrees, the majority opinion prevails. The text then addresses the case where a less deserving person is appointed: it is not prohibited but it is blameworthy (they did wrong), though the prayer remains valid. Finally, the passage lists several categories of people whose imamah is disliked: a slave, a blind person, a peasant (dehqan), an illegitimate child (if ignorant), a sinful person, and an innovator. The author provides detailed explanation: these rulings are based on general social aversion, but if such individuals are learned and respected, the dislikedness is removed. The blind person's case is due to inability to avoid impurities. The proofs cited include multiple authentic hadith from Sahih Muslim, Sahih Bukhari, Sunan Abu Dawud, Mustadrak al-Hakim, Sunan al-Bayhaqi, and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. The hadiths establish the priority of the most Quranic, then most knowledgeable of Sunnah, then earliest in Hijrah, then oldest in age, and also emphasize appointing the best and most pious. The hadith on lots is from Aisha regarding the Prophet's practice. The overall tone is instructional, guiding the congregation on proper selection of imam.

Key Terms
الاحق بالامامة (al-ahaqqu bi al-imamah): The person most entitled to lead the prayer.
القرعة (al-qur'ah): Casting lots to resolve equality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if candidates for imamah are equal in all qualifications, what is the recommended method to decide?
A) The oldest leads.
B) The congregation chooses or they cast lots.
C) The one with the best voice leads.
D) The prayer is postponed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a detailed hierarchy for choosing an imam, with flexibility through lots or congregation choice when equality occurs.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
Disliked Imams in Congregational Prayer
Rulings on disliked imams and conditions for removal of dislikedness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which persons leading the prayer is disliked (makruh tanzihi) and explain when this dislikedness is removed.

Core Idea
Imamah of slave, blind, peasant, ignorant illegitimate child, sinner, and innovator is disliked unless they are learned or no better alternative exists.

The passage lists several categories of people whose leading of prayer is considered disliked (makruh). This does not mean their prayer is invalid, but it is preferable to avoid appointing them under normal circumstances. The author provides nuanced conditions when this dislikedness is lifted, such as if they are educated and respected or if no one else is available. The underlying principle is that the imam should be the best and most pious person available.

Guided Path
1
List the categories of disliked imams
The text names: a slave, a blind person, a peasant (dehqan), an illegitimate child who is ignorant, a sinful person, and an innovator (mubtadi').
The list is not exhaustive; it represents common cases of social aversion.
2
Understand the ruling level: makruh tanzihi
The term 'makruh' here means disliked in a non-prohibitive sense (tanzihi). It is better to avoid but not sinful.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) and makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
3
Identify conditions that remove dislikedness
The commentary explains: if the person is educated and respected in society, or if no other person is fit for imamah, the dislikedness is lifted.
The blind person's case is due to inability to avoid impurities; but if he is careful, it is no longer disliked.
4
Confirm the validity of the prayer
Even when leading is disliked, if it occurs, the prayer is valid. Dislikedness does not affect validity.
This is consistent with the earlier ruling that going against priority is blameworthy but valid.

(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صوت الحسن، ج ثانی ص ١٣١٩ نمبر ٤١٨٤) (٥٠٤) اگر سب برابر درجہ والے ہوں تو قرعہ ڈالے، یا قوم جسے اختیار کرے۔ اگر آپس میں اختلاف ہو تو کثرت رائے کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ وجه: مشکل کام میں قرعہ ڈالے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أراد سفرا أقرع بين نسائه فأيتهن خرج سهمها خرج بها معه - (بخاری شریف، باب القرعة في المشکلات، ص ٤٣٨، نمبر ٢٦٨٨) (٥٠٥) اگر غیر اولی آدمی کو مقدم کیا تو اچھا نہیں کیا۔ تشریح: اگر غیر اولی کو امام بنا دیا تو نماز ہو جائے گی اس میں کوئی کراہیت نہیں ہے، البتہ اچھا نہیں کیا، کیونکہ حقدار کو حق نہیں دیا (٥٠٦) اور غلام اور نابینا اور دہقانی اور ولد زنا جو جاہل ہو اور فاسق اور بدعتی کی امامت مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح: یہ وہ لوگ ہیں جن سے عام حالات میں لوگ کراہیت کرتے ہیں اس لئے ان کی امامت مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر یہ پڑھے لکھے لوگ ہوں اور معاشرہ میں معزز ہوں تو ان کی امامت مکروہ نہیں، یا کوئی دوسرا آدمی امامت کے لائق نہیں ہے تو بھی ان کی امامت مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ نابینا آدمی کو نظر نہیں آتا اس لئے نجاست سے احتیاط نہیں کر پاتا اس لئے اس کی امامت مکروہ ہے۔ تاہم امامت کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ وجه: (١) عن مرثد بن ابی مرثد الغنوى و كان بدريا قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ان سركم أن تقبل صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم فانهم وفدكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم عزوجل - (مستدرک للحاکم، ذکر مناقب مرشد بن ابی مرثد الغنوی، ج ثالث، ص ٢٤٦، نمبر ٤٩٨١ سنن بیھقی، باب اجعلوا ائمتکم خیارکم، ج ثالث، ص ١٢٩، نمبر ٥١٣٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اپنے میں سے اچھے لوگوں کو امام بناؤ تو نماز قبول ہوگی۔ (٢) سالت ابراهیم عن ولد الزنا و الاعرابي و العبد
Chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer: The one with the best voice, then the one with the cleanest clothes (504). If they are equal, then lots are cast or the people choose. If they differ, then consideration is given to what the majority chose (505). If they put forward other than the first, they have done wrong (506). It is disliked to lead prayer for a slave, a blind person, a peasant, an illegitimate child if ignorant, a sinful person, and an innovator. Evidence: (1) From Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari that the Prophet said: The most qualified to lead the people in prayer is the one who recites the Book of Allah most. If they are equal in recitation, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. If they are equal in the Sunnah, then the earliest in Hijrah. In another hadith: If equal in Hijrah, then the oldest in age. Do not lead a man in his own household or in his authority, and do not sit on his cushion in his house except with his permission. (Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 271, no. 1534/1532/673; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 94, no. 584). This hadith indicates that the reciter has more right, but another hadith proves that the most knowledgeable of Sunnah has more right, so after that the reciter has more right. Then the older. (2) Hadith from 'Amr ibn Salamah: When the prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan, and let him lead you who has the most Quran. (Bukhari, chapter on the Prophet's station in Mecca at the time of conquest, p. 728, no. 2430; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead prayer, p. 94, no. 585). This hadith shows that the one with more Quran has more right to lead. (3) This hadith says that the pious one is better. From Murshid ibn Abi Murshid al-Ghanawi: The Prophet said: If you desire that your prayer be accepted, then let your best men lead you, for they are your delegation between you and your Lord. (Mustadrak al-Hakim, mention of Murshid's merits, vol. 3, p. 246, no. 4981; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on make your imams the best among you, vol. 3, p. 129, no. 5133). This hadith says to appoint good people as imams so prayer is accepted. (4) From Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: The Prophet said: When the prayer comes, let one of you call the adhan, and let the oldest among you lead you. (Bukhari, chapter on if equal in recitation, let the oldest lead, p. 94, no. 685; Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 237, no. 1535/674). This hadith shows that if equal in Hijrah and recitation, the older has the right to lead. (5) From Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: The Prophet said: The most qualified to lead is the one who recites the Book of Allah most and is earliest in recitation. If equal in recitation, then the earliest in Hijrah. If equal in Hijrah, then the oldest in age. (Muslim, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 236, no. 1534/673; Abu Dawud, chapter on who is most entitled to lead, p. 94, no. 582). This hadith says if all equal, the older has the right. (6) Priority is given to those with a good voice; evidence: from Anas: The Prophet said: Everything has an adornment, and the adornment of the Quran is a good voice. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on good voice, vol. 2, p. 1319, no. 4184). (504) If all are equal in rank, then lots are cast or the people choose. If they differ, the majority opinion is considered. Evidence: For difficult matters, lots are drawn; hadith from 'A'ishah: When the Prophet intended a journey, he would draw lots among his wives, and the one whose lot came out would go with him. (Bukhari, chapter on lots in difficulties, p. 438, no. 2688). (505) If they put forward someone other than the first, they have done wrong. Explanation: If they appoint a non-first, the prayer is valid with no dislikedness, but it is not good because the rightful person was not given his right. (506) It is disliked for a slave, blind, peasant, illegitimate child if ignorant, sinful, and innovator to lead prayer. Explanation: These are people from whom people generally dislike (to be led), so their imamah is disliked. But if they are educated and respected in society, their imamah is not disliked, or if no one else is fit for imamah, then it is not disliked. A blind person cannot see, so he cannot be careful about impurity, therefore his imamah is disliked. However, if he leads, prayer is valid. Evidence: (1) From Murshid ibn Abi Murshid al-Ghanawi: The Prophet said: If you desire that your prayer be accepted, then let your best men lead you... (same as above) (2) I asked Ibrahim about the illegitimate child, the Bedouin, and the slave.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a legal exposition on who is most entitled to lead the congregational prayer (imamah). The author presents a series of rulings with supporting hadith. The first ruling establishes a priority order: the imam should be chosen based on one who has the best voice, then the cleanest clothes. If multiple candidates are equal, the matter is resolved by casting lots or by the choice of the congregation. If the congregation disagrees, the majority opinion prevails. The text then addresses the case where a less deserving person is appointed: it is not prohibited but it is blameworthy (they did wrong), though the prayer remains valid. Finally, the passage lists several categories of people whose imamah is disliked: a slave, a blind person, a peasant (dehqan), an illegitimate child (if ignorant), a sinful person, and an innovator. The author provides detailed explanation: these rulings are based on general social aversion, but if such individuals are learned and respected, the dislikedness is removed. The blind person's case is due to inability to avoid impurities. The proofs cited include multiple authentic hadith from Sahih Muslim, Sahih Bukhari, Sunan Abu Dawud, Mustadrak al-Hakim, Sunan al-Bayhaqi, and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. The hadiths establish the priority of the most Quranic, then most knowledgeable of Sunnah, then earliest in Hijrah, then oldest in age, and also emphasize appointing the best and most pious. The hadith on lots is from Aisha regarding the Prophet's practice. The overall tone is instructional, guiding the congregation on proper selection of imam.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked (makruh tanzihi) - the act is less preferable but not sinful.
فاسق (fasiq): A sinful person, one who commits major sins openly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the imamah of a blind person NOT disliked?
A) Never, it is always disliked.
B) When he is careful about impurities and/or respected in society.
C) Only if he is a scholar.
D) Only if no one else is present.

Key Takeaway
Disliked imamah is conditional; the prayer remains valid, and the dislikedness may be lifted based on the individual's knowledge and social standing.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Validity of Prayer Behind Various Types of Imams
Lists categories of imams with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of prayer behind a fasiq and identify the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Prayer behind any Muslim is valid, even if sinful, but it is makruh in certain cases.

This lesson examines the extensive evidence from hadith and athar that the Hanafi school uses to support the validity of prayer behind various imams, including those who are sinful, blind, or non-Arab. The core principle is that the essential validity of the prayer depends on the fulfillment of conditions by the followers, not the righteousness of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of imams discussed
List all types of imams mentioned in the passage: bedouin Arab, illegitimate child, ignorant person, fasiq, innovator, non-Arab (ajami), slave, and blind.
Each category has a specific ruling regarding whether leading prayer is valid, makruh, or allowed.
2
For each category, state the Hanafi ruling
Based on the hadith and athar, determine if prayer behind that type of imam is valid (sahih) or invalid (batil), and if makruh (disliked). For example, behind a fasiq it is valid but makruh tahrimi.
The text explicitly says 'valid' for fasiq and 'makruh' for ajami with incorrect recitation.
3
Locate the principal dalil for each ruling
For each category, find the specific hadith or athar cited as evidence. For the fasiq, the key hadith is from Abu Huraira: 'The obligatory prayer is incumbent behind every Muslim, whether righteous or sinful.'
Multiple proofs are given; the strongest is the explicit command 'واجبة'.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The Hanafi school argues that validity of the congregation depends on the followers' actions, not the imam's personal sin. Thus, prayer behind a fasiq is valid, though disliked due to the command to avoid their evil.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i view that requires the imam to be upright ('adl).

Chapter on who is most entitled to leadership (imamah). The bedouin Arab, the illegitimate child, the ignorant, the sinful, and the innovator... and prolonging prayer, and the congregation of naked men... and the blind: do they lead? He said: Yes, when they establish the prayer. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on the ruling of the child of fornication, vol. 2, p. 263, no. 3849) In this saying of a Tabi'i, it is that if the prayer has begun and there is no one else, he can lead; otherwise it is not good. (3) The non-Arab's Quran is not correct, therefore his imamah is makruh. For this there is the following athar: I heard Ubayd ibn Umayr say: A group gathered around Makkah... Al-Musawwar ibn Makhramah said: Look at me, O Commander of the Faithful. The man had a non-Arab tongue and was in Hajj. I feared that some of the pilgrims would hear his recitation and adopt his non-Arab[ic accent]. He (Umar) said: Then you lost it? He said: Yes. Then [Umar] said: You are right. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on the dislike of imamah of the non-Arab and the one who makes mistakes, vol. 3, p. 127, no. 5127) In this athar, the villager was removed from imamah because his recitation was not good. (4) Aisha was led in prayer by her slave Zaqwan from the mushaf. Ibn Umar said: When the first Muhajirun arrived at Asbah - a place in Quba - before the arrival of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, Salim, the freed slave of Abu Hudhayfah, led them in prayer, and he was the most knowledgeable in Quran among them. (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on imamah of the slave and the freed slave, p. 96, no. 692) This hadith indicates that a slave can lead prayer provided he has knowledge and the people like him. (5) Regarding the imamah of the blind, there is this hadith: Anas reported that the Prophet ﷺ appointed Ibn Umm Maktum to lead the people in prayer while he was blind. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on imamah of the blind, p. 95, no. 595) From this it is known that if the blind person takes care of his purity and is respected among the people, he can be appointed imam; it is not makruh. (6) Prayer behind a sinful person is valid. Its evidence is this hadith: Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn Khiyar entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged. He said: You are the imam of the general public, and you see what has befallen you, and an imam of fitna leads us in prayer, and we find it objectionable. He said: Prayer is the best thing people do. So if people do good, do good with them; and if they do evil, avoid their evil. (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on imamah of the one who is tempted and the innovator, p. 96, no. 695) From this athar it is known that prayer can be offered behind a sinful person, although it is makruh. (7) Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: The obligatory prayer is incumbent behind every Muslim, whether righteous or sinful, even if he commits major sins. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on imamah of the righteous and the sinful, p. 95, no. 594) (8) Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and offer funeral prayer over every righteous and sinful person. (Darqutni, chapter on description of whom prayer with and prayer over is permissible, vol. 2, p. 44, no. 1750; also Bayhaqi, chapter on prayer over one who killed himself without considering it lawful, vol. 4, Kitab al-Janaiz, p. 29, no. 6832) From this hadith it is known that prayer behind a sinful person is valid.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on who may lead prayer, supported by hadith and athar. The chapter begins by listing categories: bedouin Arab, illegitimate child, ignorant, sinful, innovator. For each, the text provides evidence. The first athar from Abdurrazzaq indicates that in necessity, even such persons may lead. For the non-Arab (ajami) whose recitation is incorrect, imamah is makruh, as shown by the incident where Umar rejected a non-Arab imam. The hadith of Aisha and the slave Zaqwan shows that a slave may lead if knowledgeable and accepted. The blind can lead if he maintains purity and is respected, as per the Prophet's appointment of Ibn Umm Maktum. For the sinful (fasiq), multiple hadith establish that prayer behind him is valid, though it is makruh. The text quotes Uthman's statement and explicit hadith from Abu Huraira. Overall, the Hanafi position is that imamah is valid from all Muslims, but makruh tahrimi for those with defective recitation or open sin.

Key Terms
امامة (imamah): Leading others in congregational prayer
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but not sinful; prayer is still valid
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins openly

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on prayer behind a fasiq (sinful person)?
A) Invalid and must be repeated
B) Valid but makruh
C) Valid and recommended
D) Invalid without a valid excuse

Key Takeaway
Prayer behind any Muslim, including a fasiq, is valid according to Hanafi fiqh, though it is makruh due to the imam's sin.

Ruling on Prolonging Prayer
States that prolonging prayer beyond sunnah is makruh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prolonging prayer for an imam versus a person praying alone, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
For the imam, prolonging prayer to the point of hardship is makruh; alone, it is permissible as desired.

The length of recitation in prayer is not left to random choice. The Prophet ﷺ gave clear guidance: an imam must consider his congregation, while a person praying alone may recite as long as he wishes. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'prolonging prayer' (tatwil al-salah) beyond the sunnah amount. Determine the hukm level for the imam and for a person praying alone.
The sunnah amounts are specified for each prayer: long mufassal for Fajr and Zuhr, middle for Asr and Isha, short for Maghrib.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith quoted in the text. Note that it is from Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
The hadith includes the Prophet's anger and his command to be brief.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the command 'فليتجوز' (let him be brief) leads to the ruling of karahah. Consider the reason given: the weak, old, and needy.
The command is not absolute but tied to the presence of hardship.
4
Distinguish imam vs. alone
Note the clear distinction: the same hadith allows lengthening when praying alone ('وإذا صلى أحدكم لنفسه فليطول ما شاء').
This exception shows the ruling is context-dependent.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi): imam should shorten to avoid hardship; alone may lengthen.
This is based on the explicit hadith and is agreed upon across schools (muttafaq alayh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۰۷) وتطويل الصلوة (۵۰۸) وجماعة العراة و الاعمى هل يؤمون ؟ قال نعم اذا اقاموا ا را الصلاة .
تشريح : : جن نمازوں میں جتنی قرآت مسنون ہے، مثلا فجر اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل بعصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل ، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل، اس سے بہت زیادہ پڑھنا جس سے مقتدی اکتا جائے ، یہ مکروہ ہے۔ وجه : اخبــرنــي ابو مسعود ان رجل قال والله يا رسول الله اني لاتأخر عن صلوة الغداة من اجل فلان مما صلى الله يطيل بنا فما رأيت رسول الله عله في موعظه اشد غضبا منه يومئذ ثم قال ان منكم منفرين فايكم ما صلى بالناس فليتجوز فان فيهم الضعيف والكبير وذا الحاجة ۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ و اذا صلی احدکم لنفسه فليطول ما شاء (بخاری شریف، باب تخفیف الامام فی القیام و اتمام الركوع والسجو د ص ۱۵ نمبر ۷۰۳/۷۰۲ مسلم شریف ، باب أمر الائمة بتخفیف الصلوۃ فی تمام، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۱۰۴۴/۴۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بہت لمبا کرنا مکروہ ہے لیکن اپنے لئے پڑھے تو جتنی چاہے لمبی قرآت کر سکتا ہے۔
Translation: (507) And prolonging the prayer (508) And the congregation of naked men and the blind: do they lead? He said: Yes, when they establish the prayer. Explanation: In those prayers where a specific amount of recitation is sunnah, for example, in Fajr and Zuhr the long Surahs of Mufassal, in Asr and Isha the middle ones, and in Maghrib the short ones, reciting much more than that which causes the followers to tire, this is makruh. Evidence: Abu Mas'ud informed me that a man said: By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, I delay the morning prayer because of so-and-so who lengthens it for us. I never saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ more angry in an admonition than that day. Then he said: Among you are those who cause aversion. So whoever leads the people in prayer, let him be brief, for among them are the weak, the old, and the one with a need. In another narration: When any of you prays alone, he may lengthen as he wishes. (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on the imam shortening the standing and completing the bowing and prostration, p. 15, no. 703/702; Sahih Muslim, chapter on the command to imams to shorten the prayer while completing it, p. 188, no. 1044/466) This hadith indicates that lengthening excessively is makruh, but if one prays alone, he may recite as long as he wishes.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on prolonging prayer for an imam. The text first states the ruling: it is makruh for an imam to lengthen the recitation beyond the sunnah amount to the point that followers become weary. It specifies the sunnah recitations: for Fajr and Zuhr, the long surahs of al-Mufassal (from Qaf to Buruj or similar); for Asr and Isha, the middle ones; for Maghrib, the short ones. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ became very angry upon hearing that a man delayed the prayer due to a lengthy imam, and he commanded imams to be brief, considering the weak, elderly, and those with needs. However, the hadith also allows lengthening for one praying alone. The Hanafi school thus distinguishes: an imam should avoid undue length, but a person praying alone may recite as much as desired, as there is no hardship on others.

Key Terms
تطويل الصلوة (tatwil al-salah): Lengthening the prayer recitation beyond the sunnah amount
مفصل (mufassal): The section of the Quran from Surah Qaf to the end, divided into long, medium, short

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Lengthen as much as possible
B) Be brief considering the congregation's needs
C) Recite only the short surahs of Mufassal
D) Lengthen only in Fajr

Key Takeaway
The imam must avoid prolonging prayer to the point of hardship, but a person praying alone may lengthen as desired.

Congregation of Naked Men and Women: Ruling and Imam's Position
Ruling on congregational prayer for naked men and women alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer for naked men and women alone, explain the obligatory position of the imam, and justify it using the hadith about rows.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is makruh for naked men or women alone; if performed, the imam stands in the middle of the row.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: when people have no clothing (naked) or only women are present. The Hanafi school rules that forming a congregation in such cases is makruh (disliked) but provides clear guidance on how to conduct it should necessity arise. The key proof is the hadith that the best rows for women are the last, which is extended to the imam's forward position. Understanding this ruling clarifies the madhhab's approach to modesty and necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage separately discusses (a) a congregation of naked men and (b) a congregation of women only. Recognize that each has the same ruling but separate proofs.
The ruling applies when participants have no clothing or are exclusively women with no male mahram present.
2
State the ruling for each
For both cases, the Hanafi ruling is 'makruh tanzihi' (disliked, but permissible if done). The text emphasizes that it is better to pray individually.
Makruh tanzihi means it is not sinful but avoiding it is more virtuous.
3
Note the exception: imam in middle
If the congregation is formed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row, not ahead. This minimizes exposure and maintains modesty.
For women, this is based on the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah. For naked men, it is based on the action of a companion (Qatada's report).
4
Analyze the primary proof
The hadith 'Khayru sufuf al-rijal awaluha...' is used to derive the dislike. Since women are encouraged to stay in the back rows, leading (which puts them in front) is disliked.
The hadith is sahih, but its indication (dalalah) is zanni, leading to a makruh ruling, not haram.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) permit women's congregation without the imam being in the middle and do not consider it makruh. The Hanafi position is based on the combination of the hadith and the companion practices.
The practical difference (thamarah) is the imam's position and the degree of dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۰۸) وجماعة العراة والنساء فان فعلن يقف الامام وسطهن كالعراة
تشريح : آدمیوں کے پاس کپڑا نہ ہو تو یہ الگ الگ نماز پڑھے جماعت کرنا مکروہ ہے، اور اگر جماعت کر لیں تو امام بیچ میں بیٹھے سب سے آگے نہ ہوتا کہ زیادہ بے پردگی نہ ہو۔ اس طرح صرف عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر کرنا چاہے تو امام درمیان میں کھڑی ہو مرد کی طرح آگے نہ ہوتا کہ زیادہ بے پردگی نہ ہو۔

(مسلم شریف، باب تسوية الصفوف واقامتها فضل الاول الخ، ص ۱۸۲، نمبر ۹۸۵/۴۴۰ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صف النساء والتأخر عن الصف الاول ، ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۶۷۸) جب عورت کو اگلی صف میں جانا مکروہ ہے تو امامت کرنا بھی مکروہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں آگے جانا ہوتا ہے۔ (۴) عن ام حميد امرأة ابي حميد الساعدى: أنها جائت النبي فقالت : يا رسول الله علم اني احب الصلوة
Translation: (508) And the congregation of naked men and women; if they do it, the imam stands in the middle of them like the naked. Explanation: If men have no clothing, they should pray individually; congregation is makruh. If they do form a congregation, the imam should sit in the middle, not at the front, to avoid more exposure. Similarly, a congregation of only women is makruh, but if they wish, the imam (female) should stand in the middle, not like a man at the front, to avoid more exposure. Evidence (1) The imam stands in the middle: this is the practice of a companion. From Qatada: When people came out of the sea naked, one of them led them in prayer; they prayed sitting, and their imam was in the row with them, making gestures. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on prayer of the naked, vol. 2, p. 1384, no. 4576) This effect indicates that a naked man will pray sitting, make gestures, and stand in the middle of the row. (2) A woman stands in the middle: this is the practice of a female companion. From Raitah al-Hanafiyyah: Aisha led us in prayer and stood between us in the obligatory prayer. In another hadith from Hujayrah bint Husayn: Umm Salamah led us in Asr prayer and stood between us. (Darqutni, chapter on women praying in congregation and the position of their imam, vol. 1, p. 1388, no. 1493/1492; Mustadrak al-Hakim, chapter on the virtue of prayer, vol. 1, p. 320, no. 73) This effect shows that a woman's imamah is permissible and that she stands in the middle. (3) The reason why a woman's imamah is makruh is this hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first. (Sahih Muslim, chapter on straightening rows and establishing them, virtue of the first, etc., p. 182, no. 985/440; Abu Dawud, chapter on women's rows and staying behind the first row, p. 106, no. 678) Since it is makruh for a woman to go to the front row, it is also makruh for her to lead prayer because that involves going forward. (4) From Umm Humaid, the wife of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: She came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: O Messenger of Allah, I love prayer...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings for congregational prayer when the participants are naked men or women only. For naked men, it is makruh to form a congregation; they should pray individually. If they do, the imam sits in the middle of the row, not ahead, to minimize exposure. For women-only congregations, it is also makruh, based on the hadith that the best rows for women are the last, so leading (which puts her in front) is disliked. However, if they do form a congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row, as proven by the practice of Aisha and Umm Salamah. The proofs are from the actions of companions and the hadith about rows. The overall ruling: such congregations are permissible but makruh, and the imam's position is in the middle.

Key Terms
جماعة العراة (jama'at al-uraah): Congregational prayer of naked men
امام وسط (imam wast): Imam standing in the middle of the row, not ahead

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) In the middle of the row
C) At the back
D) Beside the first row

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, congregational prayer for those without proper covering or for women alone is makruh, but if performed, the imam must stand in the middle of the row.

Imam's Position for Naked Men and Women Congregations
States ruling on congregational prayer for naked men and women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's position when leading a congregation of only naked men or only women, and explain why this differs from the usual practice.

Core Idea
For naked men or all-women congregations, the imam stands in the middle, not ahead.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario where the usual practice of the imam standing ahead of the congregation is set aside. When only naked men (due to lack of clothing) or only women are present, the imam stands in the middle of the row to minimize exposure and maintain modesty. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate how modesty considerations can modify prayer postures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn mentions two cases: (1) when only women lead women in prayer, and (2) by analogy, when only naked men are present. Both require a deviation from the standard imam positioning.
2
State the ruling for the imam's position
In both cases, the imam does not stand ahead of the congregation but instead stands in the middle of the row (يقف وسطهن). This is the mufta bihi position.
The overall congregational prayer itself is makruh tanzih (disliked) due to the exposure of 'awrah.
3
Understand the rationale
The purpose is to cover the 'awrah as much as possible. For naked men, standing in the middle reduces exposure from the sides. For women, it aligns with the principle that women's rows are better at the back.
The evidence includes practices of the Companions and modesty considerations.
4
Memorize the key phrase
The phrase "كالعراة" (like the naked) connects the two cases: women leading women are treated analogously to naked men leading. Memorize this analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأحق بالإمامة والنساء فان فعلن يقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة
Chapter on who is most entitled to lead, and women, if they do (lead), the imam stands in their middle like the naked (men).
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn. It addresses two cases: (1) When naked men lead the prayer (due to lack of clothing), and (2) when women lead women in prayer. In both cases, the imam does not stand ahead of the congregation as usual but rather stands in the middle of the row. This is to minimize exposure (for naked men) and to maintain modesty (for women). The Hanafi school holds that such congregational prayer is makruh (disliked), but if performed, the imam's position is in the middle. The evidence includes practices of the Companions and the principle that women's rows are better at the back.

Key Terms
عراة (urāt): Naked persons, i.e., those without clothing to cover the 'awrah
أحق بالإمامة (ahaqqu bil-imāmah): Most entitled to lead the prayer

Position of Followers: One to Right, Many Behind
Ruling on follower placement relative to imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the placement of a single follower and multiple followers in congregational prayer and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, one follower stands to the imam's right; two or more form rows behind.

This passage from the matn gives a concise ruling on the arrangement of male followers in congregational prayer. The Hanafi school bases this on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, who placed Ibn Abbas on his right and when there were two followers, they stood behind. Understanding this placement ensures the congregation follows the sunnah in order and maintains the imam's leadership.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for a single follower
The single male follower stands to the right of the imam, slightly behind. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas who stood on the Prophet's right.
If the follower is a woman, she stands behind even if alone.
2
State the ruling for multiple followers
When there are two or more followers, they form one or more rows directly behind the imam, not to the sides.
The imam may move forward slightly to allow the followers to be behind him.
3
Understand the wisdom
This arrangement preserves the imam's position as leader and maintains the unity and straightness of the rows.
4
Identify the evidence
The evidence comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ: Ibn Abbas reported that he stood on the right; Anas reported that he and an orphan stood behind the Prophet.
Hadith sources: Bukhari and Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف الواحد عن يمين الإمام والأكثر خلفه
And the single (follower) stands to the right of the imam, and the many (stand) behind him.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn on the placement of followers in congregational prayer. The Hanafi school prescribes: if there is only one male follower, he stands to the right of the imam, slightly behind (not exactly aligned). If there are two or more followers, they form a row behind the imam. The evidence comes from hadith: Ibn Abbas prayed with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and was placed on the right; when two followers were present (Anas and an orphan), they stood behind the Prophet. The wisdom is to maintain the imam's leadership position and the unity of the congregation.

Key Terms
يمين الإمام (yamīn al-imām): The right side of the imam
خلفه (khalafahu): Behind him (the imam), i.e., in a row or rows behind the imam

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
States the sequence of rows in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows for congregational prayer and identify the hukm (sunnah muakkadah) of following this order.

Core Idea
Rows: men first, then boys, then khuntha, then women — a sunnah sequence rooted in modesty and hadith.

When Muslims pray in congregation behind an imam, the arrangement of rows is not arbitrary. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific order based on the Sunnah: men (the closest to the imam), then male children, then hermaphrodites (khuntha), and finally women at the back. This lesson unpacks the source text and explains the reasoning, hukm, and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn describes the recommended sequence for arranging rows (sufuf) in congregation. First, recognize that this is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) – following it is rewarded, but violating it is only makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).
2
Memorize the exact order
The text states: الرجال (men), ثم الصبيان (then boys), ثم الخناثى (then hermaphrodites/khuntha), ثم النساء (then women). Commit this sequence to memory.
The term 'khunāthā' (sing. khunthā) refers to persons with ambiguous gender characteristics.
3
Understand the basis in hadith
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The best rows for men are the first, and the worst are the last; the best rows for women are the last, and the worst are the first.' (Sahih Muslim). This hadith guides the order: men at the front, women at the back. Boys and khuntha are placed in between because they share some characteristics of both.
The placement of khuntha between children and women is uniquely Hanafi; other schools may place them with women or men.
4
Note the consequences of non-compliance
If the order is deliberately reversed (e.g., women in front of men), the prayer is still valid, but the arrangement is makruh tanzih (disliked). The imam should gently guide the congregation to correct order.
This disorder does not invalidate the salah; it only reduces reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم الخناثى ثم النساء
And he arranges (the rows): the men, then the boys, then the hermaphrodites, then the women.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn on the arrangement of rows when different categories of people are present in the congregational prayer. The Hanafi order is: adult males first (closest to the imam), then male children, then hermaphrodites (khuntha, i.e., persons of ambiguous gender), and finally women at the back. This is based on hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the best rows for men are the first, and for women the last. Children and khuntha are placed between because their status is intermediate. This order ensures modesty and follows the sunnah.

Key Terms
خناثى (khunāthā): Hermaphrodites; persons with ambiguous gender characteristics
صف (saff): Row (in congregational prayer)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi row order in congregational prayer is men, then boys, then khuntha, then women — a sunnah sequence rooted in the Prophet's guidance on best rows.

Positioning of Muqtadis: One to the Right, Many Behind
Rulings and proofs for muqtadi positioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for positioning of a single muqtadi and multiple muqtadis relative to the imam, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
One muqtadi stands to the right of the imam; many stand behind.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on where muqtadis should stand in congregational prayer. The ruling is derived from multiple authentic hadith and is considered sunnah muakkadah. Understanding these positions ensures proper arrangement and avoids confusion, especially when the congregation is small.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the positioning of muqtadis relative to the imam during prayer. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), meaning it is highly recommended but not obligatory; the prayer remains valid even if the recommended positioning is not followed.
This is not a condition of validity, so if a muqtadi stands behind or to the left, the prayer is still valid.
2
State the ruling for a single muqtadi
When there is only one muqtadi, he should stand to the right of the imam, but slightly behind him—not exactly level. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet turned him from left to right.
The right side is preferred due to its honor and the practice of the Prophet.
3
State the ruling for multiple muqtadis
When there are two or more muqtadis, they should stand behind the imam, forming rows. The hadith of Anas and the orphan (two men) and the hadith of Jabir (two men) show that the Prophet placed them behind him.
The first row is best; subsequent rows are arranged behind in order.
4
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The three hadith cited are: (1) Ibn Abbas: stood to left, Prophet turned him to right; (2) Anas and orphan: prayed behind Prophet; (3) Jabir and Ibn Sakhr: both placed behind. These are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawood.
The Hanafi school relies on these explicit practices of the Prophet.
5
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (indication of the proof)
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is considered a proof (dalil) of sunnah. The consistent pattern—one man to right, two or more behind—indicates the preferred method. The hadith are specific and not contradicted by other texts.
Shafi'is argue from a different hadith that one should stand behind, but Hanafis give weight to these explicit actions.

Source Text

Proof: (1) The right side is better, so if there is one follower, the imam makes him stand to his right. (2) Hadith: Ibn Abbas said: I prayed with the Prophet one night and stood to his left, so he took my head from behind and placed me to his right... (Bukhari, Muslim). In this hadith, Anas and the orphan were two men, so they stood behind the Prophet. (3) We came to Jabir bin Abdullah: he said I went with the Prophet in a battle... then I came and stood to the left of the Prophet, so he took my hand and turned me to his right, then Ibn Sakhr came and stood to his left, so he took both our hands and made us stand behind him (Abu Dawood). In this hadith, when there were two, he made them stand behind. Translation (510): Rows are arranged: first men, then children, then khunatha, then women. Explanation: If there are various types of people, first the row of men, then children, then khunatha, and last women. Since khunatha are between men and women, they are made to stand a bit ahead of women. Proof: (1) Anas bin Malik said: I and an orphan prayed behind the Prophet, and my mother behind us. In this hadith, men are first, then children, and last women. (2) Abu Huraira said: the Prophet said... (incomplete).

Two or more stand behind the imam, forming rows. The proofs come from three hadith. (2) Order of rows: men first, then children, then khunatha (intersex), then women. This order ensures purity and prevention of fitnah. The hadith of Anas and Umm Sulaim shows the separation.

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on row sequence with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of rows in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Men first, then children, then khunatha, then women — best row for men first, for women last.

This lesson establishes the sunnah order of rows in congregational prayer. The order is not obligatory but following it brings greater reward. We'll examine the proofs from the hadith of Anas and the general principle about the virtue of first rows for men and last rows for women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the order: men, then boys (children), then khunatha (intersex), then women. This is the preferred sequence.
It is sunnah muakkadah; reversing is valid but makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths: (1) Anas ibn Malik prayed with an orphan behind the Prophet, with Umm Sulaym behind them. (2) The Prophet said the best rows for men are the first, worst are the last; best for women are the last, worst are the first.
These show men first, children before women, and women behind.
3
Understand the hikmah
Placing women at the back preserves modesty and prevents fitnah. The khunatha are placed between men and women due to their ambiguous gender.
4
Apply the ruling
In a mixed congregation, arrange rows accordingly. If someone stands in a different row, the prayer is still valid but the sunnah order is missed.

(513) If the imam adds an extra sajdah or stands after the final qa'dah... the rows of men: the first is best, the last is worst; the rows of women: the last is best, the first is worst (Muslim, Abu Dawood). This hadith states that women's row should be last. Chapter: statement of wajib acts of muqtadi after imam finishes. Translation (511): If the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, the muqtadi completes it. Explanation: Reciting tashahhud is wajib, so if the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes it, the muqtadi completes it, then says salam. Because tashahhud is wajib, and there is no further action, so he completes tashahhud then says salam. This issue is based on two principles: (1) Following the imam is wajib, so if by following the imam a wajib act is missed, it is delayed; but if a sunnah is missed, it is left off and the imam is followed.

Commentary
This passage covers the order of rows (510) and then introduces the chapter on muqtadi's actions after the imam (511-513). The order of rows is based on the sunnah practice: men first, then children, then khunatha, then women. The hadith of Anas shows this order. The Prophet also said that the best rows for men are the first and worst are the last, for women the best are the last and worst are the first, which is why women are placed at the back. Then the chapter begins: if the imam gives salam before the muqtadi finishes tashahhud (which is wajib), the muqtadi completes it and then says salam, since wajib takes precedence over following the imam when there is no conflict later.

صَفّ (ṣaff): Row or line in congregational prayer.

Completing Tashahhud After Imam's Salam
Ruling on muqtadi completing tashahhud after imam's salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that if the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, the muqtadi must complete it, and justify based on the principle that wajib takes precedence over following the imam when no further action remains.

Core Idea
If the imam says salam before you finish tashahhud, complete tashahhud then say salam — wajib over following.

This lesson addresses a common situation in congregational prayer: the imam completes prayer while the muqtadi is still reciting tashahhud. The Hanafi school gives a clear priority: complete the wajib act of tashahhud before following the imam in salam. We will examine the reasoning and the two principles behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The muqtadi is reciting tashahhud (which is wajib) when the imam says salam. The imam completes prayer before the muqtadi finishes tashahhud.
Tashahhud is a wajib act in the Hanafi school.
2
Apply the first principle: following the imam is wajib
Following the imam in all actions is wajib for the muqtadi. Normally, he should salam with the imam.
This is established in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the second principle: preserve a wajib when possible
If following the imam would cause a wajib act (like tashahhud) to be missed, and there is no further action after tashahhud, then the muqtadi delays following the imam and completes the wajib.
If the action missed were only sunnah, the muqtadi would skip it and follow the imam.
4
Determine the ruling
The muqtadi completes tashahhud (since it is wajib and there is no later action), then says salam. He does not follow the imam's salam immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۱۰) ويصفّ الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم الخناثي ثم النساء.
تشريح : اگر کئی قسم کے لوگ ہوں تو پہلے مردوں کی صف ہوگی ، پھر بچوں کی پھر خلفی کی ، اور اخیر میں عورتوں کی ۔ چونکہ خفی مرد اور عورت کے درمیان کے لوگ ہیں اس لئے ان کو عورتوں سے تھوڑا آگے کھڑا کیا۔
وجه : (۱) عن انس بن مالک قال صليت انا ويتيم في بيتنا خلف النبى وامی خلفنا ام سلیم ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفا ،ص ۱۱۸، نمبر ۷۲۷ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب اذا کانوا ثلثۃ کیف یقومون ،ص ۹۹، نمبر ۶۱۲ ) اس حدیث میں مرد پہلے ہیں پھر جو بچے بھی ہیں اور اخیر میں عورتیں ہیں۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله

فصل فيما يفعله المقتدى
فصل : فيما يفعله المقتدى بعد فراغ امامه من واجب و غیره
(۵۱۱)لو سلّم الامام قبل فراغ المقتدى من التشهد يتمّه (۵۱۲) ولو رفع الامام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدى ثلاثا في الركوع او السجود يتابعه (۵۱۳) ولو زاد الامام سجدة او قام بعد القعود الاخير صفوف الرجال اولها وشرها آخرها و خیر صفوف النساء آخرها و شرها اولها. (مسلم شریف، باب تسوية الصفوف واقامتها فضل الاول الخ ص ۱۸۶، نمبر ۹۸۵/۴۴۰ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صف النساء والتأخر عن الصف الاول ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۶۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کی صف اخیر میں ہونی چاہئے ۔
فصل : ۔ امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد مقتدی کے افعال واجبہ کا بیان
ترجمه : (۵۱۱) اگر امام مقتدی کے تشہد پڑھنے سے پہلے سلام پھیرے تو مقتدی اپنا تشہد پورا کرے۔ تشریح : تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے اس لئے تشہد پڑھنے سے پہلے امام سلام پھیر دے تو مقتدی اپنا تشہد پورا کرے اس کے بعد سلام پھیرے۔ کیونکہ تشہد واجب ہے ، اور آگے کوئی کام بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے تشہد پورا کر کے سلام پھیرے۔ یہ مسئلہ دو اصولوں پر ہے [1] ایک یہ ہے کہ امام کی اقتداء واجب ہے اس لئے اگر امام کے ساتھ چلنے میں کوئی واجب چھوٹ رہا تو اس سے تاخیر کی جائے گی ، اور اگر سنت چھوٹ رہی ہو تو اس کو چھوڑ کر امام کے ساتھ ہوکر عمل کیا جائے گا۔
(510) And rows are arranged: men, then boys, then khunatha, then women. Explanation: If there are various types of people, the row of men is first, then boys, then khunatha, and last women. Since khunatha are between men and women, they are placed slightly ahead of women. Proof: (1) Anas bin Malik said: I and an orphan prayed in our house behind the Prophet, and my mother behind us (Bukhari, Abu Dawood). In this hadith, men are first, then children, and last women. (2) Abu Huraira said: the Prophet said... (incomplete). [Page 344] Chapter on what the muqtadi does. Chapter: what the muqtadi does after the imam finishes wajib and other acts. (511) If the imam gives salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, he completes it. (512) If the imam raises his head before the muqtadi says three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, he follows him. (513) If the imam adds an extra sajdah or stands after the final qa'dah... the rows of men: the first is best, the last is worst; the rows of women: the last is best, the first is worst (Muslim, Abu Dawood). This hadith states that women's row should be last. Chapter: statement of wajib acts of muqtadi after imam finishes. Translation (511): If the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, the muqtadi completes it. Explanation: Reciting tashahhud is wajib, so if the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes it, the muqtadi completes it, then says salam. Because tashahhud is wajib, and there is no further action, so he completes tashahhud then says salam. This issue is based on two principles: (1) Following the imam is wajib, so if by following the imam a wajib act is missed, it is delayed; but if a sunnah is missed, it is left off and the imam is followed.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage covers the order of rows (510) and then introduces the chapter on muqtadi's actions after the imam (511-513). The order of rows is based on the sunnah practice: men first, then children, then khunatha, then women. The hadith of Anas shows this order. The Prophet also said that the best rows for men are the first and worst are the last, for women the best are the last and worst are the first, which is why women are placed at the back. Then the chapter begins: if the imam gives salam before the muqtadi finishes tashahhud (which is wajib), the muqtadi completes it and then says salam, since wajib takes precedence over following the imam when there is no conflict later.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'At-tahiyyatu lillah...' in the sitting position of prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately say salam and skip tashahhud.
B) Complete tashahhud then say salam.
C) Repeat the prayer because the imam's salam was invalid.
D) Make sajdah al-sahw then say salam.

Key Takeaway
Complete tashahhud before salam because it is wajib and cannot be skipped when following the imam.

Completing Tashahhud After Imam's Salam
Ruling on muqtadi completing tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muqtadi completing tashahhud after the imam's salam and explain the two principles that govern this ruling.

Core Idea
Tashahhud is wajib; when imam speeds ahead, muqtadi completes his wajib before following.

You are praying behind an imam. He says salam while you are still in the middle of tashahhud. Should you quickly say salam to follow him, or finish tashahhud? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer based on two principles: the obligation of tashahhud and the rule of which duty takes precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tashahhud is a wajib (obligatory) act in the Hanafi school. Understand its legal status.
Wajib: omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Identify the scenario
The imam says salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud. There is a conflict: should the muqtadi follow the imam immediately or complete his tashahhud?
3
Apply the principle of prioritization
The text states two principles: (1) Following the imam is wajib, but if it causes missing another wajib, it is delayed. (2) If a sunnah would be missed, it is abandoned. Here, tashahhud is wajib, so it takes precedence.
4
Derive the conclusion
The muqtadi completes his tashahhud, then says salam. This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is consider tashahhud as sunnah, so they would say muqtadi should follow the imam immediately. Understand the basis of the difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۱۱) لو سلّم الامام قبل فراغ المقتدى من التشهد يتمّه
ترجمه : (۵۱۱) اگر امام مقتدی کے تشہد پڑھنے سے پہلے سلام پھیرے تو مقتدی اپنا تشہد پورا کرے۔ تشریح : تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے اس لئے تشہد پڑھنے سے پہلے امام سلام پھیر دے تو مقتدی اپنا تشہد پورا کرے اس کے بعد سلام پھیرے۔ کیونکہ تشہد واجب ہے ، اور آگے کوئی کام بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے تشہد پورا کر کے سلام پھیرے۔ یہ مسئلہ دو اصولوں پر ہے [1] ایک یہ ہے کہ امام کی اقتداء واجب ہے اس لئے اگر امام کے ساتھ چلنے میں کوئی واجب چھوٹ رہا تو اس سے تاخیر کی جائے گی ، اور اگر سنت چھوٹ رہی ہو تو اس کو چھوڑ کر امام کے ساتھ ہوکر عمل کیا جائے گا۔
(511) If the imam gives salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, he completes it. Translation: (511) If the imam says salam before the muqtadi recites tashahhud, the muqtadi completes his tashahhud. Explanation: Reciting tashahhud is wajib, so if the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes tashahhud, the muqtadi completes it, then says salam. Because tashahhud is wajib, and there is no further action, so he completes tashahhud then says salam. This issue is based on two principles: (1) Following the imam is wajib, so if by following the imam a wajib act is missed, it is delayed; but if a sunnah is missed, it is left off and the imam is followed.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This is a ruling about the muqtadi's obligation when the imam finishes the prayer earlier. Tashahhud is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school. If the imam says salam before the muqtadi finishes tashahhud, the muqtadi should complete it, then say salam. The reason is that tashahhud is wajib and there is no further act to follow; thus the wajib takes precedence over immediate following. The text mentions two principles: following the imam is wajib, but if a wajib is about to be missed, it is delayed, while a sunnah is abandoned to follow.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation 'Attahiyyat lillahi...' during sitting in prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): A person praying behind an imam in congregational prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is proven by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.

Key Takeaway
