Following the Imam When Tasbih Is Missed
Ruling on muqtadi following imam even if tasbih not completed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the imam raises his head before the muqtadi completes three tasbihs, and explain the hierarchy of sunnah vs wajib.

Core Idea
Following the imam (wajib) overrides completing the sunnah tasbih.

In congregational prayer, the muqtadi is obligated to follow the imam's actions. A common situation arises when the imam moves quickly and the muqtadi hasn't finished the recommended tasbih. This lesson clarifies the priority between sunnah and wajib in such a scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and conflict
The act is raising from ruku or sujud. The conflict is between finishing three tasbihs (sunnah) and following the imam immediately (wajib).
2
State the ruling
The muqtadi must follow the imam immediately, even if tasbih is incomplete.
Wajib takes precedence over sunnah.
3
Examine the first dalil
The hadith from Anas ibn Malik commands: follow the imam in takbir, ruku, and raising. This establishes the general obligation of mutaaba'ah.
Bukhari and Muslim
4
Examine the second dalil
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaina shows the Prophet stood after two rak'ahs without tashahhud, and the companions followed him—even though tashahhud is wajib. This proves following takes precedence even over a wajib, so certainly over a sunnah.
Abu Dawood
5
Apply the Hanafi principle
When sunnah and wajib conflict, wajib prevails. The muqtadi's duty to follow the imam is wajib; tasbih is sunnah.
Cross-madhhab: some schools consider tasbih wajib or rukn, leading to ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۱۲) ولو رفع الامام رأسه قبل تسبيح المقتدى ثلاثا في الركوع او السجود يتابعه
ترجمه (۵۱۲ ) اگر امام نے اپنا سر رکوع میں یا سجدے میں مقتدی کے تین مرتبہ تسبیح سے پہلے اٹھالیا تو مقتدی اس کی اتباع کرے تشریح : رکوع میں یا سجدے میں تین مرتبہ تسبیح پڑھنا سنت ہے، اور امام کی اتباع کرنا واجب ہے اس لئے اگر امام نے سراٹھا لیا اور تین تسبیح چھوٹ گئی تب بھی امام کی متابعت کرے۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کی متابعت کرو۔ عن انس بن مالك ..... و قال انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فاذا كبر فكبروا و اذا ركع فاركعوا و اذا رفع فارفعوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة القاعد ، ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۱۱۱۴ار مسلم شریف ، باب ائتمام المأموم بالامام ، ص ۱۷۴ نمبر ۹۲۱/۴۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ تکبیر کہو ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلا تشہد چھوڑ کر کھڑے ہوئے تو مقتدی بھی آپ کے ساتھ کھڑے ہو گئے ۔ عن عبد الله بن بحينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله الا الله و ركعتين ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلاته و انتظر التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتین ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب من قام من نشتین ولم یتشھد ، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۱۰۳۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور اٹھے تو اس کے ساتھ مقتدی بھی کھڑے ہوئے۔
(512) And if the imam raises his head before the muqtadi says three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, he follows him. Translation: (512) If the imam raises his head before the muqtadi completes three tasbihs in ruku or sujud, the muqtadi follows him. Explanation: Reciting three tasbihs in ruku or sujud is sunnah, and following the imam is wajib, so if the imam raises his head and three tasbihs are missed, the muqtadi still follows him. Proof: (1) The hadith: follow the imam; if he recites takbir, recite takbir; if he bows, bow; if he raises, raise (Bukhari, Muslim). (2) The hadith of Abdullah bin Buhaina: the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs then stood without sitting, and the people stood with him (Abu Dawood).
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This ruling addresses a conflict between sunnah and wajib. Reciting three tasbihs in ruku and sujud is sunnah (recommended), while following the imam is wajib (obligatory). If the imam raises his head before the muqtadi completes three tasbihs, the muqtadi must follow the imam immediately (wajib) and leave the sunnah. The proofs are the general command to follow the imam, and the specific incident where the Prophet stood up after two rak'ahs and the companions followed him, even though the first tashahhud (wajib) was missed.

Key Terms
التسبيح (al-tasbīḥ): Saying 'Subhana rabbiya al-azim' in ruku and 'Subhana rabbiya al-a'la' in sujud.
المتابعة (al-mutaaba'ah): The obligation of the muqtadi to follow the imam in all actions of the prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The person praying behind an imam (follower).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Raise immediately with imam
C) Wait for imam to say salam
D) Perform sajda sahw

Key Takeaway
When sunnah and wajib conflict in prayer, wajib (following the imam) overrides sunnah (completing tasbih).

Not Following the Imam in Extra Actions
Ruling on muqtadi not following imam in extra invalidating actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when the muqtadi must not follow the imam in salah and identify the condition that triggers this exception.

Core Idea
The muqtadi must not follow the imam in actions that clearly add to the prayer, such as an extra sajdah or standing after the final tashahhud.

In congregational prayer, following the imam is generally wajib. However, if the imam commits an action that clearly invalidates or adds to the prayer, the muqtadi must not follow. This lesson examines the ruling from the matn regarding two specific extra actions: an extra sajdah and standing after the final qa‘dah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's extra actions
Read the phrase 'zad al-imam sajdatan aw qama ba‘d al-qu‘ud al-akhir'. Note that these are two distinct extra actions: an extra prostration and standing up after the final sitting.
2
Recognise the muqtadi's duty
The text says 'yutabi‘uh? bal la yutabi‘uh' – the muqtadi should NOT follow. Understand that following is normally required, but here it is prohibited.
The question form 'yutabi‘uh?' implies a common doubt.
3
Apply the condition for not following
The condition is that the imam's action clearly adds to the prayer (i.e., an invalidating addition). In Hanafi fiqh, an extra sajdah or extra rak‘ah invalidates the prayer if done intentionally, so the muqtadi must not participate.
4
Derive the practical consequence
The muqtadi should remain seated and wait for the imam to correct via sajdat al-sahw. The prayer continues without that extra action.
This prevents the muqtadi from nullifying his own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۱۳) ولو زاد الامام سجدة او قام بعد القعود الاخير يتابعه؟ بل لا يتابعه
(513) And if the imam adds an extra sajdah or stands after the final qa'dah, he does not follow him.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This ruling states that the muqtadi should not follow the imam in extra actions that are clearly mistakes, such as an extra sajdah or standing up after the final sitting (which would add an extra rak'ah). The muqtadi should remain seated and wait for the imam to correct the mistake, possibly by performing sajda sahw. Following the imam is normally wajib, but if the imam's action invalidates the prayer or is clearly an error, the muqtadi should not follow.

Key Terms
القعود الاخير (al-qu'ūd al-akhir): The final sitting after the last sujud before salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must not follow the imam in actions that clearly add to the prayer, such as an extra sajdah or standing after the final qa'dah, to avoid invalidating his own salah.

Completing Tashahhud if Imam Says Salam Early
Ruling on muqtadi completing tashahhud after imam's early salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a muqtadi must complete his tashahhud when the imam says salam early, and explain the principle that a wajib takes precedence over following the imam.

Core Idea
A wajib (tashahhud) must be completed even if it delays following the imam's salam.

This lesson addresses a common situation in congregational prayer: the imam finishes the prayer and says salam, but the follower (muqtadi) has not yet completed the obligatory tashahhud. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that prioritizes completing the wajib act over immediate conformity with the imam. Understanding this ruling reinforces the importance of wajib acts in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? It is the muqtadi's tashahhud when the imam says salam early. The ruling: the muqtadi must complete the tashahhud before saying salam.
2
Recognize the underlying principle
Why must the muqtadi complete it? Because tashahhud is wajib in the Hanafi school. A wajib act cannot be abandoned merely to follow the imam when no other obligatory action remains after salam.
The principle: obedience to the imam is limited by the requirement to fulfill one's own wajib.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers tashahhud as sunnah, not wajib. For them, following the imam's salam immediately would be preferred because the sunnah can be forgone.
This ikhtilaf arises from different classifications of the tashahhud.
4
Identify the practical consequence
In Hanafi practice, the muqtadi delays his salam, completes the tashahhud, then says salam. If he follows immediately, he omits a wajib and must perform sajdah sahw.
The muqtadi's prayer remains valid if he forgets to complete it, but sajdah sahw is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو سلم الامام قبل فراغ المقتدي من التشهد يتمه
If the imam says salam before the follower completes the tashahhud, he (the follower) completes it.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This is a ruling about the follower (muqtadi) when the imam finishes prayer early. The tashahhud is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school. If the imam says salam before the muqtadi completes his tashahhud, the muqtadi must complete the tashahhud and then say salam. This is because the wajib act (tashahhud) takes precedence over following the imam when there is no subsequent action except salam. The principle is that wajib cannot be left for mere following.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadī): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (at-tahiyyat) in the sitting posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Following Imam When He Rises Early from Ruku or Sujud
Ruling on following the imam when he rises early from ruku/sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam rises before the muqtadi completes three tasbihat and apply the principle that wajib overrides sunnah.

Core Idea
Follow the imam immediately — wajib overrides sunnah, even if tasbihat incomplete.

This passage addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: what should a follower do when the imam moves on before the follower has finished reciting sunnah tasbihat? The text provides a clear ruling based on the hadith that the imam is to be followed. Understanding this hierarchy of obligations ensures the validity and synchronization of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act in question? The muqtadi following the imam in action. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
Following the imam is a wajib, not a fard, due to the zanni thubut of the dalil.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise.'
This hadith is reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'فاركعوا' and 'فارفعوا' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
Al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah that diverts it.
4
Apply the hierarchy
Following the imam is wajib; tasbihat are sunnah. The wajib takes precedence, so the muqtadi must abandon the sunnah and follow immediately.
This is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh: al-wajib muqaddam 'ala al-sunnah.

Not Following the Imam in Extra Sajdah or Standing After Final Qa'dah
Ruling on muqtadi not following imam's extra actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the imam makes an extra sajdah or stands after the final qa'dah and apply it in a congregational prayer scenario.

Core Idea
Muqtadi does not follow imam in forgetful extra acts; he says salam alone.

In congregational prayer, muqtadis must follow the imam in all actions of the prayer. However, this rule has an important exception: if the imam performs an extra sajdah or stands up after the final qa'dah forgetfully, the muqtadi should not follow. Instead, he remains seated and says salam. This lesson explains the ruling, its proof, and how to apply it correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's forgetful action
The two scenarios are: (1) Imam performs an extra sajdah (e.g., three prostrations instead of two in one rak'ah). (2) Imam stands up after the final qa'dah (i.e., after tashahhud) intending an additional rak'ah by mistake.
The forgetfulness must occur after the final sitting.
2
State the ruling for the muqtadi
The muqtadi does not follow the imam in these actions. He must not stand up or perform the extra sajdah. Instead, he remains seated and says salam (taslim) on his own.
This is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the reasoning
Following the imam is required only in actions that are part of the prayer. Extra sajdah and standing after the final qa'dah are not part of the prayer; they are errors. If the muqtadi follows, his prayer would be invalid because he is adding an extra integral (rukn) deliberately.
The imam's forgetfulness does not obligate the muqtadi to repeat the error.
4
Apply the proof from hadith
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhayn (Abu Dawud) shows that when the Prophet (ﷺ) stood after two rak'ahs forgetfully, the companions did not follow him but waited until he returned. This establishes that not following in such cases is the correct practice.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear and decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو زاد الامام سجدة او قام بعد القعود الاخير ساهيا لا يتبعه المؤتم وان قيدها سلم وحده
And if the imam adds a sajdah or stands after the final qa'dah forgetfully, the follower does not follow him; and if he completes it, he (the follower) says salam alone.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage gives two scenarios: (1) The imam makes an extra sajdah (e.g., three sajdahs instead of two) or stands up after the final tashahhud forgetfully. In both cases, the muqtadi does not follow because these actions are not part of the prayer. The muqtadi remains seated and says salam. (2) If the imam stands for an extra rak'ah and completes it with its sajdah, then the imam will eventually say salam after completing that rak'ah, but the muqtadi should not wait; he says salam alone. The commentary explains that the muqtadi should not follow because following the imam in an error that is not part of the prayer is not required.

Key Terms

القعود الاخير (al-qu'ūd al-akhīr): The final sitting after the last rak'ah before salam.

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must not follow the imam in any forgetful act that is not part of the prayer, such as an extra sajdah or standing after the final qa'dah; he says salam alone to preserve his prayer's validity.

Waiting for the Imam Who Forgets the Final Qa'dah
Ruling on muqtadi waiting for imam who forgetfully stands before final qa'dah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam forgetfully stands before the final qa'dah and identify the consequence if the muqtadi says salam prematurely.

Core Idea
The muqtadi must wait for the imam; early salam invalidates the prayer.

In congregational prayer, the imam leads and the muqtadi follows. If the imam forgetfully stands up from the final sitting before salam, a critical question arises: should the muqtadi wait or act? This lesson clarifies the obligation and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The imam forgetfully stands before the final qa'dah. The muqtadi must wait for him. This is wajib.
Final qa'dah is fard; omitting it requires the imam to return.
2
State the consequence of early departure
If the muqtadi says salam before the imam completes the extra sajdah (i.e., before the imam resolves the extra rak'ah), the muqtadi's fard prayer becomes invalid.
The muqtadi separated while the imam's prayer was still incomplete due to a missed fard.
3
Understand the proof
The hadith 'The Prophet (ﷺ) urged them to pray and forbade them from leaving before he left' shows that the muqtadi must remain until the imam finishes.
Dalil: Abu Dawud, hadith 624.

This is because the muqtadi has separated from the imam while the imam's prayer is still incomplete due to the missed fard.

Disliking Muqtadi's Salam Before Imam's After Tashahhud
Ruling with proof on dislike of early salam by muqtadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a muqtadi saying salam before the imam after tashahhud and apply the Hanafi principle that following the imam is wajib until the very end.

Core Idea
Saying salam before the imam is makruh but valid, because the prayer is complete after tashahhud.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) is bound to follow the imam until the end. This lesson addresses a specific question: what if the follower says his own salam before the imam does, after both have completed the tashahhud? The Hanafi school rules that this is makruh (disliked) but the prayer remains valid. We will examine the proof from hadith and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muqtadi saying salam after tashahhud but before the imam says salam. The ruling (hukm) is makruh (disliked), but the prayer is still valid.
Makruh here is likely makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it violates the wajib of following the imam.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith recorded by Darqutni: 'When the imam sits for the final rak'ah, then a man behind him breaks his wudu before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete.' This indicates that the prayer is valid once the final sitting is made, even before the salam.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalalah) for the Hanafis.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The hadith shows that the final tashahhud sitting completes the prayer's essential structure. Therefore, saying salam early does not invalidate the prayer, but it is makruh because the muqtadi abandons the wajib of following the imam until his salam.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard/wajib and conditions of validity. Missing a wajib does not invalidate the act but may require compensation (here, no compensation needed).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و كره سلام المقتدى قبل سلام الامام بعد التشهد
And it is disliked for the follower to say salam before the imam's salam after the tashahhud.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This ruling states that it is makruh (disliked) for the muqtadi to say salam before the imam says salam, even after both have completed the tashahhud. The reason is that following the imam is wajib until the very end. However, if the muqtadi does say salam early, his prayer is still valid because the essential part (tashahhud) has been completed. The hadith cited (Darqutni) indicates that if a person sits for the final tashahhud and then breaks his wudu before the imam's salam, his prayer is complete, which analogically supports the validity of early salam.

Key Terms
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; an act that is blameworthy but not sinful enough to invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid but it is makruh.
C) The prayer is valid and not makruh.
D) The muqtadi must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a muqtadi's early salam after tashahhud is makruh but does not invalidate the prayer.

Ruling 514: Follower's Prayer Invalid if He Says Salam Before Imam Completes Extra Rakah
Ruling on follower when imam forgetfully adds a rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the follower's prayer when he says salam before the imam completes an extra rak'ah performed forgetfully, and explain why the prayer becomes invalid.

Core Idea
If the follower disassociates before the imam completes a forgetful extra rak'ah, his prayer is void.

In congregational prayer, the imam may forgetfully stand for an extra rak'ah instead of sitting for the final tashahhud. The Hanafi school rules that the follower must not follow this extra action but must wait for the imam to return. This lesson examines the consequence if the follower prematurely says salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam forgetfully stands before the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). This is an extra rak'ah not part of the original prayer.
The final sitting is fard, so the imam must return to it.
2
State the follower's obligation
The follower must wait for the imam to return to sitting; he does not follow the extra standing or sajdah.
The follower remains seated and waits.
3
Identify the invalidating action
If the follower says salam before the imam performs the sajdah of the extra rak'ah, his fard prayer becomes invalid (batil).
Saying salam at this point severs his connection before the fard of the final sitting is completed.
4
Understand the rationale
The final sitting is fard. By saying salam early, the follower fails to complete this fard with the congregation. The imam's extra actions are not part of the prayer, so the follower cannot follow them.
This is based on the hadith prohibiting departing before the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدى ساهيا لا يتبعه المؤتم وان قيدها سلّم وحده (۵۱۴) وان قام الامام قبل القعود الاخير ساهيا انتظره الماموم فان سلّم المقتدى قبل ان يقيد امامه الزائدة بسجدة فسد فرضه (۵۱۵) و کره سلام کرے۔ اور اگر امام زائد رکعت کا سجدہ کر لیوے تو مقتدی سلام پھیر دے۔
تشریح : امام دو سجدے کے بجائے تین سجدہ کرلے تو چونکہ یہ نماز کا حصہ نہیں ہے اس لئے مقتدی اس کی اتباع نہ کرے۔ اور قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو یہ بھی نماز کا حصہ نہیں ہے اور آگے سلام کے علاوہ اور کوئی کام بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے مقتدی اس کی اتباع نہ کرے۔ اور اگر انگلی رکعت پوری کر کے اس کا سجدہ بھی کر لیا تو اب اس کے واپس ہونے کا کوئی چانس نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ دوسری رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیرے گا، اس لئے مقتدی اب اکیلے سلام پھیر دے۔
ترجمه : (۵۱۴) اور اگر امام قعدہ اخیرہ سے پہلے بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو مقتدی اس کے لوٹنے کا انتظار کرے۔ اور امام کے زائد رکعت کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر مقتدی سلام پھیر دے گا تو اس کی فرض نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی تشریح : قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اس کو بھول کر کھڑے ہو گئے تو امام کے ساتھ ایک فرض رہ گیا اس لئے انکے لوٹنے کا انتظار کرے تا کہ ساتھ سلام پھیرے۔ لیکن اگر ابھی امام نے اگلی رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا اور مقتدی نے سلام پھیر دیا تو مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ عن انس ان النبى الله الله محضهم على الصلاة و نهاهم ان ينصرفوا قبل انصرافه من الصلاة (ابوداود شریف، باب فیمن نصرف قبل الامام، ص ۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۲۴ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام سے پہلے نماز سے نہ نکلے۔
ترجمه : (۵۱۵) اور امام کے تشہد کے بعد سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے مقتدی کا سلام پھیر نا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح امام نے قعدہ آخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھ لیا لیکن ابھی سلام نہیں پھیرا تو مقتدی ابھی سلام نہ پھیرے اس کا سلام پھیر نا مکروہ ہے وجه : (۱) حدیث کے اعتبار سے مقتدی کو امام کی اتباع کرنی چاہئے ، اور اس نے اتباع نہیں کی اس لئے مکروہ ہے، تاہم امام کے ساتھ تشہد پڑھ چکا ہے اس لئے نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عتبان بن مالك قال صلينا مع النبي الله فسلمنا حسين مسلم - ( بخاری شریف، باب يسلم حين يسلم الامام ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۳۸) (۳) لیکن اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ، اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال اذا جلس الامام في آخر ركعة ثم احدث رجل من خلفه قبل ان يسلم الامام فقد تمت صلوته ( دارقطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسليم ، ج اول ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی بھی مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ، اسی طرح سلام پھیر دے تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔
Chapter on what the follower does when the imam forgets: The follower does not follow him. (514) If the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower waits for him. If the follower says salam before the imam performs the extra sajdah, his fard prayer becomes invalid. (515) It is makruh for the follower to say salam after the imam's tashahhud before the imam says salam. Explanation: If the imam performs three sajdahs instead of two, the follower does not follow because this is not part of the prayer. If the imam forgetfully stands after the final sitting, that is also not part of the prayer, so the follower does not follow. If the imam completes an extra rak'ah and its sajdah, he cannot return, so the follower should say salam alone. Translation: (514) If the imam forgetfully stands before the final sitting, the follower waits for him to return. If the follower says salam before the imam performs the extra sajdah, his fard prayer is invalid. Explanation: The final sitting is fard; if the imam forgets and stands, a fard remains, so the follower waits so they can say salam together. But if the imam has not yet performed the sajdah of the next rak'ah and the follower says salam, the follower's prayer is invalid. Evidence: This hadith can be used: From Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded them to pray and forbade them from departing before his departure from prayer (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who departs before the imam, p. 101, no. 624). This hadith states that one should not leave prayer before the imam. Translation: (515) It is makruh for the follower to say salam after the imam's tashahhud before the imam says salam. Explanation: The imam recited tashahhud in the final sitting but has not yet said salam; the follower should not say salam yet; his saying salam is makruh. Evidence: (1) Based on hadith, the follower must follow the imam, and he did not follow, so it is makruh; however, since he recited tashahhud with the imam, his prayer is valid. (2) From 'Utban ibn Malik: We prayed with the Prophet and he said salam after us? (Bukhari, chapter on saying salam when the imam says salam, p. 136, no. 838) (3) But if he says salam, his prayer is complete; for this there is a hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: When the imam sits in the last rak'ah, then a person behind him breaks wudu before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete (Darqutni, chapter on one who breaks wudu before salam, vol. 1, p. 368, no. 1407). This hadith indicates that if the follower sits for the duration of tashahhud and then breaks wudu, his prayer is complete; similarly, if he says salam, his prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Hanafi school on the actions of a muqtadi (follower) when the imam forgetfully adds or omits elements in prayer. The passage covers two numbered rulings (514 and 515). In (514), if the imam forgetfully stands before the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), the muqtadi must wait for the imam to return to sitting, because the final sitting is fard and the followers need to complete it with the imam. However, if the muqtadi says salam before the imam performs the sajdah of an extra rak'ah, his fard prayer becomes invalid because he has disassociated from the imam before the imam's prayer is complete. If the imam completes an extra rak'ah with sajdah, the muqtadi should say salam alone, as the imam will complete his prayer with an extra rak'ah. In (515), it is makruh tanzihi for the muqtadi to say salam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam says salam, because he fails to follow the imam in the final action. However, if he does so, his prayer is valid because he has completed the obligatory parts. The proofs are hadith from Abu Dawud, Bukhari, and Darqutni. The Hanafi position is that although the muqtadi must follow the imam in all obligatory and recommended actions, he does not follow in forgetful extra actions that are not part of the prayer structure.

Key Terms
مقتدى (muqtadī): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
ساهيا (sāhiyan): Forgetfully, unintentionally, without meaning to add or omit.
قعدة اخيرة (qa‘dah akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, where tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The follower's prayer is valid but makruh.
B) The follower's prayer is invalid (batil).
C) The follower's prayer is valid because the imam's action is forgetful.
D) The follower must repeat the rak'ah only.

Key Takeaway
The follower must wait for the imam to return to the final sitting; prematurely saying salam before the extra sajdah invalidates the prayer.

Ruling 515: Follower Saying Salam After Tashahhud Before Imam is Makruh Tanzih
Ruling on follower saying salam before imam after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the follower saying salam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam says salam, and explain why it is makruh tanzih yet the prayer remains valid.

Core Idea
Saying salam after tashahhud but before the imam is disliked but valid.

After the imam completes tashahhud in the final sitting, he will say salam. The Hanafi school teaches that the follower should not say salam until the imam does. This lesson explains why doing so is makruh tanzih and why the prayer is still valid, supported by hadith from Bukhari and Darqutni.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam has completed the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and recited tashahhud, but has not yet said salam.
The fard (final sitting) is complete; only the sunnah salam remains.
2
State the follower's action and ruling
If the follower says salam at this point, it is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but the prayer is still valid.
3
Understand the rationale for karahah
The follower has not followed the imam in the salam, which is a recommended act of congregation. The hadith (Bukhari) indicate that the follower should say salam when the imam says salam.
Violating the preferred sequence is disliked.
4
Understand why the prayer is still valid
The hadith from Darqutni states that if the follower sits for the last rak'ah and then breaks wudu before the imam's salam, his prayer is complete. This shows that the prayer is not dependent on the imam's salam for validity once the fard (sitting) is complete.
Thus the early salam does not invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يفعله المقتدى ساهيا لا يتبعه المؤتم وان قيدها سلّم وحده (۵۱۴) وان قام الامام قبل القعود الاخير ساهيا انتظره الماموم فان سلّم المقتدى قبل ان يقيد امامه الزائدة بسجدة فسد فرضه (۵۱۵) و کره سلام کرے۔ اور اگر امام زائد رکعت کا سجدہ کر لیوے تو مقتدی سلام پھیر دے۔
تشریح : امام دو سجدے کے بجائے تین سجدہ کرلے تو چونکہ یہ نماز کا حصہ نہیں ہے اس لئے مقتدی اس کی اتباع نہ کرے۔ اور قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو یہ بھی نماز کا حصہ نہیں ہے اور آگے سلام کے علاوہ اور کوئی کام بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے مقتدی اس کی اتباع نہ کرے۔ اور اگر انگلی رکعت پوری کر کے اس کا سجدہ بھی کر لیا تو اب اس کے واپس ہونے کا کوئی چانس نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ دوسری رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیرے گا، اس لئے مقتدی اب اکیلے سلام پھیر دے۔
ترجمه : (۵۱۴) اور اگر امام قعدہ اخیرہ سے پہلے بھول کر کھڑا ہو جائے تو مقتدی اس کے لوٹنے کا انتظار کرے۔ اور امام کے زائد رکعت کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر مقتدی سلام پھیر دے گا تو اس کی فرض نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی تشریح : قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اس کو بھول کر کھڑے ہو گئے تو امام کے ساتھ ایک فرض رہ گیا اس لئے انکے لوٹنے کا انتظار کرے تا کہ ساتھ سلام پھیرے۔ لیکن اگر ابھی امام نے اگلی رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا اور مقتدی نے سلام پھیر دیا تو مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ عن انس ان النبى الله الله محضهم على الصلاة و نهاهم ان ينصرفوا قبل انصرافه من الصلاة (ابوداود شریف، باب فیمن نصرف قبل الامام، ص ۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۲۴ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام سے پہلے نماز سے نہ نکلے۔
ترجمه : (۵۱۵) اور امام کے تشہد کے بعد سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے مقتدی کا سلام پھیر نا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح امام نے قعدہ آخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھ لیا لیکن ابھی سلام نہیں پھیرا تو مقتدی ابھی سلام نہ پھیرے اس کا سلام پھیر نا مکروہ ہے وجه : (۱) حدیث کے اعتبار سے مقتدی کو امام کی اتباع کرنی چاہئے ، اور اس نے اتباع نہیں کی اس لئے مکروہ ہے، تاہم امام کے ساتھ تشہد پڑھ چکا ہے اس لئے نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عتبان بن مالك قال صلينا مع النبي الله فسلمنا حسين مسلم - ( بخاری شریف، باب يسلم حين يسلم الامام ، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۳۸) (۳) لیکن اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ، اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال اذا جلس الامام في آخر ركعة ثم احدث رجل من خلفه قبل ان يسلم الامام فقد تمت صلوته ( دارقطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسليم ، ج اول ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی بھی مقدار تشہد بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دے تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ، اسی طرح سلام پھیر دے تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔
Chapter on what the follower does when the imam forgets: The follower does not follow him. (514) If the imam stands before the final sitting forgetfully, the follower waits for him. If the follower says salam before the imam performs the extra sajdah, his fard prayer becomes invalid. (515) It is makruh for the follower to say salam after the imam's tashahhud before the imam says salam. Explanation: If the imam performs three sajdahs instead of two, the follower does not follow because this is not part of the prayer. If the imam forgetfully stands after the final sitting, that is also not part of the prayer, so the follower does not follow. If the imam completes an extra rak'ah and its sajdah, he cannot return, so the follower should say salam alone. Translation: (514) If the imam forgetfully stands before the final sitting, the follower waits for him to return. If the follower says salam before the imam performs the extra sajdah, his fard prayer is invalid. Explanation: The final sitting is fard; if the imam forgets and stands, a fard remains, so the follower waits so they can say salam together. But if the imam has not yet performed the sajdah of the next rak'ah and the follower says salam, the follower's prayer is invalid. Evidence: This hadith can be used: From Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded them to pray and forbade them from departing before his departure from prayer (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who departs before the imam, p. 101, no. 624). This hadith states that one should not leave prayer before the imam. Translation: (515) It is makruh for the follower to say salam after the imam's tashahhud before the imam says salam. Explanation: The imam recited tashahhud in the final sitting but has not yet said salam; the follower should not say salam yet; his saying salam is makruh. Evidence: (1) Based on hadith, the follower must follow the imam, and he did not follow, so it is makruh; however, since he recited tashahhud with the imam, his prayer is valid. (2) From 'Utban ibn Malik: We prayed with the Prophet and he said salam after us? (Bukhari, chapter on saying salam when the imam says salam, p. 136, no. 838) (3) But if he says salam, his prayer is complete; for this there is a hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: When the imam sits in the last rak'ah, then a person behind him breaks wudu before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete (Darqutni, chapter on one who breaks wudu before salam, vol. 1, p. 368, no. 1407). This hadith indicates that if the follower sits for the duration of tashahhud and then breaks wudu, his prayer is complete; similarly, if he says salam, his prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Hanafi school on the actions of a muqtadi (follower) when the imam forgetfully adds or omits elements in prayer. The passage covers two numbered rulings (514 and 515). In (514), if the imam forgetfully stands before the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), the muqtadi must wait for the imam to return to sitting, because the final sitting is fard and the followers need to complete it with the imam. However, if the muqtadi says salam before the imam performs the sajdah of an extra rak'ah, his fard prayer becomes invalid because he has disassociated from the imam before the imam's prayer is complete. If the imam completes an extra rak'ah with sajdah, the muqtadi should say salam alone, as the imam will complete his prayer with an extra rak'ah. In (515), it is makruh tanzihi for the muqtadi to say salam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam says salam, because he fails to follow the imam in the final action. However, if he does so, his prayer is valid because he has completed the obligatory parts. The proofs are hadith from Abu Dawud, Bukhari, and Darqutni. The Hanafi position is that although the muqtadi must follow the imam in all obligatory and recommended actions, he does not follow in forgetful extra actions that are not part of the prayer structure.

Key Terms
مقتدى (muqtadī): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
ساهيا (sāhiyan): Forgetfully, unintentionally, without meaning to add or omit.
قعدة اخيرة (qa‘dah akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, where tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In (515), what is the ruling on the follower saying salam after the imam's tashahhud but before the imam says salam?
A) Haram and the prayer is invalid.
B) Makruh tanzih and the prayer is valid.
C) Mustahabb and the prayer is valid.
D) The follower must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Saying salam after tashahhud but before the imam is disliked, but the prayer remains valid because the obligatory final sitting is complete.

Recommended Actions After Fard Prayer: Sunnah, Imam's Turning, and Dhikr
Rulings on sunnah prayer and dhikr after fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the recommended actions after fard prayer, including praying sunnah immediately, the imam's turning, and the recitation of dhikr, and differentiate between the default view and al-Halwani's permissive view regarding awrad.

Core Idea
After fard prayer, praying sunnah immediately is sunnah; awrad between are permissible per al-Halwani.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text details the recommended sequence after the obligatory prayer. It covers the sunnah of standing immediately for the sunnah prayer, an alternative view allowing awrad in between, the imam's mustahabb turning after salam, and the communal dhikr including Ayat al-Kursi and tasbih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (standing for sunnah, imam turning, dhikr) and the hukm level (sunnah, mustahabb, mubah).
2
Locate the dalil
For each act, find the hadith evidence cited: the hadith of Mughirah for sunnah prayer, the hadith of Abu Hurairah for awrad, the hadith of al-Bara' for turning, and the hadith of 'Abdullah for turning direction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each hadith proves the ruling. For example, the prohibition 'لا يصلي في الموضع' implies the imam must move, indicating the sunnah is separate from fard.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the difference between the default view (pray sunnah immediately) and al-Halwani's view (permissible to recite awrad between). Understand that both are valid within the school.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference is whether one may engage in dhikr between fard and sunnah or should pray the sunnah first. The mufta bihi is to pray sunnah first, but awrad are not prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الاذكار الواردة بعد الفرض (۵۱۶) القيام الى السنة متصلا بالفرض مسنون وعن الشمس الائمة الحلواني لا بأس بقراءة الاوراد بين الفريضة والسنة. (۵۱) ويستحب للامام بعد سلامه ان يتحوّل الى يساره لتطوّع بعد الفرض (۵۱۸) وان يستقبل بـعـده الناس ويستغفرون الله ويقرء ون آية الكرسي والمعوذات
فصل : فرض نماز کے بعد اذکار کے بیان میں
ترجمه : (۵۱۶) فرض نماز کے بعد متصلا نماز کے لئے کھڑ ا ہو ناسنت ہے۔ اور شمس الائمہ حلوائی سے مروی ہے کہ فرض وسنت کے درمیان اوراد پڑھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں۔ تشریح : فرض نماز کے بعد متصلا سنت نماز پڑھے، البتہ تھوڑا ہٹ کر پڑھے، اور شمس الائمہ حلوائی کی رائے ہے کہ فرض اور سنت کے درمیان اوراد و وظائف پڑھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (1) سنت پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال قال لا يصلي الامام في الموضع الذي صلى فيه حتى يتحول ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب الامام يتطوع في مكانه ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۶۱۶ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز کے بعد سنت پڑھے۔ (۲) اور اد کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال جاء الفقراء الى النبي الله ..... تسبحون و تحمدون و تكبرون خلف كل صلاة ثلاثا وثلاثين ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الذکر بعد السلام، ص ۱۳۷، نمبر ۸۴۳)
ترجمه : (۵۱۷) اور امام کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ سلام کے بعد دائیں جانب پھر جائے تا کہ فرض کے بعد نفل پڑھ سکے۔ وجه : (۱) عن البراء بن عازب قال كنا اذا صلينا خلف رسول الله الا الله احببنا ان نكون عن يمينه فيقبل علينا بوجهه ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الامام تحرف بعد التسلیم، ص ۱۰۰ نمبر ۲۶۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں جانب مڑے (۲)عــن عبـد الـلـه قال لا يجعل احدكم نصيباللشيطان من صلاته ان لا ينصرف الا عن يمينه و قد رأيت رسول الله الله الله اكثر ما ينصرف عن شماله - ( ابوداود شریف ، باب کیف الانصراف من الصلاة، ص ۱۵۸، نمبر ۱۰۴۲ بخاری شریف ، باب الانفتال والانصراف عن اليمين والشمال ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۸۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں جانب مڑے لیکن بائیں جانب مڑنا بھی جائز ہے۔
Chapter on the reported remembrances after the fard prayer. (516) Standing for the sunnah prayer immediately after the fard is sunnah. And from Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani: There is no harm in reciting awrad between fard and sunnah. (517) It is mustahabb for the imam after his salam to turn to his left to perform nafl after fard. (518) And then to face the people, and they seek forgiveness from Allah, and recite Ayat al-Kursi and the Mu'awwidhat. Chapter on dhikr after fard prayer. Translation: (516) Standing immediately after fard for sunnah is sunnah. And from Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani: No harm in reciting awrad between fard and sunnah. Explanation: One should pray sunnah immediately after fard, but slightly to the side. Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani's opinion is that there is no harm in reciting awrad and litanies between fard and sunnah. Evidence: (1) For praying sunnah, there is this hadith from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: He said, 'The imam should not pray in the same place he prayed until he moves.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on imam performing nafl in his place, p. 100, no. 616) This hadith indicates to pray sunnah after prayer. (2) For awrad, there is this hadith from Abu Hurairah: The poor came to the Prophet... 'Glorify Allah, praise Him, and declare His greatness after every prayer thirty-three times.' (Bukhari, chapter on dhikr after salam, p. 137, no. 843) Translation: (517) It is mustahabb for the imam after salam to turn to the right side so that he can perform nafl after fard. Evidence: (1) From al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: When we prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, we loved to be on his right side so that he would turn his face towards us. (Abu Dawud, chapter on imam turning after salam, p. 100, no. 2615) This hadith indicates turning to the right. (2) From 'Abdullah: Do not make for Satan a share of your prayer by only turning to the right, and I have seen the Messenger of Allah mostly turning to his left. (Abu Dawud, chapter on how to turn from prayer, p. 158, no. 1042; Bukhari, chapter on turning to right and left, p. 138, no. 852) This hadith indicates turning to the right, but turning to the left is also permissible.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Hanafi school on the recommended actions after completing the fard prayer. It covers three numbered rulings (516, 517, and part of 518). (516) states that it is sunnah to stand up for the sunnah prayer immediately after the fard prayer, without engaging in lengthy dhikr in between. However, Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani (a prominent Hanafi scholar) permits reciting awrad (litanies) between the fard and sunnah, indicating flexibility. The proof is the hadith of Mughirah that the imam should move to a different spot for nafl, implying the sunnah is prayed after the fard. (517) says it is mustahabb for the imam after salam to turn to his left (though the text may have an error; the hadith and Urdu commentary mention the right side as preferred, but left is also permissible). The wisdom is to face the congregation. (518) mentions that after the sunnah, the imam and congregation should face each other, recite istighfar three times, Ayat al-Kursi, and the Mu'awwidhat, then tasbih, tahmid, takbir 33 times each, and conclude with tahlil. The Hanafi school considers these acts recommended based on authentic hadith.

Key Terms
اوراد (awrād): Litanies or specific dhikr recited regularly, especially after prayers.
مسنون (masnūn): Sunnah; an action established by the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a regular practice.
التحول (al-taḥawwul): Turning or moving from the spot, specifically the imam turning after salam.
المعوذات (al-muʿawwidhāt): The two chapters of refuge: Surah al-Falaq and Surah an-Nas, often recited for protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the text, what should an imam do after the salam of the fard prayer before praying nafl?
A) Stay in place
B) Turn to the right
C) Turn to the left
D) Recite Ayat al-Kursi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends praying the sunnah immediately after fard, with optional awrad permissible between, and prescribes specific post-prayer dhikr.
